The Hanafi Position on Exile for the Bikr: Discretionary, Not Mandatory
Ruling that the bikr is flogged, and exile is only if the imam deems it beneficial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining flogging and exile for the bikr, explain the Hanafi proof from the actions of the Companions, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
No forced exile for the bikr—the imam decides based on public interest.

The punishment for an unmarried person (bikr) who commits zina is a core point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While both agree on 100 lashes, the Hanafi school holds that exile is not a fixed part of the hadd but a discretionary ta'zir measure that the imam may impose only if he sees a public benefit (maslahah). This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proofs from the Companions' practice, and the response to the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi rule
Read the Arabic text: 'ولا يجمع في البكر بين الجلد والنفى الا ان يرى الامام ذلك مصلحة' – flogging and exile are not combined unless the imam sees a maslahah. The default is flogging alone.
The text uses 'لا يجمع' (not combined) indicating prohibition of mandatory combination.
2
Locate the Hanafi proofs
The commentary cites the athar of Umar (he stopped exile after a case of apostasy) and the athar of Ali ('exile itself is a fitnah'). These show that the early caliphs did not treat exile as a fixed hadd.
The athar are from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, a reliable source of early practice.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument
The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid: 'جلد مائة وتغريب عام'. Identify the opposing dalil and note its apparent strength.
The hadith is sahih (Bukhari and Muslim), making it a strong apparent proof.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (a) the hadith is abrogated or qualified by the later practice of the Companions, and (b) the command is interpreted as permissibility (ibahah) rather than obligation (wujub) due to the overriding practice of Umar and Ali.
This is an example of istihsan overriding a zanni dalil.

2469 (26) And flogging and stoning shall not be combined for the muhsan.
[2470] (27) And flogging and exile shall not be combined for the bikr, unless the imam sees a maslahah in it, then he may exile him as he sees fit.
[2470] (27) And flogging and exile shall not be combined for the unmarried. Rather, unless the imam sees a maslahah in it, then he may exile as he sees fit.
The unmarried person who is to be flogged should not be exiled along with the flogging. However, if the imam deems it beneficial, he may exile for a few days according to his discretion.
Hadrat Umar exiled a person, and he went out and became a Christian. So he said: I will never exile any Muslim after this.
The athar is: 'Abu Bakr ibn Umayyah ibn Khalaf was exiled for drinking to Khaybar; he joined the enemy and became a Christian. Umar said: I will never exile a Muslim after this.' And from Ibrahim that Ali said: 'Exile itself is sufficient fitnah (trial) for them.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on exile, vol. 7, p. 314 no. 13320). From this athar it is learned that exile was practiced earlier, but later Umar forbade it. However, if the imam sees it appropriate, he may still exile.
But Imam Shafi'i says that along with flogging, he should also be exiled for one year.
The hadith is: 'From Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding in the case of one who committed zina and was not muhsan: one hundred lashes and exile for a year.' (Bukhari, chapter on the bikr: flogging and exile, p. 1010 no. 6831; Muslim, chapter on confession of zina, p. 66 no. 1697).
Footnote: (b) Abu Bakr ibn Umayyah ibn Khalaf was exiled to Khaybar for drinking; he joined the enemy and became a Christian. So Umar said: I will never exile any Muslim after this. And it is narrated from Ibrahim that Ali said: Exile is sufficient fitnah for them. (c) The Prophet used to command in the case of one who committed zina and was not muhsan: one hundred... Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage covers ruling (27) regarding the bikr (unmarried person) guilty of zina. The text states that flogging and exile are not automatically combined; the default punishment is flogging alone. Exile is only added if the imam (ruler) sees a maslahah (public benefit) and may decide the duration. The commentary provides historical evidence: Hadrat Umar initially practiced exile for zina, but after a case where an exiled person apostatized, he stopped the practice. The athar from Ali also indicates that exile itself can be a fitnah. However, if the imam thinks exile is beneficial, he may apply it. The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i position, which mandates both flogging and a fixed one-year exile, citing the hadith from Zayd ibn Khalid. The Hanafi response, implied, is that the hadith is either abrogated or the command is not binding but discretionary. The footnote elaborates on the athar. Thus, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that exile for the bikr is not a required hadd; it is left to the imam's discretion based on circumstances.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): An unmarried person (never married) who commits zina; also used for virgin.
نفي / تغريب (nafi / taghrib): Exile or banishment from one's town as a punishment, usually for one year.
مصلحة (maslahah): Public interest or benefit; here, the imam's discretion to exile based on what he deems beneficial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the default punishment for an unmarried person (bikr) who commits zina?
A) 100 lashes and one year of exile
B) Stoning to death
C) 100 lashes only
D) Exile only

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, exile for the bikr is a discretionary ta'zir punishment, not a fixed hadd; it is imposed only when the imam deems it a public benefit.

The Hanafi Ruling on Exile for Bikr
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute on exile

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the hadd for a bikr and explain why exile is discretionary, not obligatory.

Core Idea
Flogging is the fixed hadd for bikr; exile is a discretionary ta'zir left to the Imam.

This passage addresses the Islamic penal code for unmarried persons (bikr) who commit zina. While flogging is undisputedly the prescribed hadd, the role of exile has been a point of scholarly debate. The Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of Caliph Umar, holds that exile is not a mandatory part of the hadd but a supplementary measure that the Imam may apply when it serves the public interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zina committed by a bikr (unmarried free person). The ruling for the bikr is flogging (wajib) and potentially exile (discretionary). Determine what is obligatory and what is optional.
The source clearly states flogging is applied, and exile is only added if the Imam sees benefit.
2
Locate the dalil for the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position relies on the athar from Caliph Umar who discontinued exile after an exiled person apostatized, and the saying of Ali that 'exile itself is sufficient trial.' These are used to argue that exile is not obligatory.
The dalil is not a direct text from Quran or Sunnah but the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, which is a source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the opposing Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that exile for one year is obligatory based on the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani. The hadith explicitly commands 'one hundred lashes and exile for a year.' Understand how the same hadith is interpreted differently.
The key difference lies in the interpretation of the imperative form: Hanafis see it as permissive or recommended, not absolute.
4
Apply the Hanafi ruling to a scenario
In practice, a Hanafi judge will order flogging for a bikr who committed zina. He may optionally add exile (nafy) if he deems it beneficial for the community, such as preventing corruption or allowing reform.
The duration of exile is also discretionary; the Imam decides based on the circumstances.

Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the hadd penalty for a bikr (unmarried free person) who commits zina. The ruling states that the default punishment is flogging only, and exile is not combined automatically. However, the Imam may add exile at his discretion if he sees a public benefit (maslahah). The commentator supports this with an athar (report) that Caliph Umar initially exiled an offender but later discontinued the practice when the exiled person apostatized. This shows that exile is not an obligatory part of the hadd but a discretionary penalty. The passage then contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i's view, who holds that exile for one year is mandatory alongside flogging based on the hadith of Zayd ibn Khalid. The Hanafi response is that the command in the hadith is interpreted as recommended or subject to Imam's discretion, not obligatory, and the practice of Umar supports this. The footnote clarifies the narrations. The core lesson is that while flogging is the fixed hadd for bikr, exile is a supplementary measure left to the Imam's judgment.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): An unmarried free person who has not previously engaged in valid marital intercourse.
النفى (al-nafiy): Exile or banishment from one's locality as a penalty.
مصلحة (maslahah): Public benefit or interest that the Imam considers in applying a discretionary penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory, like flogging.
B) It is forbidden, because Umar stopped it.
C) It is discretionary, to be applied if the Imam sees a benefit.
D) It is recommended in all cases.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, flogging is the mandatory hadd for a bikr, while exile is a discretionary ta'zir penalty subject to the Imam's judgment of public interest.

Sick Person's Hadd: Stoning Immediate, Flogging Delayed
Ruling that stoning for a sick person is not delayed, but flogging is delayed until recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying hadd penalties to a sick person and distinguish when it is immediate (stoning) vs delayed (flogging) using the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
Stoning is immediate for the sick; flogging is delayed to avoid harm—capital punishment admits no delay, corporal does.

This lesson addresses a specific question in Hanafi hudud: what if the offender is sick? The ruling distinguishes between stoning (for muhsan) and flogging (for bikr). Stoning is to be carried out immediately regardless of health, while flogging is postponed until recovery. The proof comes from a hadith where the Prophet approved delaying the flogging of a postpartum slave woman. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi concern for avoiding excessive harm (darar) in non-capital penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the two possible hadd penalties for zina (stoning for muhsan, flogging for bikr) and the ruling for each when the offender is sick: immediate stoning, delayed flogging.
The passage explicitly says: 'if his hadd is stoning, he is stoned; if his hadd is flogging, he is not flogged until he recovers.'
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith of the postpartum slave woman (nafsa') whose flogging was delayed. Find the specific hadith quote in the source.
The hadith is from Muslim and Tirmidhi; the Prophet said 'You did well' to the one who delayed flogging due to postpartum bleeding.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's approval indicates that flogging can be delayed when there is a health risk. By qiyas, any illness that makes flogging dangerous leads to delay.
The analogy is based on the shared illa of potential harm or death from flogging while in a weak state.
4
Note the principle
The key distinction: stoning is capital (intended to kill), so delaying offers no benefit; flogging is non-capital and can be postponed to avoid worsening the condition or causing death.
The commentator explains: 'The purpose is to kill by stoning, so whether sick or not, it makes no difference.'
5
Apply to the sick person
By analogy, a sick person whose hadd is flogging is not flogged until recovery. A sick muhsan is stoned immediately.
The ruling also extends to the pregnant woman: hadd is delayed until delivery (ruling 30).

Source Text

[۲۴۷۱ (۲۸) واذا زنى المريض وحده الرجم رجم [ ۲۴۷۲] (۲۹) وان كان حده الجلد لم يجلد حتى يبرأ [۲۴۷۳ (۳۰) فاذا زنت الحامل لم تُحدَّ حتى تضع حملها . (صفحہ 387 پر) [۲۴۷۱] (۲۸) بیمار نے زنا کیا اور اس کی حد رجم ہو تو رحم کیا جائے گا۔ رجم کر کے مارنا ہی مقصود ہے اس لئے بیمار ہو یا غیر بیمار ہو اس سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑتا۔ اس لئے تندرست ہونے تک انتظار نہیں کیا جائے (۲۴۷۲ (۲۹) اور اگر اس کی حد کوڑے لگا نا ہوتو کوڑے نہ لگائے جائیں یہاں تک کہ اچھا ہو جائے۔ اگر حد کوڑے لگا نا ہو تو بیمار آدمی کو ابھی کوڑے نہ لگا ئیں تندرست ہونے کے بعد کوڑے لگا ئیں۔ تا کہ زیادہ بیمار نہ ہو جائے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ نفساء باندی پر کوڑے لگانا تھا تو نفاس ختم ہونے تک تاخیر کی تاکہ زیادہ بیمار نہ ہو جائے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی عبد الرحمن ... فان امة لرسول الله الا الله زنت فامرنى ان اجلدها فاذا هي حديث عهد بنفاس فخشيت ان انا جلدتها ان اقتلها فذكرت ذلك للنبى الله الله فقال احسنت (الف)(مسلم شریف، باب تا خیر الحد عن النفساء ص ۶۷ نمبر ۷۰۵ ارترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی اقامتہ الحمد علی الا ماء ص ۲۶۶ نمبر (۱۴۴) اس حدیث میں عورت نفاس میں تھی تو اس کو تندرست ہونے کے بعد کوڑے لگائے ۔ انت ببراً : تندرست ہو جائے ،ٹھیک ہو جائے۔
[2471] (28) And if the sick person commits zina and his hadd is stoning, he is stoned. [2472] (29) And if his hadd is flogging, he is not flogged until he recovers. [2473] (30) And if a pregnant woman commits zina, she is not penalized until she gives birth. [2471] (28) A sick person committed zina and his hadd is stoning, so stoning will be done. The purpose is to kill by stoning, so whether sick or not, it makes no difference. Therefore, one does not wait until recovery. [2472] (29) And if his hadd is flogging, then flogging will not be applied until he becomes well. If the hadd is flogging, do not flog the sick person now; flog after recovery so that he does not become more ill. (2) There is a hadith that a slave woman in postpartum bleeding was to be flogged, so flogging was delayed until after postpartum bleeding so that she would not become more ill. The hadith: From Abu Abdurrahman... that a slave woman of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) committed zina, so he ordered me to flog her. I found that she had recently given birth and was in postpartum bleeding. I feared that if I flogged her, she might die. So I mentioned that to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and he said: You did well. (Muslim, Bab ta'khir al-hadd 'an al-nafsa', p. 67, no. 705; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi iqamat al-hadd 'ala al-ima', p. 266, no. 144) In this hadith, the woman was in postpartum bleeding, so she was flogged after recovery. 'anta bi barra' : you become healthy, become well.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage presents three rulings (28, 29, 30) concerning the application of hadd penalties on individuals with health-related conditions. The first ruling (28) addresses a sick person whose hadd is stoning (i.e., he is muhsan). Since stoning is a capital punishment intended to cause death, the sick person is stoned immediately without waiting for recovery. The condition of sickness does not affect this ruling because the goal is execution. The second ruling (29) applies if the hadd is flogging (i.e., the person is a bikr). Here, flogging is delayed until the person recovers from illness. The reason given is that flogging a sick person could worsen their condition or even cause death, so it is postponed. The commentator cites a hadith about a postpartum slave woman: the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved delaying her flogging until after her postpartum state ended. This serves as a precedent for delaying flogging for health reasons. The third ruling (30) will be covered in the next lesson. The key principle is that stoning, being capital, is executed immediately, while flogging is postponed to avoid excessive harm.

Key Terms
المريض (al-marid): A person who is ill to the extent that flogging may cause harm or death.
النفساء (al-nafsa'): A woman in the postpartum period after childbirth, during which she is considered weak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what should be done if a sick person commits zina and his hadd is stoning?
A) Delay stoning until recovery
B) Execute stoning immediately
C) Replace stoning with flogging
D) Pardon him

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hudud, stoning is never delayed due to illness, but flogging is delayed until recovery to avoid harm, based on the Prophet's approval of delaying the flogging of a postpartum slave woman.

Delaying Flogging for a Sick Person
Ruling that flogging is delayed for a sick person until health is restored.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on flogging a sick person and identify the hadith proof used to justify the delay.

Core Idea
Flogging is wajib but delayed for a sick person to avoid worsening harm — the Prophet praised this postponement.

In the application of hudud penalties, the Shari'ah balances justice with mercy. This ruling addresses a specific situation: when a person liable to flogging is ill. Rather than immediate execution, the penalty is postponed until recovery, demonstrating that preservation of life and avoidance of excess harm take precedence over the timing of the punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the prescribed hadd for a non-muhsan person? Flogging. What does the text rule? That flogging is not carried out until the person recovers.
The ruling is about the timing of the penalty, not its obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites a hadith about a postpartum slave woman. The Prophet (peace be upon him) approved delaying her flogging.
The hadith is found in Muslim and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit words of praise (أحسنت) show that postponing flogging due to health risk is commendable and therefore establishes the ruling.
The illah is the risk of worsening illness or death.
4
Note the scope and limitations
The ruling applies only to flogging, not to other hadd penalties like stoning (rajm), which are not delayed for illness.
The text does not discuss stoning, but commentators clarify this distinction.
5
Evaluate the authority
The ruling is based on a sahih hadith and is agreed upon among schools (muttafaq alayh). It is from the zahir al-riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned.

Commentary
This passage specifically focuses on ruling (29): if a sick person's prescribed hadd is flogging (i.e., he is a non-muhsan), the flogging is delayed until he recovers from his illness. This lesson underscores the Hanafi concern for avoiding excessive harm (la darar wa la dirar) in the application of hadd penalties.

Delaying Hadd for Pregnant Woman Until After Delivery
Ruling with proof via prophetic incident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponing hadd for a pregnant woman and explain the rationale based on the incident of al-Ghamidiyyah.

Core Idea
Hadd is delayed to protect the innocent fetus, not waived.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a pregnant woman is liable to stoning (hadd al-rajm), the punishment is not executed until she delivers the child and proper care is arranged. This ruling is based on the prophetic precedent of al-Ghamidiyyah. The underlying principle is the prevention of harm to an innocent third party — the unborn child. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zina by a pregnant muhsan woman. The ruling is that the hadd (stoning) is wajib but its execution is delayed until after childbirth and childcare arrangements.
The delay is not a cancellation.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the incident of al-Ghamidiyyah, a sahih hadith. The Prophet (peace be upon him) delayed her stoning until she delivered and a nurse was found for the child.
This is a Sunnah ahad report.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit action — waiting for the child to be born and cared for — demonstrates that the hadd must be postponed to avoid harming the child. The child is innocent and not responsible for the mother's sin.
The welfare of the child overrides immediate punishment.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies whether the pregnancy resulted from the zina or was pre-existing. It is specific to stoning (hadd for muhsan), but the principle of avoiding harm to a third party could extend to other punishments that would endanger the fetus.
The text focuses on rajm; flogging may also be delayed if it risks miscarriage.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi school uniformly holds this position. It is based on the practice of the Prophet and is considered agreed upon across madhahib.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۳ (۳۰) فاذا زنت الحامل لم تُحدَّ حتى تضع حملها . (۳۰) اگر حاملہ عورت نے زنا کرایا تو حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی یہاں تک کہ وضع حمل ہو جائے۔ زنا کرانے کی وجہ سے حاملہ ہوگئی ہے یا حمل کی حالت میں زنا کرایا دونوں صورتوں میں بچہ پیدا ہو جائے اور بچے کی پرورش کا انتظام ہو جائے تب عورت رجم کی جائےگی۔ اگر حمل کی حالت میں رجم کر دیں تو بچے کی موت واقع ہوگی اور بچے کی کوئی غلطی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے حمل کی حالت میں رجم نہیں کی جائے گی (۲) حضرت غامد یہ حاملہ تھی تو حضور نے وضع حمل کے بعد بچے کی پرورش کا انتظام ہوا تب اس کو رجم کیا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے ۔ قال ثم جاءته امرأة من غامد من الازد فقالت يا رسول الله طهرني ... فاتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال قد وضعت الغامدية فقال اذا لا نرجمها وندع ولدها صغيرة ليس له من يرضعه فقام رجل من الانصار فقال الى رضاعه يا نبي الله ! قال فرجمها
[2473] (30) And if a pregnant woman commits zina, she is not penalized until she gives birth. (30) If a pregnant woman commits zina, the hadd will not be applied until she delivers. Whether she became pregnant due to zina or committed zina while already pregnant, in both cases, after the child is born and arrangements for its care are made, then the woman will be stoned. If she is stoned while pregnant, the child would die, and the child is not at fault. Therefore, she is not stoned while pregnant. (2) Al-Ghamidiyyah was pregnant, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) stoned her after delivery and after arranging for the child's nursing. The hadith fragment: He said: Then a woman from Ghamid from Azd came to him and said: O Messenger of Allah, purify me... Then the Prophet (peace be upon him) came and said: Al-Ghamidiyyah has given birth. He said: Then we will not stone her and leave her child small with no one to nurse him. So a man from the Ansar said: I will take care of his nursing, O Prophet of Allah. He said: Then he stoned her.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling (30) that a pregnant woman who is liable to hadd (specifically stoning, as she was muhsan) is not punished until after she gives birth and until arrangements are made for the child's care. The commentator explains that this applies whether the pregnancy resulted from the zina or occurred before. The reason is to protect the unborn child from harm, since stoning would inevitably kill the fetus, and the fetus is innocent. The commentator cites the well-known incident of al-Ghamidiyyah, who came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) seeking purification. The Prophet delayed her stoning until after she delivered, and then arranged for a man to nurse the child before the punishment was carried out. This demonstrates the principle of considering the welfare of the child. The ruling is specific to stoning (hadd for muhsan); if the hadd were flogging, the same reasoning would apply to avoid harm to the fetus? The text does not specify, but the focus is on stoning. The underlying principle is that the hadd is delayed to prevent harm to an innocent third party (the child).

Key Terms
الحامل (al-hamil): A pregnant woman who is liable to hadd (usually muhsan).
وضع حملها (wada' hamlaha): To give birth, to deliver the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A pregnant woman's hadd (stoning) is wajib but must be delayed until after childbirth and childcare arrangements, based on the prophetic precedent of protecting the innocent child.

Stoning a Sick Person: Immediate Execution
Ruling statement with purpose-based expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on executing rajm on a sick person and explain the purpose-based rationale (maqsad) that justifies immediate execution.

Core Idea
Sickness does not delay stoning (rajm) because the purpose is to kill, and health does not affect death.

This lesson addresses a specific legal question: should a person who is sentenced to stoning (rajm) for adultery have their punishment delayed if they become sick? The text presents the Hanafi position clearly: no delay is allowed. The reasoning is rooted in the very purpose of the punishment (maqsad). Understanding this ruling helps clarify how Hanafi jurists prioritize the objectives of punishments over incidental conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the execution of rajm on a sick person who has been convicted. The ruling is that he is stoned immediately.
The matn says 'he is stoned'; the commentator confirms no delay.
2
Extract the explicit hukm
The base text states the ruling, and the commentary reinforces that waiting for health is not required.
The phrase 'he is stoned' is unconditional.
3
Analyze the talil (purpose-based reasoning)
The commentator provides the rationale: the purpose (maqsad) of rajm is to kill by stoning. Since death does not depend on health, sickness is irrelevant.
This is a teleological argument (al-maqsad).
4
Contrast with the next ruling (lashes)
The text implies that for lashes (jald), sickness does delay execution, highlighting the uniqueness of rajm.
This contrast reinforces the specific logic for rajm.
5
Note the authority weight
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement is reported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۱ (۲۸) واذا زنى المريض وحده الرجم رجم
[۲۴۷۱] (۲۸) بیمار نے زنا کیا اور اس کی حدر جم ہو تو رحم کیا جائے گا۔ رحم کر کے مارنا ہی مقصود ہے اس لئے بیمار ہو یا غیر بیمار ہو اس سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑتا۔ اس لئے تندرست ہونے تک انتظار نہیں کیا جائے
When a sick person commits adultery and his punishment is stoning, he is stoned. A sick person committed adultery and his punishment is stoning: he is stoned. The purpose is to kill by stoning, so whether he is sick or not, there is no difference. Therefore one does not wait until he becomes healthy.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn expanded by the commentator. The author states the principle that when a person is already sentenced to stoning (rajm), even if they become sick, the punishment is not delayed. The reason given is that the objective of rajm is to cause death, and death does not depend on health. Since rajm is already a fatal punishment, it is carried out immediately. The commentator clarifies that the same applies whether the person is sick or healthy, so there is no waiting for recovery. This ruling is specific to rajm; the next ruling addresses the case of lashes where waiting is required.

Key Terms
الرجم (al-rajm): The fixed punishment (hadd) for adultery for a married person, consisting of stoning to death.
المريض (al-marīḍ): A person suffering from illness or disease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The stoning is carried out immediately without waiting.
C) The stoning is changed to lashes due to sickness.
D) The stoning is delayed indefinitely until health improves.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sickness does not delay rajm because its purpose is death, and health is irrelevant to that outcome.

Postponing Lashes for a Sick Person
Presents ruling: sick person with hadd of lashes is not lashed until recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponing lashes for a sick person and explain the prophetic proof used to derive this ruling.

Core Idea
A sick person must not be lashed until recovery — the Prophet delayed lashing a woman in nifas to prevent harm.

This lesson addresses the specific hadd punishment of lashes (jald) for an unmarried adulterer. The Hanafi school rules that if the offender is ill, the lashes are postponed until he recovers, based on a hadith where the Prophet delayed lashing a woman in postpartum bleeding. The ruling demonstrates the principle of avoiding additional harm in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that if a person's hadd is lashes (jald), they are not to be lashed until they recover. Identify this as the ruling: postponement of the punishment due to sickness.
The ruling applies to lashes, not to other punishments like stoning.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim about a slave woman in nifas whose lashing was delayed by the Prophet's approval.
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad, which provides a zanni proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's approval indicates that lashing a person in a weak condition is harmful and must be avoided. This is analogized to any illness.
The illah (ratio legis) is preventing harm or death.
4
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
This ruling is muttafaq alayh; there is no major disagreement among schools.
Some schools might have nuances, but the principle is widely accepted.
5
Determine the thamarah
The practical consequence is that a sick person is not flogged until fully recovered, ensuring mercy in the execution of hudud.
This reflects the broader Sharia principle of easing hardships.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۲ (۲۹) وان كان حده الجلد لم يجلد حتى يبرأ
[۲۴۷۲] (۲۹) اور اگر اس کی حد کوڑ الگا نا ہو تو کوڑے نہ لگائے جائیں یہاں تک کہ اچھا ہو جائے۔
اگر حد کوڑے لگا نا ہو تو بیمار آدمی کو ابھی کوڑے نہ لگا ئیں تندرست ہونے کے بعد کوڑے لگا ئیں۔ تا کہ زیادہ بیمار نہ ہو جائے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ نفساء باندی پر کوڑے لگانا تھا تو نفاس ختم ہونے تک تاخیر کی تاکہ زیادہ بیمار نہ ہو جائے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی عبد الرحمن ... فان امة لرسول الله الا الله زنت فامرنى ان اجلدها فاذا هي حديث عهد بنفاس فخشيت ان انا جلدتها ان اقتلها فذكرت ذلك للنبى الله الله فقال احسنت (الف)(مسلم شریف، باب تا خیر الحد عن النفساء ص ۶۷ نمبر ۷۰۵ ارترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی اقامتہ الحمد علی الا ماء ص ۲۶۶ نمبر (۱۴۴) اس حدیث میں عورت نفاس میں تھی تو اس کو تندرست ہونے کے بعد کوڑے لگائے ۔
انت ببراً : تندرست ہو جائے ،ٹھیک ہو جائے۔
And if his punishment is lashes, he is not lashed until he recovers. And if his punishment is lashes, then lashes are not applied until he becomes healthy. If the punishment is lashes, do not lash the sick person immediately; lash after he becomes healthy, so that he does not become more ill. (2) The hadith: a slave woman of the Prophet committed adultery and he ordered me to lash her, and I found she was recently in nifas and feared that if I lash her she might die, so I mentioned that to the Prophet and he said 'you did well' (Muslim). In this hadith, the woman was in nifas, so she was lashed after becoming healthy. 'Tabarra' means to become healthy.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The base ruling states that a sick person who must receive lashes (hadd jald) is not flogged until they recover. The commentator explains the wisdom: to prevent the punishment from causing additional harm or death. The proof comes from a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ delayed the flogging of a slave woman who was in nifas (postpartum bleeding). Although the case involves nifas, the principle is extended to any illness: lashes are delayed to avoid exacerbating the condition. The Arabic word 'yabra' refers to complete recovery. The hadith is cited from Sahih Muslim. This ruling is specific to lashes; the earlier lesson showed that rajm is not delayed.

Key Terms
الجلد (al-jald): The fixed punishment (hadd) for adultery for an unmarried person, consisting of lashes (usually 100).
النفاس (al-nifās): Postpartum bleeding after childbirth, a condition that prevents a woman from fasting, prayer, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A verse from the Quran about mercy.
B) The hadith of the slave woman in nifas whose lashing was postponed by the Prophet.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Analogy with prayer of the sick.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates postponing lashes for a sick person to prevent harm, based on the Prophet's approval of delaying the lashing of a woman in nifas.

Postponing Hadd for Pregnant Women Until Delivery
States ruling: pregnant woman not punished until delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponing hadd punishment for a pregnant woman and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A pregnant woman’s hadd is delayed to protect her unborn child's life.

This ruling addresses the intersection of criminal justice and mercy in Islamic law. While hadd punishments are severe, the Hanafi school, following the Prophet's example, ensures that an innocent child is not harmed. This lesson examines the ruling, its rationale, and the primary proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is the act being judged? A pregnant woman commits adultery. What is the ruling? She is not punished until she delivers the child.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the pregnancy resulted from the adultery or was pre-existing.
2
Understand the Rationale
Why postpone? The commentator explains that stoning during pregnancy would kill the innocent child. The child has no fault, so punishment is delayed to protect its life.
This shows the Shari’ah's concern for the innocent.
3
Locate the Dalil
What proof supports this ruling? The hadith of the woman from Ghamid (Ghamidiyya).
The hadith is found in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud.
4
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet explicitly waited for her to deliver and for a wet nurse to be arranged before stoning her. This shows that punishment during pregnancy is not allowed.
The Prophet's action is a binding sunnah (zanni al-thubut but accepted).
5
Note the Scope
Does this apply to all pregnant women? Yes, regardless of how she became pregnant. The ruling also includes the requirement to secure the child's care after delivery before punishment.
The care provision is also evident from the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۳ (۳۰) فاذا زنت الحامل لم تُحدَّ حتى تضع حملها
[۲۴۷۳] (۳۰) اگر حاملہ عورت نے زنا کرایا تو حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی یہاں تک کہ وضع حمل ہو جائے۔ زنا کرانے کی وجہ سے حاملہ ہوگئی ہے یا حمل کی حالت میں زنا کرایا دونوں صورتوں میں بچہ پیدا ہو جائے اور بچے کی پرورش کا انتظام ہو جائے تب عورت رحم کی جائے گی۔ اگر حمل کی حالت میں رجم کر دیں تو بچے کی موت واقع ہوگی اور بچے کی کوئی غلطی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے حمل کی حالت میں رجم نہیں کی جائے گی (۲) حضرت غامد یہ حاملہ تھی تو حضور نے وضع حمل کے بعد بچے کی پرورش کا انتظام ہوا تب اس کو رجم کیا۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے ۔ قال ثم
جــاء تــه امــرأة من غامد من الازد فقالت يا رسول الله طهرني ... فاتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال قد وضعت الغامدية فقال اذا لا نرجمها وندع ولدها صغيرة ليس له من يرضعه فقام رجل من الانصار فقال الى رضاعه يا نبي الله ! قال فرجمها
When a pregnant woman commits adultery, she is not punished until she delivers. If a pregnant woman committed adultery, punishment is not applied until delivery. If she became pregnant from the adultery or committed adultery while already pregnant, in both cases, after childbirth and when arrangements for the child's care are made, then she is stoned. If she is stoned during pregnancy, the child would die and the child has no fault, so she is not stoned during pregnancy. The case of Lady Ghamidiyya: she was pregnant and the Prophet delayed her stoning until after delivery and care for the child. The hadith: A woman from Ghamid came and said 'O Prophet, purify me'... then the Prophet said 'The Ghamidiyya has delivered', so he said 'Then we will not stone her and leave her child small with no one to nurse him.' A man from the Ansar stood and said 'I will take care of his nursing, O Prophet.' He said 'So stone her.'
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This ruling covers the case of a pregnant woman who is liable to hadd (either rajm or jald, but focus here on rajm). The text states clearly that punishment is postponed until she delivers the child. The commentator explains the rationale: stoning or lashing during pregnancy could kill the unborn child, who is innocent. The ruling applies whether the pregnancy resulted from the adultery or was pre-existing. The proof is the well-known hadith of the woman from Ghamid who confessed to adultery while pregnant. The Prophet delayed her stoning until after she delivered and a wet nurse was found for the infant. This establishes the principle that the baby's life and care must be taken into account. Note that this lesson primarily addresses the initial postponement until delivery; the next lessons detail what happens after delivery for each type of punishment.

Key Terms
الحامل (al-ḥāmil): A pregnant woman who commits adultery and is liable to hadd.
وضع الحمل (waḍʿ al-ḥaml): Childbirth, delivery of the baby.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadd punishment for a pregnant woman delayed until after delivery according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because pregnancy makes her immune to punishment.
B) Because the Prophet never punished pregnant women.
C) To protect the unborn child from harm.
D) Because she needs to recover from childbirth first.

Key Takeaway
Hadd punishment for a pregnant woman is wajib to delay until delivery and child care arrangements, based on the Prophet's handling of the Ghamidiyya case.

Ruling on Lashes for a Postpartum Woman After Nifas
Specifies timing of lashes for a woman after childbirth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for administering lashes to a postpartum woman and derive the ruling from the hadith.

Core Idea
Lashes for a postpartum woman are delayed only until nifas ends—child care arrangements are not required.

This passage clarifies the timing of hadd lashes for a woman after childbirth. Unlike stoning (rajm), lashes do not require waiting for child care because they are less severe. The key condition is the completion of nifas, as established by a sahih hadith. By the end of this lesson, you will grasp the precise ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is administering hadd lashes to a woman who has given birth. The ruling is that it is wajib, but its execution is delayed until she becomes free from nifas.
The ruling applies only to lashes (jald), not to stoning (rajm).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Sahih Muslim: the Prophet ﷺ ordered postponing lashes for a slave woman who had recently given birth and was still in nifas.
The hadith is ahad, but it is accepted in hudud matters according to the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'leave her until she recovers' indicates that the condition is recovery from nifas. The term 'tumāthil' (recovers) specifically points to cessation of postpartum bleeding.
This shows that nifas is considered a state of illness that must end before punishment.
4
Distinguish from rajm
For rajm, the text requires both delivery and arranging child care because rajm is fatal. For lashes, only delivery and end of nifas are required, as lashes are not fatal to the child.
This distinction is based on the illa of harm to the child.
5
Conclude the conditions
Two conditions: (1) the child must be born, and (2) the woman must be free from nifas. No additional waiting for child care is needed.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۴ (۳۱) وان كان حدها الجلد فحتى تتعالى من نفاسها
[۲۴۷۴] (۳۱) اور اس کی حد کوڑے ہوں تو یہاں تک کہ نفاس سے پاک ہو جائے۔
اگر حاملہ عورت پر کوڑا لگنا ہو تو چونکہ اس میں انسان کو مارنا نہیں ہے اس لئے بچے کی پرورش کے انتظام تک انتظار کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ لیکن بچہ پیدا ہو جائے اور عورت نفاس سے پاک ہو جائے تب کوڑے لگائے جائیں۔ تا کہ بچے کو نقصان نہ ہو اور بچے کی موت واقع نہ ہو۔ نیز عورت نفاس میں ہے تو گویا کہ ایک مرض میں ہے اس لئے مرض سے تندرست ہو جائے تب کوڑے لگائے جائیں گے (۲) اوپر حدیث گزری کہ نفاس کے بعد کوڑے لگائے گئے۔ فان امة لرسول الله زنت فامرنى ان اجلدها فاذا هي حديث عهد بنفاس فخشيت ان انا جلدتها ان اقتلها فذكرت ذلك للنبى الله الله فقال احسنت ۔ اور دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ اتركها حتى تماثل (ب) (مسلم شریف ، باب تا خیر الحد عن النفساء ص ۶۷ نمبر ۱۷۰۵ را بود اؤ د شریف ، باب فی اقمته الحد علی المریض ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۴۴۷۳ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفاس والی عورت کا نفاس ختم ہو جائے تب کوڑے لگیں گے۔
تعالی : بلند ہو جائے ، نفاس سے باہر ہو جائے۔
And if her punishment is lashes, then until she becomes clean from her nifas. And if her punishment is lashes, then until she becomes purified from nifas. If a pregnant woman is to be lashed, since it does not involve killing, there is no need to wait for arranging child care. But the child must be born and the woman be pure from nifas, then lashes are applied, so that the child is not harmed and does not die. Also, a woman in nifas is like in a state of illness, so lashes are postponed until she recovers. The hadith above mentioned that after nifas she was lashed: 'the slave woman of the Prophet committed adultery... he said you did well.' And in another narration: 'Leave her until she recovers.' This hadith shows that a woman in nifas is lashed after nifas ends. 'Ta'āla' means to become elevated, to go out of nifas.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This ruling specifies the timing of lashes for a woman after childbirth. Unlike rajm, which requires both delivery and arrangement of child care, lashes only require that the child is born and the mother has completed her nifas (postpartum bleeding). The reason is that lashes are not fatal, so the risk of killing the child is less; however, striking the mother during pregnancy could still cause a miscarriage. After birth, the child is safe from the lashes. Nifas is considered a state of illness, and the same principle of delaying punishment until recovery applies, as established by the hadith of the slave woman in nifas. The commentator stresses that nifas must end completely before administering lashes.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifās): Postpartum bleeding that prevents ritual purity and is considered a state of illness for legal purposes.
تتعالى (tataʿālā): To become elevated, i.e., to be free from nifas and in a state of purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately after delivery.
B) After child care arrangements are made, regardless of nifas.
C) After nifas ends, even if child care is not arranged.
D) Only after the child is weaned.

Key Takeaway
Lashes for a postpartum woman are wajib but are executed only after nifas ends; child care arrangements are not a condition.

Postponing Rajm for Childbirth and Childcare
Specifies timing of rajm for a woman after childbirth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for executing rajm on a pregnant woman and apply the Hanafi ruling that childcare arrangements must be made before stoning.

Core Idea
Rajm of a pregnant woman is delayed until after childbirth and childcare is ensured.

The hadd penalty of stoning (rajm) applies to a married adulterer or adulteress. If the condemned woman is pregnant, execution is postponed until after delivery and the end of nifas. Moreover, the community must arrange for the infant's care before stoning the mother. This ruling safeguards the child's life and is derived from the prophetic practice with the woman of Ghamidiyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? Execution of rajm on a pregnant/mother woman. The ruling: wajib to delay until after delivery and nifas, and conditionally after childcare.
The obligation is on the state/community.
2
Locate the condition
The text adds 'bisharṭīkah' (provided that) – childcare must be arranged. Without it, rajm is impermissible.
This is a shart (condition) for validity of the execution.
3
Trace the hadith evidence
The hadith of Ghamidiyya: The Prophet (ﷺ) waited until she delivered and then arranged a wet nurse before stoning her. This is the basis.
Though zanni in transmission, the practice is accepted.
4
Note the wisdom (sabab)
The ruling protects the child from being lost due to the mother's death. Child welfare is prioritized over immediate punishment.
This reflects the maqasid (preservation of life).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۵ (۳۲) وان كان حدها الرجم رجمت
[۲۴۷۵] (۳۲) اگر اس کی حد رجم ہو تو رجم کیا جائے گا۔
حاملہ عورت کی حد رجم ہو تو نفاس سے باہر آنے کے بعد رجم کی جاسکتی ہے لیکن بشر طیکہ بچے کی پرورش کا انتظام ہو چکا ہو۔ اور اگر نہ ہوا ہو تو پرورش کے انتظام کے بعد رحم کرے تا کہ بچہ ضائع نہ ہو۔
And if her punishment is stoning, she is stoned. If a pregnant woman's punishment is stoning, she can be stoned after coming out of nifas, but provided that arrangements for the child's care have been made. And if not, then after arranging care she should be stoned so that the child is not lost.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This ruling complements the previous ones. For a woman sentenced to stoning, the delay continues beyond just delivery and nifas: the community must arrange care for the infant before executing the punishment. The reason is that stoning causes the mother's death, leaving the child without a caregiver. Therefore, ensuring the child's welfare is a precondition. This is based on the hadith of Ghamidiyya, where the Prophet arranged for a wet nurse before stoning her. The commentator uses the word 'bisharṭīkah' meaning 'provided that'.

Key Terms
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as hadd for married adulterer/adulteress.
بشرط (bi-sharṭ): Condition (provided that) – here the condition is that child care is arranged before rajm is executed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Her nifas must end.
B) The child's care must be arranged.
C) Her husband must consent.
D) The child must be weaned.

Key Takeaway
Rajm of a mother is postponed until after delivery and nifas, but only after childcare is arranged to protect the child.

Testimony About an Old Hadd Punishment
States ruling on accepting testimony about a long-past hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony about an old hadd and explain the talil (rationale) behind the rejection.

Core Idea
Old hadd testimony is rejected; initial concealment is praiseworthy, later testimony may be malice.

In Hanafi criminal procedure, testimony about a hadd punishment that was committed long ago is generally not accepted unless the witnesses had a valid excuse for the delay. This ruling balances the need for justice with the protection of privacy and the prevention of frivolous accusations. The passage explains the rationale and the exception for qadhf and civil cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is giving testimony about a hadd crime after a long delay. The ruling is that such testimony is not accepted.
Focus on the condition 'old' (mutaqadim) and the absence of a valid excuse.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
The commentator provides the reason: the initial silence may be due to commendable concealment of faults; later testimony could be motivated by enmity. This explains why the ruling is strict.
This is a istihsan-based rationale, not a direct textual proof.
3
Identify the exception and its basis
The exception is the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of adultery), which is treated like a right of the individual (ḥaqq ādamī). The text also notes that in civil transactions (muʿāmalāt), old testimony is accepted because they are rights of people.
The distinction is between ḥuqūq Allāh and ḥuqūq al-ʿibād.
4
Evaluate the practical implication
A judge must reject delayed testimony for hadd unless the witnesses prove a valid excuse (e.g., the imam was far away). The ruling prevents misuse of the judicial system for personal grudges.
This protects the integrity of hadd punishments and encourages repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۷۶ (۳۳) واذا شهد الشهود بحد متقادم لم يمنعهم عن اقامته
[۲۴۷۶] (۳۳) اگر گواہوں نے پرانی حد کی گواہی دی جس کو قائم کرنے سے امام سے دور ہونا اس کو روکتا نہ تھا تو ان کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی مگر خاص طور پر حد قذف میں۔ معاملات میں پرانی گواہی بھی قابل قبول ہے کیونکہ وہ حقوق العباد ہیں۔ لیکن حد اور حقوق اللہ کے بارے میں اگر کوئی عذر نہیں تھا مثلا امام سے اتنا دور نہیں تھا کہ اتنی تاخیر کرنے کی ضرورت ہو پھر بھی گواہی دینے میں بہت تاخیر کی تو یہ گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ ابتدا میں گواہی نہ دینے کی وجہ یہ ہوسکتی ہے کہ مجرم پر پردہ پوشی کرنا چاہتا تھا جس کی حدیث میں ترغیب ہے۔ بعد میں کسی حسد اور بغض کی بنا
حاشیه : (الف) قبیلہ از دکی عورت حضور کے پاس آئی اور کہا غامد یہ نے بچہ دے دیا ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا میں اس کو جسم نہیں کروں گا کیونکہ اس کے چھوٹے بچے کو ایسا نہیں چھوڑ سکتا کہ کوئی اس کو دودھ پلانے والا نہ ہو۔ پس انصار کا ایک آدمی کھڑا ہوا اور کہا میرے ذمہ اس کا دودھ پلانا ہے اے اللہ کے رسول ! آپ نے فرمایا اب اس کو رجم کرو (ب) حضور کی ایک باندی نے زنا کرایا تو مجھ کوحکم دیا کہ میں اس پر کوڑے لگاؤں، میں نے دیکھا کہ وہ ابھی نفاس میں ہے اور مجھے ڈر ہوا کہ اگر اس کو کوڑے لگاؤں تو وہ مر جائے گی۔ میں نے اس کا تذکرہ حضور سے کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا اچھا کیا کہ ابھی چھوڑ دیا۔ دوسری روایت میں ٹھیک ہونے تک اسے چھوڑ دو۔
When witnesses testify about an old hadd that distance from the imam did not prevent [them from reporting earlier], their testimony is not accepted, except specifically in hadd of qadhf. In transactions, old testimony is acceptable because they are rights of people. But regarding hadd and rights of Allah, if there was no excuse such as the imam being so far away that such delay was necessary, and still they delayed testifying greatly, then their testimony is not accepted. The reason for not testifying initially could be that he wanted to conceal the criminal, which is encouraged in hadith. Later due to some envy and malice...
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This ruling addresses the acceptance of testimony regarding a hadd punishment that was committed long ago. The principle is that if witnesses witnessed a hadd crime but did not report it promptly without a valid excuse (such as the imam being far away), their later testimony is not accepted for hadd punishments (except qadhf, where the right of the victim is involved). In civil matters (ḥuqūq al-ʿibād), delayed testimony is still acceptable because it concerns individual rights. The rationale is that the initial silence may be due to a praiseworthy concealment of faults, but subsequent testimony may be motivated by personal enmity. The footnote includes the hadith of Ghamidiyya as an example of the correct procedure. This teaches that the hadd system is not merely punitive but also protects privacy and encourages sincere repentance.

Key Terms
حد متقادم (hadd mutaqādim): An old hadd punishment, i.e., a fixed punishment for a crime that was committed long ago, concerning which testimony is given after a significant delay.
حقوق الله (ḥuqūq Allāh): Rights of Allah, which include hadd punishments; these are not subject to leniency in testimony.
حقوق العباد (ḥuqūq al-ʿibād): Rights of people, such as financial claims; testimony is accepted even after delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, why is testimony about an old hadd (mutaqadim) generally not accepted?
A) Because witnesses may have forgotten details.
B) Because the initial silence may indicate concealment, and later testimony could be motivated by enmity.
C) Because the criminal may have repented.
D) Because the imam is no longer in power.

Key Takeaway
Testimony about an old hadd is rejected unless a valid excuse explains the delay, preserving the integrity of hadd and preventing misuse.

Postponement of Hadd for Pregnant Woman
Ruling on delaying hadd for pregnant woman with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on postponing hadd for a pregnant woman and distinguish between the conditions for flogging and stoning.

Core Idea
Hadd for a pregnant woman is wajib but delayed: flogging after nifas, stoning after the child is weaned.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses a nuanced point in Hanafi fiqh: the timing of hudud punishments for pregnant women. The ruling distinguishes between jald and rajm based on the severity of the punishment and the need to protect the child. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the hadd correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of hadd
Note that the passage discusses two punishments: flogging (jald) and stoning (rajm). Their conditions for postponement differ.
2
Analyze the condition for flogging
For flogging, the hadd is postponed only until the woman becomes free from nifas (postpartum bleeding). No need to wait for weaning because flogging is not lethal.
Reason: to avoid harm during illness and protect the child from physical shock.
3
Analyze the condition for stoning
For stoning, the hadd is postponed until after delivery and until the child's upbringing is arranged (i.e., weaning or an alternative caregiver). Stoning is lethal, so the child must not be left without care.
This is based on the hadith of the woman from Ghāmidiyya.
4
Examine the prophetic proof
The hadith of the slave girl who was flogged after nifas (with the Prophet's approval) shows that flogging is not delayed beyond nifas. The stoning case of the Ghāmidiyya woman shows the need for weaning.
Both hadiths are from Sahih Muslim.
5
Recognize the rationale
The difference in delay reflects the severity: flogging does not kill, so only the woman's health is considered; stoning kills, so the child's welfare takes priority.
This is a core Hanafi principle: al-maslahah (public interest) guides the implementation of punishments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if her hadd is flogging, then until she becomes free from her nifas. [2475 (32)] And if her hadd is stoning, she is stoned. [2476 (33)] And if the witnesses testify to an old hadd that does not prevent them from establishing it... (a) From this hadith it is known that a pregnant woman should give birth and arrangement for the child's upbringing be made, then she is stoned. [2474] (31) And if her hadd is lashes, then until she becomes pure from nifas. If a pregnant woman is to be lashed, since it does not kill a person, there is no need to wait for the arrangement of the child's upbringing. But after the child is born and the woman becomes pure from nifas, lashes are inflicted, so that the child is not harmed and the child's death does not occur. Also, the woman is in nifas, which is like an illness, so after she recovers from the illness, lashes are inflicted. (2) The hadith passed that lashes were inflicted after nifas: 'A slave girl of the Messenger of Allah committed zina, so he ordered me to flog her. I found she was recently in nifas, and I feared that if I flogged her I would kill her. So I mentioned that to the Prophet, and he said: You did well.' And in another narration: 'Leave her until she recovers.' (b) From this hadith it is known that a woman in nifas is to be lashed after her nifas ends. Ta'ala: becomes high, exits nifas. (2475 (32)) If her hadd is stoning, she is stoned. If a pregnant woman's hadd is stoning, she can be stoned after exiting nifas, provided that the arrangement for the child's upbringing has been made. If not, then after the arrangement of upbringing, she is stoned so that the child is not lost.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage addresses the postponement of hadd punishments for pregnant women. The ruling is divided based on the type of punishment. For flogging (jald), the hadd is postponed only until the woman becomes pure from nifas (postpartum bleeding). The reasoning given is that flogging does not kill, so there is no need to wait for weaning; however, it is delayed to protect the child from harm and because the woman is ill during nifas. For stoning (rajm), the hadd is postponed until after delivery and until the child's upbringing is arranged, because stoning results in death and the child would be left without care. The proofs cited include the hadith of the woman from Ghāmidiyya who was stoned after the Prophet arranged for her child's nursing, and the hadith of the slave girl who was flogged after her nifas. The commentator emphasizes that the waiting period differs according to the severity of the punishment.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding after childbirth.
وضع حمل (wad' al-haml): Delivery of the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After she gives birth and the child is weaned.
B) After she gives birth and becomes pure from nifas, regardless of weaning.
C) Immediately, because pregnancy is not a valid excuse.
D) Only after the child reaches the age of two.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school delays flogging only until nifas ends, but delays stoning until the child is weaned, based on the type of punishment and child welfare.

Acceptance of Delayed Testimony for Hadd
Ruling on testimony regarding an old hadd and its exception for qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for delayed testimony on hadd and apply the exception for qadhf.

Core Idea
Delayed testimony for hadd is rejected unless it's qadhf — a right of the servant.

This passage explains the Hanafi position on accepting testimony regarding hudud when the testimony is delayed. The general rule is that unjustified delay suggests the witness's motive changed from concealment (encouraged) to enmity, making testimony unreliable. However, there is an exception for hadd qadhf because it involves the right of the accused. The proof is the statement of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The Hanafi school does not accept delayed testimony on hadd without a valid excuse.
The delay must be without any valid reason such as distance from the imam.
2
Identify the underlying rationale
Unjustified delay indicates personal malice (rancor) rather than a desire to uphold Allah's rights.
Initially concealing a sin is encouraged; later testifying suggests a change of motive.
3
Identify the exception
Hadd qadhf is accepted even with delay because it is a right of the servant (haqq al-‘abd).
In qadhf, the punishment vindicates the falsely accused person's honor.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
The statement equates delayed testimony with rancor.
5
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'from rancor' shows that delay without excuse makes testimony suspect, hence not reliable for hudud.
The Hanafi school considers this proof sufficient to reject delayed testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا شهد الشهود بحد متقادم لم يمنعهم عن اقامته [۲۴۷۶ (۳۳) اگر گواہوں نے پرانی حد کی گواہی دی جس کو قائم کرنے سے امام سے دور ہونا اس کو روکتا نہ تھا تو ان کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی مگر خاص طور پر حد قذف میں۔ معاملات میں پرانی گواہی بھی قابل قبول ہے کیونکہ وہ حقوق العباد ہیں۔ لیکن حد اور حقوق اللہ کے بارے میں اگر کوئی عذر نہیں تھا مثلا امام سے اتنا دور نہیں تھا کہ اتنی تاخیر کرنے کی ضرورت ہو پھر بھی گواہی دینے میں بہت تاخیر کی تو یہ گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ ابتدا میں گواہی نہ دینے کی وجہ یہ ہوسکتی ہے کہ مجرم پر پردہ پوشی کرنا چاہتا تھا جس کی حدیث میں ترغیب ہے۔ بعد میں کسی حسد اور بغض کی بنا پر گواہی کے لئے آمادہ ہو گیا تو گواہی اب حسد اور بغض کی بنیاد پر ہے۔ حقوق اللہ کی بنیاد پر نہیں ہے اس لئے ایسی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابی عون قال عمر بن الخطاب ايما رجل شهد على حد لم يكن بحضرته فانما ذلك عن ضغن (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب لا يوجل في الحدودج سابع ص ۲۳۲ نمبر ۱۳۷۶۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دیر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اب کینہ کی وجہ سے گواہی دے رہا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔ البتہ حد قذف چونکہ حقوق العباد میں سے ہے اس لئے وہ تاخیر کے ساتھ بھی مقبول ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حد قذف میں آدمی کو تہمت لگائی جارہی ہے۔
And if the witnesses testify to an old hadd that does not prevent them from establishing it... [2476 (33)] If witnesses give testimony about an old hadd, where their distance from the imam did not prevent them from establishing it, then their testimony is not accepted, except specifically in the case of hadd qadhf. In transactions, old testimony is also acceptable because they are rights of the servants. But regarding hadd and rights of Allah, if there was no excuse—for example, it was not so far from the imam that such delay was necessary—yet they delayed giving testimony greatly, then this testimony is not accepted. The reason for not giving testimony initially could be that they wished to conceal the criminal, which is encouraged in hadith. Later, due to some jealousy and enmity, they became inclined to testify, so the testimony is now based on jealousy and enmity, not on the rights of Allah. Therefore, such testimony is not accepted. (2) There is an athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: Any man who testifies about a hadd that was not in his presence, that is only from rancor.' (a) From this athar it is known that the meaning of delay is that he is now testifying out of malice. Therefore, it is not acceptable. However, hadd qadhf, since it is among the rights of the servants, is accepted even with delay, because in hadd qadhf a person is being accused.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage discusses the acceptance of testimony regarding a hudud punishment when the testimony is delayed. The general rule is that if witnesses delay giving testimony about a hadd without a valid excuse (such as being far from the imam), their testimony is not accepted. The reason is that delaying may indicate that they initially wanted to conceal the sin (which is encouraged) but later, due to personal malice, they come forward. Such testimony is based on enmity, not on upholding Allah's rights. The exception is hadd qadhf (false accusation of zina), because qadhf is a right of the servant (haqq al-‘abd), and delayed testimony for qadhf is accepted. The proof is the statement of ‘Umar ibn al-Khattab. In transactions (mu‘amalat), delayed testimony is also accepted because they are rights of the servants.

Key Terms
حد متقادم (hadd mutaqadim): A hadd offense that occurred long ago.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the hadd has expired by then.
D) Because the imam must be present at the time of the crime.

Key Takeaway
Delayed testimony on hadd is rejected unless it is qadhf, because delay without excuse indicates personal malice rather than upholding Allah's rights.

Ta'zir for Non-Vaginal Intercourse
Ruling on ta'zir for non-vaginal intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on non-vaginal intercourse with a foreign woman and distinguish when hadd applies vs. ta'zir.

Core Idea
Hadd is only for vaginal zina; all other illicit sexual acts incur ta'zir.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position that the fixed punishment (hadd) for zina is reserved exclusively for vaginal penetration. Any other form of illicit sexual contact, such as intercourse between the thighs or other body parts, is a major sin but punishable by ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The passage also cites an athar indicating that even acts like lesbian rubbing are subject to ta'zir of 100 lashes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Determine what the act is: sexual intercourse with a foreign woman (non-mahram) but not in the vagina – e.g., between the thighs or other body parts.
The text specifies 'what is below the private part' (mā dūna al-farj).
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is ta'zir (discretionary punishment), not hadd. Hadd for zina is only for vaginal penetration.
The passage explicitly says 'yujalladu ta'zīran'.
3
Understand the Condition
The key condition is that the act must be with a foreign woman. If the woman were his wife or slave, the act is permissible or has no punishment.
The term 'ajnabiyyah' means a woman prohibited in marriage.
4
Note the Exception
Anal intercourse (dubur) is separate and will be discussed later; it may have its own ruling.
The text says 'wa ammā al-dubur fa-inna al-mas'alah ta'tī ba'dahu'.
5
Apply the Ta'zir
The judge imposes ta'zir, which can include lashes (as in the athar) or other punishment, at discretion.
The athar cited gives 100 lashes for similar acts, but ta'zir is flexible.

Source Text

And whoever has intercourse with a foreign woman in other than the private part is to be given ta'zir. [2477 (34)] If someone has intercourse with a foreign woman in other than the vagina, then ta'zir is given. If he did not have intercourse in the vagina of the foreign woman but in another place, then hadd is not imposed, but ta'zir is given. And the ruling for intercourse in the anus will come later. In an athar: Ibn Shihab said, 'I found our scholars saying about a woman who comes to a woman with rubbing and the like, they are both flogged one hundred lashes each, the active and the passive.' (b) From this athar it is learned that as ta'zir, both are given one hundred lashes each.

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: if a man commits intercourse with a foreign woman (not his wife or slave) in any place other than the vagina (such as between the thighs or other parts), then he is not subject to the hadd punishment for zina, but rather to ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The commentator notes that the ruling for anal intercourse will be discussed later. The passage also cites an athar regarding lesbian acts (sihaq), where both parties are given one hundred lashes as ta'zir. This indicates that similar acts of sexual gratification outside the vagina incur ta'zir, not hadd.

Key Terms
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment administered at the judge's discretion for offenses not subject to fixed hadd.
فرج (farj): The private part, specifically the vagina.
أجنبية (ajnabiyyah): A woman who is not a mahram (i.e., not a wife or close relative one cannot marry).

No Hadd for Intercourse with Son's Slave Girl
Ruling that intercourse with son's or grandson's slave girl incurs no hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding a father's intercourse with his son's slave girl and explain the legal reasoning based on the hadith.

Core Idea
A father faces no hadd for intercourse with his son's slave girl because Islamic law treats the son's property as belonging to the father.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling: a father is exempt from the hadd punishment for zina when he has intercourse with his son's (or grandson's) slave girl, even if he knows it is forbidden. The reasoning rests on a Prophetic hadith that establishes a father's ownership-like right over his son's property. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school applies the concept of constructive ownership to hudud cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the hukm regarding a father who has intercourse with his son's slave girl. The passage states clearly: there is no hadd on him.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father' (Abu Dawood). This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its dalalah is considered qati (clear) in establishing the principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the exemption. The hadith implies that a father has a kind of ownership over his son's property, including slave girls. Thus, intercourse with a son's slave girl is analogous to intercourse with one's own slave girl, for which no hadd is imposed.
The Hanafi school extends this principle to grandsons' slave girls as well.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that the father is subject to hadd because the slave girl is owned by the son, not the father. They base their view on the general rules of zina.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate; both sides have valid evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school due to the strength of the hadith and the principle of istihsan (juristic preference) that considers the father's broad authority over his son's property.
The passage does not specify a later tarjih authority, but the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا حد على من وطئ جارية ولده او ولدولده وان قال علمت انها على حرام [۲۴۷۸] (۳۵) نہیں حد ہے اس آدمی پر جس نے اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے وطی کی ہو یا پوتے کی باندی سے وطی کی ہو اگر چہ وہ کہتا ہو کہ میں جانتا ہوں کہ وہ مجھ پر حرام ہے۔ بیٹے کی باندی یا پوتے کی باندی سے ولی کی اور کہتا ہو کہ مجھے معلوم تھا کہ یہ باندی مجھ پر حرام ہے پھر بھی باپ پر حد نہیں ہے۔ ے اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا آپ کا مال والد کے لئے ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ انت و مالک لوالدك ان اولادکم من اطيب كسبكم فكلوا من كسب اولادکم (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الرجل یا کل من مال ولده ج ثانی ص ۱۴۱ نمبر ۳۵۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹے کی باندی اور پوتے کی باندی میں کچھ اپنی باندی ہونے کا اثر ہے اس لئے اس سے ولی کی تو حد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔
And there is no hadd on one who has intercourse with the slave girl of his son or the son of his son, even if he says, 'I knew that she is forbidden for me.' [2478] (35) There is no hadd on this man who has intercourse with his son's slave girl or his grandson's slave girl, even if he says, 'I know that she is forbidden for me.' If a father has intercourse with his son's or grandson's slave girl and says, 'I knew that this slave girl is forbidden for me,' still there is no hadd on the father. It has passed above that the Prophet said, 'You and your wealth belong to your father.' The hadith is: 'You and your wealth belong to your father. Verily, your children are the best of your earnings, so eat from the earnings of your children.' (c) From this hadith it is known that the son's slave girl and the grandson's slave girl have some effect of being his own slave girl, therefore, intercourse with her does not necessitate hadd.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage provides a special ruling: a father is not subject to the hadd punishment for zina if he has intercourse with his son's or grandson's slave girl. This applies even if he knows it is prohibited for him. The reasoning is based on the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father,' which implies that a father has a kind of ownership or right over his son's property, including slave girls. Consequently, intercourse with a son's slave girl is treated similarly to intercourse with one's own slave girl, for which there is no hadd (only ta'zir if he is unmarried, but here the focus is on hadd). The passage also notes that this principle extends to grandsons' slave girls.

Key Terms
جارية (jariyah): Female slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a father not subject to hadd for intercourse with his son's slave girl?
A) Because it is not considered zina.
B) Because the son has no ownership over the slave girl.
C) Because the father is considered the owner of the son's property.
D) Because the father is not required to follow Islamic law.

Key Takeaway
A father incurs no hadd for intercourse with his son's or grandson's slave girl because the son's property is considered the father's, based on the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father.'

Hadd for Intercourse with Non-Owned Slave Girls
Ruling on hadd for intercourse with non-owned slave girls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hadd for intercourse with a non-owned slave girl and identify the condition that removes the hadd.

Core Idea
Hadd for zina with another's slave girl is dropped if the offender claims ignorance of the prohibition.

This lesson examines a specific ruling on the hadd penalty for intercourse with slave girls that are not one's own. The Hanafi school holds that the punishment depends on the offender's knowledge of the prohibition. If he knew it was haram, hadd applies; if he mistakenly thought it permissible, hadd is warded off. This reflects the broader principle that hudud are averted by doubts (shubuhat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Intercourse with a slave girl belonging to one's father, mother, wife, or (for a male slave) his master.
2
State the default ruling
Hadd of zina is imposed if the offender knows the act is haram.
3
Identify the condition that removes hadd
The offender's claim of ignorance (that he thought it was halal) removes the hadd.
The claim must be plausible; it creates a doubt that averts the punishment.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Hanafi fiqh holds that hudud are warded off by doubts (shubuhat); ignorance of prohibition is a valid doubt.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may impose hadd regardless of ignorance, but the Hanafi position gives weight to the offender's knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا وطئ جارية ابيه او امه او [۲۴۷۹ (۳۶) اگر باپ کی باندی سے ولی کی ، یاماں یا اپنی بیوی کی باندی سے یا غلام نے آقا کی باندی سے ولی کی اور کہا کہ میں جانتا ہوں کہ وہ مجھ پر حرام ہے تو حد لگے گی اور اگر کہا کہ میراگمان تھا کہ وہ میرے لئے حلال ہے تو حد نہیں لگے گی۔
And if he has intercourse with the slave girl of his father or his mother, or [2479 (36)] If he has intercourse with his father's slave girl, or his mother's, or his wife's slave girl, or a slave has intercourse with his master's slave girl, and he says, 'I know that she is forbidden for me,' then hadd will be imposed. But if he says, 'I thought she was permissible for me,' then hadd will not be imposed.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage outlines the ruling for intercourse with slave girls who are not one's own: the slave girl of one's father, mother, wife, or (for a slave) his master's slave girl. In such cases, hadd of zina is imposed if the offender knew the prohibition. If he was ignorant and genuinely believed it was permissible (e.g., due to a misconception), then hadd is not imposed. The distinction is based on whether the element of criminal intent (knowledge of prohibition) is present. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that hudud are warded off by doubts (shubuhat).

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): Male slave.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment for certain crimes (here, zina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is subject to hadd regardless.
B) Hadd is not imposed due to his claim of ignorance.
C) He is only given ta'zir.
D) He is considered to have committed zina but the punishment is reduced.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of prohibition is a condition for hadd in intercourse with non-owned slave girls; ignorance removes the punishment.
