Delayed Testimony in Hudud: General Rule and Exception for Qadhf
Ruling on acceptance of delayed testimony in hudud with proof and exception for qadhf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delayed testimony in hudud, identify the exception for hadd al-qadhf, and explain the rationale and proof.

Core Idea
Delayed testimony in hudud is rejected except for qadhf, as it is presumed spiteful and qadhf involves a personal right.

In Hanafi fiqh, testimony is crucial for establishing hudud punishments. However, if witnesses come forward after the event, their credibility is suspect. This lesson examines the general principle that such testimony is not accepted, and the unique exception for false accusation (qadhf) where the victim's reputation is at stake.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and exception
The passage states: testimony of witnesses who come to the imam after the crime is not accepted, except in hadd al-qadhf.
The exception is clearly stated: 'except in hadd al-qadhf specifically'.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that delayed testimony is motivated by envy and malice, not by the rights of Allah. Qadhf is an exception because it is a right of the servant.
The distinction between rights of Allah and rights of servants is key.
3
Analyze the dalil
The athar from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab indicates that testifying after the fact about a hadd is from spite (ضغن). This supports the presumption of unreliability.
The dalil has zanni thubut and dalala, so it is not absolutely binding but guides the ruling.
4
Evaluate the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position restricts acceptance; the Shafi'i school may accept delayed testimony in some cases. Recognize that this ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.
Practical effect: Hanafi muftis will almost always reject delayed testimony except in qadhf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود بعدهم عن الامام لم تقبل شهادتهم الا في حد القذف خاصة [۲۴۷۷] پر گواہی کے لئے آمادہ ہو گیا تو گواہی اب حسد اور بغض کی بنیاد پر ہے۔ حقوق اللہ کی بنیاد پر نہیں ہے اس لئے ایسی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابی عون قال عمر بن الخطاب ايما رجل شهد على حد لم يكن بحضرته فانما ذلك عن ضغن (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب لا يوجل في الحدودج سابع ص ۲۳۲ نمبر ۱۳۷۶۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دیر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اب کینہ کی وجہ سے گواہی دے رہا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔ البتہ حد قذف چونکہ حقوق العباد میں سے ہے اس لئے وہ تاخیر کے ساتھ بھی مقبول ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حد قذف میں آدمی کو تہمت لگائی جارہی ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت مڑنے فرمایا جس وقت جرم کیا اس وقت گواہی نہ دے بعد میں کسی آدمی پر گواہی دے تو وہ کینہ کی وجہ سے گواہی دے رہا ہے
The book of Hudud: After they [the witnesses] come to the Imam, their testimony is not accepted except in hadd al-qadhf specifically. [2477] He became prepared for testimony, so the testimony is now based on envy and malice, not on the rights of Allah, therefore such testimony is not accepted. (2) There is an athar: From Abu Awn, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: Any man who testifies about a hadd that he did not witness, that is only out of spite.' (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab la yujal fi al-hudud, vol. 7, p. 232, no. 13760) From this athar it is understood that the meaning of delay is that he is now testifying out of malice, so it is not acceptable. However, hadd al-qadhf, because it is from the rights of the servants, is accepted even with delay, because in hadd al-qadhf a person is being accused. Footnote: (a) Hadrat [Umar] said: When the crime was committed, he did not testify; later he testifies against someone, so he is testifying out of malice.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the acceptance of testimony in hudud (fixed punishments). The base ruling states that if witnesses come to the imam (the judge) with testimony after the event, their testimony is not accepted except in cases of hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of adultery/fornication). The author then provides an Urdu commentary explaining the reasoning: such delayed testimony is likely motivated by personal enmity rather than a sense of upholding Allah's rights, so it is rejected. The exception for qadhf is because it involves the rights of individuals (the accused has been slandered). The proof is an athar (narration) from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, who stated that a person who testifies about a hadd he did not witness does so out of spite. This is classified as a weak (zanni) proof, but it supports the principle. The footnote clarifies the meaning of 'spite' as malice.

Key Terms
حد (حدود) (hadd (hudud)): Fixed punishments prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes like zina, qadhf, theft, etc.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (adultery/fornication) against a chaste person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because the imam can always investigate the delay
D) Because qadhf is proven by a single witness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects delayed testimony in hudud except for qadhf, due to the presumption of spite and the personal nature of the right in qadhf.

Ta'zir for Intercourse Below the Private Part
Ruling on punishment for non-vaginal intercourse with a non-mahram woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why intercourse below the private part with a non-mahram woman incurs ta'zir rather than hadd and cite the proof from the athar.

Core Idea
Only vaginal penetration triggers hadd; all other sexual acts with non-mahram incur discretionary ta'zir.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a man who has intercourse with a woman who is not his wife, but not in the vagina. The text clearly distinguishes this from zina, stating that such an act does not incur the fixed punishment (hadd) but rather a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) left to the judge. The author also provides a proof from an athar to support that ta'zir can be severe.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that if a man has intercourse with a foreign woman below the private part (i.e., not vaginal), he is given ta'zir. The act is haram, but the punishment is discretionary.
The ruling is clearly stated in the opening sentence: 'عُزّر'.
2
Understand the exclusion of hadd
Hadd of zina is only applied for vaginal penetration. The author explicitly notes that hadd is not imposed in this case, only ta'zir.
This is a key Hanafi position: hadd is restricted to actual vaginal intercourse.
3
Examine the proof cited
The author cites an athar from Ibn Shihab about women who rub genitals (sahaq) receiving 100 lashes as ta'zir, analogizing to the case of non-vaginal intercourse.
The athar shows that ta'zir can be severe (100 lashes), even though the Hanafi limit for ta'zir is typically lower.
4
Note the distinction from anal intercourse
The text postpones discussion of anal intercourse, indicating it may have a different ruling.
This reflects the Hanafi view that anal intercourse is also not zina but a separate issue to be discussed later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن وطئ امرأة اجنبية فى ما دون الفرج عُزّر [ ۲۴۷۸] (۳۴) کسی نے اجتنبیہ عورت سے ولی کی فرج کے علاوہ میں تو تعزیر کی جائے گی۔ اجمیہ عورت کی شرم گاہ میں ولی نہیں کی بلکہ اور جگہ ولی کی تو حد تو نہیں لگے گی البتہ تعزیر ہوگی۔ اور دبر میں وطی کی تو اس کا مسئلہ آگے آرہا ہے اثر میں ہے۔ اخبرنی ابن شهاب قال ادرکت علماء نا يقولون في المرأة تأتى المرأة بالرفعة واشباهها تجلدان مئة مئة الفاعلة والمفعولة بها (ب) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب السحاقه ج سابع ص۳۳۴ نمبر ۱۳۳۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ تعزیر کے طور پر دونوں کو سوسو کوڑے لگیں گے۔ حاشیہ : (ب) این شہاب فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے علماء کو یہ کہتے ہوئے پایا کہ عورت عورت کے ساتھ شرمگاہ رگڑایا اس طرح کی بات کی تو دونوں کو سوسوکوڑے لگائے ، اور کرنے والی کو اور کرانے والی کو بھی
And whoever has intercourse with a foreign woman below the private part (i.e., not vaginal) is given ta'zir. [2478] (34) If someone has intercourse with a foreign woman in other than the vagina, then ta'zir will be given. If he did not have intercourse in the private part of the foreign woman but elsewhere, then hadd is not imposed but ta'zir is. And for anal intercourse, the issue will come later. There is an athar: Ibn Shihab informed me, he said: I found our scholars saying regarding a woman who comes to a woman by rubbing and similar acts, both are flogged one hundred lashes each, the active and the passive. (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-sahaq, vol. 7, p. 334, no. 13383) From this athar it is understood that both are given one hundred lashes as ta'zir. Footnote: (b) Ibn Shihab says: I found the scholars saying that if a woman rubs her private part with another woman or does similar things, both are flogged one hundred lashes, the doer and the one on whom it is done.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage deals with a ruling where a man has intercourse with a non-mahram woman (ajnabiyyah) but not in the vagina (e.g., between thighs or other parts). The author states that such an act does not incur the hadd penalty for zina (which requires vaginal penetration), but rather ta'zir (a discretionary punishment). The commentary notes that if the intercourse is in the anus (dubr), it will be discussed later. The proof cited is an athar from Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, who reports that scholars held that if women engage in sapphic acts (sahaq, i.e., rubbing genitals), both are flogged one hundred lashes as ta'zir. This shows that ta'zir can be severe (100 lashes) for such immoral acts. The footnote repeats this. The ruling is from the Hanafi school; ta'zir is for acts that are sinful but not subject to a fixed hadd.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment given by the judge for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd.
فرج (farj): The private part; in context, specifically the vagina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) No punishment because it is not zina

Key Takeaway

No Hadd for Father with Son's Slave-Girl
Ruling exempting a father from hadd for intercourse with his son's slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father is exempt from hadd for intercourse with his son's slave-girl and explain the role of shubhah derived from the hadith.

Core Idea
A father's proprietary connection to his son's property creates a legal doubt (shubhah) that drops the hadd punishment.

In this passage, the author addresses a specific case in the law of hudud: a father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl. Despite the act being sinful and the father knowing it, the hadd punishment is not applied. The reason is a shubhah (legal doubt) arising from the father's property rights over his son's possessions, based on a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a father having intercourse with his son's or grandson's slave-girl. The ruling: no hadd applies, even if the father knew it was forbidden.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'You and your wealth belong to your father' (Sunan Abi Dawud).
This is a hadith ahad, thus zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith indicates that the father has a proprietary interest in the son's property. This interest creates a shubhah (legal doubt) that the father had some right over the slave-girl, thereby averting the hadd.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school may impose hadd because there is no direct ownership or marriage, and they require a clear legal right to make intercourse permissible.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith and the broad application of shubhah to drop hadd, considering the father's property connection sufficient doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا حد على من وطئ جارية ولده او ولدولده وان قال علمت انها على حرام [۲۴۷۹ (۳۵) نہیں حد ہے اس آدمی پر جس نے اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے وطی کی ہو یا پوتے کی باندی سے وطی کی ہو اگر چہ وہ کہتا ہو کہ میں جانتا ہوں کہ وہ مجھ پر حرام ہے۔ بیٹے کی باندی یا پوتے کی باندی سے ولی کی اور کہتا ہو کہ مجھے معلوم تھا کہ یہ باندی مجھ پر حرام ہے پھر بھی باپ پر حد نہیں ہے۔ ے اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا آپ کا مال والد کے لئے ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ انت و مالک لوالدک ان اولادکم من اطيب كسبكم فكلوا من كسب اولادکم (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب الرجل یا کل من مال ولده ج ثانی ص ۱۴۱ نمبر ۳۵۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹے کی باندی اور پوتے کی باندی میں کچھ اپنی باندی ہونے کا اثر ہے اس لئے اس سے ولی کی تو حد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (ج) تم اور تمہارا مال تمہارے والد کے لئے ہے۔ اور تمہاری اولاد تمہاری بہترین کمائی ہے اس لئے اپنی اولاد کی کمائی سے کھاؤ۔
And there is no hadd on one who has intercourse with the slave-girl of his son or the slave-girl of his grandson, even if he says 'I knew it was forbidden for me.' [2479] (35) There is no hadd on this man who had intercourse with his son's slave-girl or his grandson's slave-girl, even though he says he knew it was forbidden for him. If he had intercourse with his son's or grandson's slave-girl and says he knew it was forbidden, still there is no hadd on the father. It has passed above that he (the Prophet) said: 'You and your wealth are for your father.' The hadith is: 'You and your wealth belong to your father; your children are among the best of your earnings, so eat from the earnings of your children.' (c) (Abu Dawud, Bab al-rajul ya'kulu min mal waladihi, vol. 2, p. 141, no. 3530) From this hadith it is understood that the son's slave-girl and the grandson's slave-girl have some effect of being one's own slave-girl, therefore hadd is not necessary. Footnote: (c) You and your wealth are for your father, and your children are the best of your earnings, so eat from your children's earnings.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a man has intercourse with a slave-girl owned by his son or grandson. The ruling states that no hadd punishment (for zina) applies to him, even if he was aware that the woman was forbidden to him (since she is owned by his son, and a father cannot marry his son's slave-girl, but the property relation creates a shubhah (semblance of right). The author cites the well-known hadith: 'You and your wealth belong to your father' and 'Your children are the best of your earnings.' Based on this, the father has a kind of ownership right over his son's property, which creates a shubhah (legal doubt) that prevents the hadd. The Urdu commentary explains that because of this hadith, the son's slave-girl is treated as if she were partly the father's own, thus the hadd of zina is not imposed. The footnote repeats the hadith.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt or semblance of right that averts the hadd punishment.
جارية (jariyah): A female slave (bondsmaid).
حد (hadd): A fixed punitive measure prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes (e.g., zina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

The father is exempt from hadd for intercourse with his son's slave-girl due to the shubhah created by his proprietary interest, as established by the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father.'

Hadd for Intercourse with Relatives' Slave-Girls: Knowledge of Prohibition
Ruling on hadd for intercourse with certain relatives' slave-girls depending on knowledge of prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for intercourse with a relative's slave-girl and explain how knowledge of the prohibition affects the penalty.

Core Idea
Hadd is dropped when doubt exists; knowledge of prohibition triggers the full penalty.

This passage addresses a specific scenario where a man has intercourse with a slave-girl belonging to his father, mother, wife, or (if he is a slave) his master. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the perpetrator's knowledge: if he knew it was forbidden, hadd (flogging or stoning) applies; if he thought it was permissible due to frequent interaction, hadd is dropped due to shubhah (doubt). The passage reconciles conflicting evidence from hadith and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its inherent ruling
The act is intercourse with a slave-girl of certain relatives (father, mother, wife, master). This is inherently haram (forbidden) because the slave-girl is not owned by the perpetrator.
2
Identify the condition of knowledge
The text presents two scenarios: if the perpetrator says 'I knew it was haram,' hadd is imposed; if he says 'I thought it was halal,' hadd is not imposed. Knowledge of prohibition is thus a necessary condition for hadd.
The basis for thinking it halal is the close daily interaction with the relative, which may create a wrong assumption of permissibility.
3
Examine the primary proof
The hadith from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir states: for a man who comes to his wife's slave-girl, if she made her permissible, he is flogged 100; if not, he is stoned. This indicates severe punishment when permission is not given, which implies knowledge of prohibition.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but it is used as evidence.
4
See how conflicting reports are reconciled
Another athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i says only ta'zir (not hadd) for such acts. The Hanafi school reconciles by applying the hadith to cases where the perpetrator knows the prohibition, and Ibrahim's athar to cases where he is ignorant.
This reconciliation shows the principle that shubhah (doubt) averts hadd.
5
Note the practical consequence
In practice, a judge must investigate the perpetrator's state of knowledge. If he claims ignorance and there is a plausible basis for doubt (e.g., frequent interaction), hadd is averted, but ta'zir (discretionary punishment) may still be applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا وطئ جارية ابيه او امه او زوجته او وطئ العبد جارية مولاه وقال علمت انها على حرام حُدَّ وان قال ظننت انها تحل لى لم يُحدَّ [۳۷۲۴۸۰) باپ، ماں، بیوی آقا وغیرہ کے ساتھ رات دن کھانا پینا ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ گمان ہو سکتا ہے کہ ان کی باندی میرے لئے حلال ہو اس لئے ولی کرنے والے کو یہ گمان ہو کہ یہ میرے لئے حلال ہے اور حلال سمجھ کر دلی کر لیا تو حد نہیں لگے گی۔ ملکیت کے شبہ کی وجہ سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ لیکن اگر مسئلہ معلوم تھا کہ ان لوگوں کی باندیاں میرے لئے حلال نہیں پھر بھی ولی کر لی تو حد لگے گی ۔ کیونکہ حقیقت میں بھی حلال نہیں تھیں اور علم بھی تھا کہ حلال نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے حرمت میں کوئی شبہ نہیں رہا اس لئے حد لگے گی۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن النعمان بن بشير عن النبي عله انه قال في الرجل يأتى جارية امرأته قال ان كانت احلتها له جلد مائة وان لم تكن احلتها له رجمته (الف) (سن للبیهقی ، باب ماجاء فیمن اتی جاریہ امر تتدرج عنا من ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۱۷۰۶۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی کی باندی سے وطی کرنے والے کو رجم کیا جائے گا۔ اور اسی اثر میں باپ، ماں، بیوی اور آقا کی باندیاں داخل ہیں اس لئے ہم ان کو اس صورت پر محمول کرتے ہیں جبکہ مسئلہ معلوم ہو۔ اور دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال يعزر ولا يحد (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الرجل يصيب وليدة امرأته ج سابع ص ۱۳۲۴ نمبر ۱۳۴۲۲ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حد نہیں لگے گی بلکہ تعزیر ہوگی۔ اس لئے اس اثر کو اس صورت پر محمول کریں گے کہ وطی کرنے والے کو معلوم نہیں تھا کہ وہ باندی میرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ ماں کی باندی کے سلسلے میں یہ اثر ہے۔ سالت حمادا والحكم عن الرجل يقع على جارية امه قالا عليه الحد وعن الحسن قال ليس عليه الحد (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۸۲ فی الرجل یا تی جاریہ امر ج خامس ص ۵۱۴ نمبر ۲۸۵۶۳) حاشیہ : (الف) حضور سے منقول ہے کہ کوئی آدمی بیوی کی باندی سے وطی کرے تو فرمایا اگر بیوی نے حلال کیا ہو تو سو کوڑے اور اگر حلانہ کیا ہو تو اس کور حجم کرے۔ حاشیه : (ب) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا تعزیر کی جائے اور حد نہیں لگے گی (ج) حضرت حکم نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی بیوی کی باندی سے وطی کرے تو اس پر حد ہے۔ اور حضرت حسن نے فرمایا اس پر حد نہیں ہے
And if one has intercourse with the slave-girl of his father, or his mother, or his wife, or a slave has intercourse with the slave-girl of his master, and he says 'I knew it was forbidden for me,' he is subject to hadd; and if he says 'I thought it was permissible for me,' he is not subject to hadd. [372480] With father, mother, wife, master etc., eating and drinking goes on day and night, so it is possible that one may think their slave-girl is permissible for him. Therefore, if the one having intercourse has the assumption that it is permissible for him and does it thinking it is halal, then hadd will not be imposed. Due to the doubt of ownership, hadd will be dropped. But if he knew the ruling that these people's slave-girls are not permissible for him, yet he still had intercourse, then hadd will be imposed, because in reality they were not halal and he knew they were not halal, so there remains no doubt in the prohibition, therefore hadd will be imposed. There is a hadith: From al-Nu'man ibn Bashir from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said regarding a man who comes to his wife's slave-girl: 'If she (the wife) has made her permissible for him, he is flogged one hundred; if she has not made her permissible for him, he is stoned.' (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma ja'a fi man ata jariyat imra'atihi, vol. 8, p. 216, no. 17068) From this hadith it is understood that the one who has intercourse with his wife's slave-girl will be stoned. And in this same athar, the slave-girls of father, mother, wife, and master are included, so we apply them to the case when the ruling is known. And in another athar: From Ibrahim, he said: 'He is given ta'zir and not hadd.' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-rajul yusib walidata imra'atihi, vol. 7, p. 1324, no. 13422) In this athar, it says that hadd is not imposed, rather ta'zir is. So we apply this athar to the case where the one having intercourse did not know that the slave-girl was not permissible for him. Regarding the mother's slave-girl, there is this athar: I asked Hammad and al-Hakam about a man who has intercourse with his mother's slave-girl; they both said: 'He is subject to hadd.' And from al-Hasan: 'He is not subject to hadd.' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Fi al-rajul ya'ti jariyata imra'atihi, vol. 5, p. 514, no. 28563) Footnote: (a) It is narrated from the Prophet that if a man has intercourse with his wife's slave-girl, if the wife made her permissible, then one hundred lashes; if she did not make her permissible, then stoning. (b) Ibrahim said: Ta'zir is given and not hadd. (c) Al-Hakam said: If a man has intercourse with his wife's slave-girl, he is subject to hadd. And al-Hasan said: He is not subject to hadd.

Commentary
This passage covers a complex ruling: the hadd penalty for intercourse with the slave-girl of one's father, mother, wife, or (for a slave) his master's slave-girl depends on the perpetrator's knowledge of the prohibition. The author distinguishes two scenarios: if the person thought it was halal (due to frequent interaction suggesting indirect ownership), no hadd; if he knew it was haram, hadd is imposed. The proof is a hadith from al-Nu'man ibn Bashir that for a wife's slave-girl, if the wife gave permission, flogging (100 lashes), otherwise stoning. This indicates severe punishment when the prohibition is known. The ruling is reconciled with another athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i who said only ta'zir, by applying the latter to cases of ignorance. The passage also notes a difference of opinion among early scholars (Hammad, al-Hakam, al-Hasan) regarding the mother's slave-girl. The Hanafi position, as presented, is that knowledge of the prohibition triggers hadd; ignorance drops it. The footnotes summarize the key athar.

Key Terms
ظن (zann): A belief or assumption; here it means thinking something is permissible, which creates shubhah.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for zina committed by a married person.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion, less than hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Knowledge of prohibition is decisive for hadd; doubt (shubhah) from close interaction drops the fixed penalty but the act remains sinful.

Hadd for Intercourse with Relatives' Slave Girls
Ruling on hadd for wat' with relative's slave girl conditioned on knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for intercourse with a relative's slave girl and apply the condition of knowledge (shubha) to determine whether hadd or ta'zir applies.

Core Idea
Hadd is dropped when shubha of permissibility exists due to close social interaction.

This passage from the Book of Hadd addresses a specific scenario: a man who has intercourse with a slave girl belonging to his close relatives (wife, father, mother, master). The Hanafi school introduces a crucial nuance — the presence of a doubt (shubha) arising from the frequent contact that can lead the man to mistakenly believe the slave girl is permissible for him. The ruling hinges on whether he knew the prohibition or not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling categories
The act is sexual intercourse (wat') with a slave girl belonging to a close relative (wife, father, mother, master). The two possible outcomes are hadd (prescribed punishment) or ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
The text mentions both 'hadd' and 'ta'zir' as possible outcomes.
2
Locate the condition
The single determining factor is the perpetrator's knowledge of the prohibition. If he knew it was forbidden and still did it, hadd applies. If he believed it was permissible due to a plausible doubt, hadd is dropped and ta'zir is applied.
The Urdu commentary explains that frequent eating/drinking together creates a doubt of ownership.
3
Analyze the evidence
The author cites a hadith from Nu'man bin Bashir: stoning for wife's slave girl without permission. Another effect from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: only ta'zir. The Hanafis reconcile these by conditioning on knowledge.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi; the effect from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Reconcile the proofs
The hadith is interpreted as applying when the man knew the prohibition; the effect is taken as the default case of ignorance. The two are not contradictory but address different scenarios.
This is a classic Hanafi method of combining seemingly conflicting evidences.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, ask: Did the man know the ruling that this slave girl is forbidden? If yes, hadd. If no (plausible doubt due to close association), ta'zir.
The mother's slave girl is explicitly discussed: Hammad and al-Hakam said hadd, al-Hasan said no hadd. The Hanafi position aligns with Hammad/al-Hakam when knowledge is present.

Book of Hadd. He or the slave who had intercourse with his master's slave girl and said 'I knew it was forbidden' is punished with hadd, but if he said 'I thought it was permissible for me' he is not punished with hadd. And whoever has intercourse with his brother's or uncle's slave girl and said 'I thought it was permissible' is punished with hadd. [Commentary:] With father, mother, wife, master, etc., eating and drinking happens day and night, so there can be a thought that their slave girl is permissible for me. So if the one who had intercourse thought it was permissible and did it thinking it was halal, then hadd is not applied. Due to doubt of ownership, hadd is dropped. But if he knew the ruling that those people's slave girls are not permissible for him, yet he still had intercourse, then hadd is applied. Because in reality they were not halal and he also knew they were not halal, so there remains no doubt about prohibition, so hadd is applied. Hadith: From Nu'man bin Bashir from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said regarding a man who comes to his wife's slave girl: If she permitted him, he receives a hundred lashes, and if she did not permit him, he is stoned. This hadith indicates that one who has intercourse with his wife's slave girl is stoned. And similarly, the slave girls of father, mother, wife, and master are included. So we interpret these cases as when the ruling is known. And in another effect: From Ibrahim, he said: He is given ta'zir and not hadd. This effect says that hadd is not applied but rather ta'zir. So we interpret this effect as referring to the case when the one who had intercourse did not know that that slave girl was not permissible for him. Regarding the mother's slave girl, there is this effect: I asked Hammad and al-Hakam about a man who has intercourse with his mother's slave girl; they said: He is subject to hadd. And from al-Hasan, he said: He is not subject to hadd.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Hadd presents the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse (wat') with slave girls belonging to close relatives: wife, father, mother, and master. The key principle is that hadd (the prescribed punishment for zina) is applied only if the perpetrator had knowledge of the prohibition. If he had a genuine doubt (shubha) about permissibility due to frequent social interaction (eating/drinking together), then the hadd is dropped because of the doubt of ownership. The author first states the ruling: if he says 'I knew it was forbidden' (علمت انها على حرام), then hadd is applied; if he says 'I thought it was permissible' (ظننت انها تحل لي), then no hadd. The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning: with father, mother, wife, and master, constant daily interaction can create a mistaken belief that their slave girls are permissible. However, if the person knows the Islamic ruling that such slave girls are not permissible, then no doubt remains and hadd applies. The author then provides evidence: a hadith from al-Bayhaqi narrated by Nu'man bin Bashir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled: 'If the wife permitted him to have intercourse with her slave girl, then 100 lashes; if she did not permit, then stoning.' The author reconciles this with the earlier ruling by conditioning on knowledge: the stoning applies only when the man knows the prohibition. Another effect from Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i) states: 'He is given ta'zir and not hadd.' The author interprets this as referring to the case of ignorance. For the mother's slave girl, there is a difference: Hammad and al-Hakam said hadd, while al-Hasan said no hadd. The Hanafi position, as presented, favors hadd when the ruling is known, and no hadd when there is doubt. Thus, the passage establishes the nuance of shubha in hadd cases.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): The fixed, prescribed punishment for certain crimes like zina, theft, etc. In this passage, it specifically refers to the punishment for unlawful intercourse.
تعزير (ta'zir): A discretionary punishment determined by the judge, less than hadd, for crimes that do not have a fixed punishment or where hadd conditions are not met.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd. In this context, the doubt arises from frequent social interaction leading to a mistaken belief of permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to this passage, when does a man who has intercourse with his wife's slave girl receive the hadd punishment?
A) Always, regardless of his knowledge
B) Only if he knew the slave girl was forbidden to him
C) Only if his wife permitted it
D) Never; he only receives ta'zir

Key Takeaway
The application of hadd for zina with a relative's slave girl depends on the perpetrator's knowledge of the prohibition; shubha arising from close association can drop the hadd to ta'zir.

Hadd for Intercourse with Brother's or Uncle's Slave Girl
Ruling on intercourse with brother's or uncle's slave girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the credibility of shubha (doubt) in hudud depends on the frequency of social interaction, and state the ruling for intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave girl.

Core Idea
Lack of daily interaction with a brother or uncle means no genuine doubt — hadd applies even if the person claims ignorance.

This passage addresses a specific hudud case: intercourse with a slave girl belonging to a brother or uncle. Unlike the earlier scenario with the master's slave girl, where constant daily interaction created a plausible doubt (shubha), here the relationship is more distant. The author argues that such a claim of ignorance is not credible, so the hadd penalty is applied. The ruling is supported by qiyas (analogy) to a report from al-Thawri concerning a slave and his master's wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is intercourse (wati’) with a brother’s or uncle’s slave girl. The ruling is that the hadd (fixed penalty for zina) is wajib (obligatory) upon the man.
The same ruling applies to both brother and uncle.
2
Examine the claimed doubt
The person claims he thought the slave girl was permissible (halal) for him. In Hanafi law, a genuine shubha can drop the hadd. Here, the author determines whether this claim is credible.
Shubha typically arises from close daily interaction, such as between a master and his slave girl.
3
Analyze why the doubt is rejected
The text states that with a brother or uncle, there is not the same level of eating and drinking (i.e., social interaction) as with a direct master or close family. Therefore, the claim of ignorance is not plausible; the person should have known that his brother’s/uncle’s slave girl is not permissible for him.
This principle of evaluating the credibility of shubha based on social customs is a key feature of Hanafi fiqh.
4
Follow the qiyas argument
The author draws an analogy: just as a slave who has intercourse with his master’s wife incurs hadd on the woman (based on a report from al-Thawri), similarly, intercourse with a brother’s or uncle’s slave girl incurs hadd. The illa (effective cause) is that in both cases, the woman is not the man’s own property and there is no frequent interaction to create a legitimate doubt.
The qiyas is clear (jali) because the illa is directly observable from the social relationship.
5
Note the ikhtilaf (difference of opinion)
The footnotes mention that al-Hasan al-Basri held that no hadd is applied (only ta’zir), while al-Hakam and others said hadd is applied. The Hanafi school adopts the view of al-Hakam and al-Thawri, ruling that hadd is wajib.
This shows that even within early Islam, there was disagreement on the role of shubha in hudud.

۲۴۸۰] (۳۷) کسی نے بھائی کی باندی سے ولی کی یا چچا کی باندی سے اور کہا کہ میں نے گمان کیا کہ وہ حلال ہے تب بھی حد لگے گی۔ بھائی اور چچا کے ساتھ اتنا کھانا پینا نہیں ہوتا اور نہ آدمی ان کا مال اپنا مال سمجھتا ہے اس لئے یہ گمان بھی ہو کہ ان کی باندیاں میرے لئے حلال ہیں تب بھی حد لگے گی۔
اثر میں ہے کہ غلام نے آقا کی بیوی سے ولی کی تو بیوی کو حد لگے گی اسی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے بھائی اور چچا کی باندی سے ولی کی پھر بھی حد لگے گی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن الثورى فى العبد یزنی بامرأة سيده فقال يقام عليها الحد (د) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب المرأة تزنی
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور سے منقول ہے کہ کوئی آدمی بیوی کی باندی سے وطی کرے تو فرمایا اگر بیوی نے حلال کیا ہو تو سو کوڑے اور اگر حلانہ کیا ہو تو اس کور حجم کرے۔ حاشیه : (ب) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا تعزیر کی جائے اور حد نہیں لگے گی (ج) حضرت حکم نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی بیوی کی باندی سے وطی کرے تو اس پر حد ہے۔ اور حضرت حسن نے فرمایا اس پر حد نہیں ہے (د) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا غلام اپنے سید کی بیوی سے زنا کرے تو اس پر حد قائم کی جائے گی۔
[37] Someone who has intercourse with his brother's or uncle's slave girl and said 'I thought it was permissible' – still hadd is applied. With a brother or uncle, there is not as much eating and drinking, nor does a person consider their property as his own, so even if he thought their slave girls were permissible for him, still hadd is applied. There is a report that a slave had intercourse with his master's wife – the wife is subjected to hadd. By analogy, for intercourse with brother's or uncle's slave girl, hadd is also applied. There is a report: From al-Thawri regarding a slave who commits zina with his master's wife – he said: the hadd is established against her. Footnotes: (a) The Prophet is reported to have said: if a man has intercourse with his wife's slave girl, if the wife permitted, 100 lashes; if not, stoning. (b) Ibrahim said: ta'zir is applied, not hadd. (c) al-Hakam said: hadd; al-Hasan said: no hadd. (d) al-Thawri said: if a slave commits zina with his master's wife, hadd is established against her.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage addresses the specific case of intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave girl. Unlike the close relatives (wife, parents, master) who share daily meals and living, a brother or uncle does not have such frequent interaction. Therefore, there is no plausible doubt (shubha) that their slave girls are permissible. Even if the perpetrator claims he thought it was halal, hadd is applied because the doubt is not genuine. The author provides a qiyas (analogy): just as a slave who has intercourse with his master's wife incurs hadd on the woman (based on the report of al-Thawri), similarly, intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave girl incurs hadd. The footnotes reiterate the earlier sources: the Prophet's hadith about the wife's slave girl, Ibrahim's view of ta'zir, the difference between al-Hakam and al-Hasan, and al-Thawri's report. The key point is that the frequency of social interaction determines whether a claim of ignorance is credible.

Key Terms
حدّ (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by the Quran or Sunnah for specific crimes (e.g., zina).
شبهة (shubha): A plausible doubt or ambiguity that can avert the hadd penalty.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a common effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi ruling impose hadd for intercourse with a brother's or uncle's slave girl even if the person claims he thought it was permissible?
A) Because a brother or uncle is a close relative
B) Because there is no frequent social interaction to create a genuine doubt
C) Because the Quran explicitly says so
D) Because the person is lying

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hudud, the credibility of a claim of ignorance depends on the objective frequency of social interaction; without it, hadd is applied.

No Hadd for Mistaken Intercourse on Wedding Night
Ruling with proof for dropping hadd due to shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd and mahr when a man has intercourse with a woman mistakenly sent as his wife on the wedding night, and explain the two shubha reasons that drop the hadd.

Core Idea
Two doubts on the wedding night drop the hadd: ignorance of identity and women's testimony.

What happens when a groom is deceived on his wedding night and sleeps with the wrong woman? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: the man is not liable for the severe punishment of zina (hadd), but he must pay a compensatory dower (mahr). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling, grounded in the principle that penalties are lifted by doubt (shubha). The passage draws on incidents from the Companions to illustrate the strength of this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
First, understand the case: a groom is presented with a woman other than his wife on the wedding night, and the attending women confirm she is his wife. He has intercourse. The ruling: no hadd, but wajib to pay mahr (aqr).
The ruling is about hadd and financial compensation, not about the validity of the marriage.
2
Analyze the two shubha elements
The text mentions two reasons for dropping hadd: (1) it was the first night, so the groom did not recognize his wife; (2) multiple women testified that she was his wife, creating a strong presumption. Together, these constitute shubha.
Shubha is doubt that prevents the application of hudud.
3
Examine the proofs from the Salaf
The author cites two athar: (a) Ali (ra) did not impose hadd when a woman claimed a man was her husband; (b) Ibrahim al-Nakha'i stated that if a woman's claim of marriage were true, no hadd would apply. The author then uses qiyas: if one woman's claim drops hadd, then multiple women's testimony does so a fortiori.
These athar are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Understand the financial obligation
Even though hadd is dropped, the man must pay mahr (called 'aqr' or mahr al-wat' bi al-shubha) to the woman because intercourse occurred under a semblance of right. This is wajib.
The mahr is the same as what would be given to a woman of similar status.

شب زفاف میں شوہر کے پاس کسی عورت کو بھیج دیا اور عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ تیری بیوی ہے۔ پس اس نے اس سے ولی کی تو اس پر حد نہیں ہے اور شوہر پر مہر ہوگا۔
ی پہلی رات تھی۔ ابھی تک بیوی کو دیکھا نہیں تھا۔ عورتوں نے اصلی بیوی کے علاوہ کسی غیر عورت کو شوہر کے پاس بھیج دیا اور لوگوں نے یہ بھی کہا کہ یہ تیری بیوی ہے۔ اس نے اس سے وطی کر لی۔ بعد میں پتا چلا کہ وہ اس کی بیوی نہیں ہے تو اس مرد پر حد نہیں ہوگی۔ البتہ چونکہ ولی بالشبہ کی ہے اس لئے عقر لازم ہوگا جس کو ولی بالشبہ کا مہر کہتے ہیں۔ شوہر یہاں دو اعتبار سے معذور ہے۔ ایک تو یہ کہ ابھی تک پہچانتا ہی نہیں ہے کہ میری بیوی کون ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ پہلی رات ہے اس لئے اس عذر کی بنا پر حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ عورتوں نے بھی گواہی دی کہ یہ تیری بیوی ہے جس سے بیوی ہونے کا گمان غالب ہو گیا۔ اس لئے ان دونوں شبیہوں کی وجہ سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ بیوی کہہ دے کہ یہ میرا شوہر ہے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ یہاں تو بہت سی عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ تیری بیوی ہے اس لئے بدرجہ اولی حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اثر یہ ہے۔ یحیی بن ابی الهيثم عن ابيه عن جده انه شهد عليا واتى برجل وامرأة وجدا في خرب مراد فاتى بهما على فقال بنت عمى وربيبتي في حجرى فجعل اصحابه يقولون قولى زوجى فقالت هو زوجي فقال على خذ بيد امرأتک ۔ دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔عن ابراهيم في المرأة توخذ مع الرجل فتقول تزوجنى فقال ابراهيم لو كان هذا حقا ما كان على زان حد (ب) مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ۱۳۹ فی الرجل يوجد مع المرأة فتقول زوجي ج خامس ص ۵۴۵ نمبر ۲۸۸۷۵/۲۸۸۷۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کہے کہ میرا شوہر ہے تو اس سے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ تو بہت عورتوں نے کہا تو بدرجہ اولی صد ساقط ہوگی۔ اور چونکہ ولی بالشبہ ہوئی ہے اس لئے
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی کے پاس ایک مرد اور ایک عورت لائے گئے جو خراب مراد میں پکڑے گئے تھے ان کو حضرت علی کے پاس لائے گئے ۔ مرد کہنے لگا یہ میرے چچا کی بیٹی ہے اور میری گود میں پالی ہوئی ہے۔ تو مرد کے ساتھ دوست کہنے لگے کہ کہو یہ میرا شوہر ہے تو عورت نے کہا یہ میرا شوہر ہے۔ تو حضرت علیؓ نے فرمایا اپنی بیوی کا ہاتھ پکڑ لو یعنی حد نہیں لگائی۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا کوئی عورت مرد کے ساتھ زنا میں پکڑی جائے پس وہ کہے کہ مجھ سے شادی کی ہے۔ پس حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا اگر یہ بات سچ ہو تو ایسے زانی پر حد نہیں ہوگی۔
[38] And whoever is brought a woman other than his wife on his wedding night, and the women say 'She is your wife', and he has intercourse with her, then no hadd upon him, and he must pay the mahr. On the wedding night, a woman was sent to the husband and the women said: 'This is your wife.' So he had intercourse with her. Then no hadd is upon him, and he must pay the mahr. It was the first night; he had not yet seen his wife. The women sent another woman besides the real wife to the husband, and people also said: 'This is your wife.' He had intercourse with her. Later it became known that she was not his wife. So no hadd is upon that man. However, because the intercourse was with a doubt (shubha), 'aqr (compensatory mahr) is obligatory, which is called mahr al-wat' bi al-shubha. The husband is excused from two aspects: first, he did not yet know who his wife was because it was the first night, so due to this excuse, hadd is dropped. Second, the women testified that this is your wife, which made the belief that she was his wife dominant. So due to these two doubts, hadd is dropped. (2) There is a report that if the wife says 'This is my husband', then hadd is dropped. Here many women said 'This is your wife', so a fortiori hadd is dropped. The report: Yahya ibn Abi al-Haytham from his father from his grandfather that he witnessed Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when a man and woman were brought who were found in Khurrib Murad. They were brought to Ali. The man said: 'She is my cousin and my foster child in my lap.' Then his companions started saying (to the woman): 'Say: he is my husband.' So she said: 'He is my husband.' Then Ali said: 'Take your wife's hand.' (i.e., no hadd). Another report: From Ibrahim: If a woman is found with a man and she says 'He married me', then Ibrahim said: 'If this were true, no hadd would be on the fornicator.' [Footnotes: (a) Ali's incident: (b) Ibrahim's saying.]
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific scenario: on the wedding night, the groom is presented with a woman other than his actual wife, and the women (family/friends) deceive him by saying 'This is your wife.' He has intercourse with her, believing she is his wife. Subsequently, the truth emerges. The ruling is that no hadd (prescribed punishment for zina) applies to the man, but he must pay a mahr (dower), specifically the 'mahr al-wat' bi al-shubha' (dower for intercourse under doubt). The reasoning is twofold: First, since it is the first night, the groom does not yet recognize his wife, so he has a valid excuse. Second, multiple women testified that she was his wife, creating a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that she is indeed his wife. These two elements constitute shubha (doubt) that prevents the application of hadd. The author then provides supporting evidence from the practice of the Companions. In one incident, Ali (ra) did not apply hadd when a woman said 'He is my husband' to a man found with her. Similarly, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said that if a woman claims marriage, no hadd is imposed if it could be true. By analogy, when many women confirm the relationship, it is even more compelling. Thus, the hadd is dropped due to shubha, but the financial obligation of mahr remains because the intercourse was not with a lawful wife.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A doubt that prevents the application of hadd. Here, the husband's ignorance of the woman's identity and the women's testimony constitute shubha.
مهر (mahr): The dower paid to a woman upon marriage. In this context, 'mahr al-wat' bi al-shubha' is a compensatory payment for intercourse under a mistaken belief of marriage, equivalent to the mahr of a woman in that situation.
عقر (aqr): Synonym for mahr in this context: the financial compensation for intercourse under a doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two reasons given for dropping hadd in the case of mistaken intercourse on the wedding night?
A) The man was drunk and the woman consented
B) It was the first night (he did not recognize his wife) and the women testified she was his wife
C) The woman was a slave and the man owned her
D) The man was coerced and the woman was tricked

Key Takeaway
Hadd is dropped due to shubha (first night and testimony), but mahr must be paid.

Shubha in Wedding Night: No Hadd
Ruling on intercourse due to mistaken identity on wedding night

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a strong shubha (semblance) removes the hadd penalty for zina and explain why the 'uqr (compensatory dower) remains wajib.

Core Idea
A man unknowingly with a mistaken bride on wedding night faces no hadd, but must pay mahr.

This lesson examines a classic case of mistaken identity on the wedding night, where a man is led to believe a woman is his wife. The Hanafi school uses this scenario to illustrate the powerful effect of shubha in criminal law: even a strong presumption can remove the fixed penalty of hadd. However, the financial obligation of mahr remains, reflecting the school's careful balancing of rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and key elements
Note the setting: wedding night, man has never seen his wife. Women bring a different woman and testify she is his wife. He has intercourse in good faith.
These elements create a strong shubha that blocks hadd.
2
State the legal ruling
The text rules: no hadd (no whipping or stoning) for the man. However, he must pay the mahr (compensatory dower) called 'uqr.
The mahr is wajib because intercourse occurred under a shubha, not as zina.
3
Analyze the two excuses
The commentator gives two reasons why hadd is removed: (1) the man does not yet know his wife (first night), (2) women's testimony created a strong presumption that she is his wife.
Both excuses together make the shubha legally effective.
4
Trace the evidence from the athar
The text cites two reports: (a) Ali (RA) was presented a man and woman found together; the woman claimed he was her husband, and Ali dropped the hadd. (b) Ibrahim said if a woman taken with a man says 'he married me', if true, no hadd. Here, multiple women testified, which is a fortiori.
The athar show the principle that a woman's claim of marriage removes hadd, and stronger testimony works similarly.
5
Distinguish weaker shubha
Not all mistaken identity removes hadd. The shubha must be strong (e.g., wedding night context, multiple witnesses). Without these, hadd may apply.
For example, if a man makes a mistake without external testimony, the shubha may be insufficient.

علیؓ نے فرمایا اپنی بیوی کا ہاتھ پکڑ لو یعنی حد نہیں لگائی۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا کوئی عورت مرد کے ساتھ زنا میں پکڑی جائے پس وہ کہے کہ مجھ سے شادی کی ہے۔ پس حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا اگر یہ بات سچ ہو تو ایسے زانی پر حد نہیں ہوگی۔
[2481] (38) Whoever is brought a woman other than his wife, and women say she is your wife, and he has intercourse with her: there is no hadd upon him, and upon him is the mahr.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This is a ruling concerning a shubha (semblance) situation on the wedding night. The text states that if a man is brought a woman other than his wife on the wedding night, and women testify that she is his wife, and he has intercourse with her in good faith, then the hadd penalty for zina is not imposed on him because of the strong shubha. However, he must pay the mahr for the woman (the mahr al-mithl or 'uqr), because intercourse with shubha makes the mahr obligatory. The commentator explains that the man has two excuses: first, he does not yet know his wife (first night), and second, the women's testimony created a strong presumption that she is his wife. The text then brings two athar (reports) to support the principle that a woman's claim of being a wife removes hadd. The first athar: from Yahya ibn Abi al-Haytham that Ali (RA) was brought a man and woman found together; the man said she is his cousin and foster-daughter; his companions told the woman to say 'he is my husband'; she said it; Ali said 'take your wife's hand' — no hadd. The second athar: Ibrahim said if a woman taken with a man says 'he married me', if true, no hadd on the adulterer. The margin note mentions that Umar (RA) flogged a man who had intercourse with his wife's slave-girl but did not stone him, indicating that shubha removes stoning but flogging may apply. Overall, the passage establishes that strong shubha from multiple women's testimony removes hadd, and the 'uqr (dower) is due.

Key Terms
شبہ (shubha): A semblance or doubt that creates a legal excuse, preventing hadd.
عقر (uqr): Compensatory dower for intercourse under shubha, equivalent to mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a man being brought a woman other than his wife on the wedding night with women testifying she is his wife, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hadd of flogging is imposed, and no mahr is due.
B) Hadd is removed, but mahr is wajib.
C) Both hadd and mahr are waived.
D) Stoning is imposed because the man could have asked.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a strong shubha (e.g., multiple witnesses on wedding night) removes the hadd penalty for zina but does not waive the financial obligation of mahr.

Finding a Woman on One's Bed: Hadd Applies
Ruling on intercourse with a woman found on one's bed without verification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of shubha to determine whether hadd is imposed in cases of intercourse with a woman found on one's bed without verification.

Core Idea
Finding a woman on your bed does not create shubha; you must verify or recognize her.

The previous lesson discussed a scenario where a man was informed that a woman was his wife, creating a strong shubha that waived hadd. This lesson addresses a man who finds a woman on his bed but does not know her. Without inquiry or recognition, there is no valid shubha, so the hadd penalty is imposed. The ruling emphasizes the importance of verification even when a woman is found in an intimate setting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is intercourse with a woman found on one's bed. The ruling is that hadd is wajib upon the man.
2
Assess the Presence of Shubha
Shubha is the key factor. The man did not know the woman's identity. He could have recognized her or asked. Since he acted without verification, there is no strong shubha.
Contrast with the earlier case where the man was told she was his wife.
3
Derive the General Principle
Whenever a person has intercourse without a strong shubha, hadd is imposed. The burden is on the man to establish shubha.
This principle is consistent across Hanafi rulings on zina.
4
Apply to Practical Scenarios
Consider a man whose daughter sometimes sleeps in his bed. He must ask before intercourse. Failure to verify leads to hadd.
The ruling is strict to prevent abuse and protect family honor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۸۲] (۳۹) ومن وجد امرأة على فراشه فوطأها فعليه الحد

شرح: آدمی نے ایک عورت کو اپنی چار پائی پر پایا ، پس اس سے ولی کر لی تو اس پر حد ہے۔
بار بار ملنے کی وجہ سے تجربہ ہے کہ بیوی کون ہے اس کا اندازہ تو اندھیرے میں بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور اگر انداز نہیں ہوا تو پوچھ لینا چاہئے۔ اس کے باوجود نہ پوچھانہ اندازہ سے کام لیا تو حد لگے گی ۔ اس طرح تو عموما گھر میں ذی رحم محرم عورتیں مثلا بیٹی ، بہو چار پائی پر سو جاتی ہے بغیر تحقیق کئے وطی کرے تو بیٹی اور بہو سے ولی کرنا لازم ہوگا اس لئے مرد پر حد لگے گی۔ اصول یہ مسائل اس اصول پر ہیں کہ جہاں بیوی ہونے کا یا اپنی باندی ہونے کا قوی شبہ ہو پھر اس سے وطی کر لی تو حد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور جہاں بیوی ہونے کا یا اپنی باندی ہونے کا قوی شبہ نہ ہو پھر بھی وطی کرلے تو پہلی کرنے والے پر حد لازم ہو جائے گی۔
[2482] (39) Whoever finds a woman on his bed and has intercourse with her: upon him is hadd.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This is a ruling contrasting with the previous one. Here, a man finds a woman on his bed (not his wife) and has intercourse without verifying. The hadd penalty is imposed. The commentator explains that due to frequent contact, a man can usually recognize his wife even in darkness. If he is unsure, he should ask. Since he acted without inquiry, there is no shubha (semblance) to excuse him. The commentator gives a practical example: if a man's daughter or daughter-in-law sleeps on the same bed, he must verify before intercourse, otherwise hadd applies. The general principle: wherever there is strong shubha (like being told she is his wife), hadd is waived; where there is no strong shubha, hadd is imposed.

Key Terms
فراش (firash): The bed; a place where one normally sleeps with his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man finds a woman on his bed but does not inquire and has intercourse, which of the following is true?
A) Hadd is waived because she was on his bed.
B) Hadd is imposed.
C) He must only pay compensation.
D) He is excused if he thought she was his wife.

Key Takeaway
Verification of identity is mandatory before intercourse, even if the woman is found in an intimate setting; failure to do so makes one liable for hadd.

Marriage to a Permanently Prohibited Woman: Hadd or Ta'zir?
Intra-Hanafi / inter-madhhab dispute on hadd for marital zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for zina with a permanently prohibited woman, evaluate the opposing proofs of Sahibayn and Shafi'i, and explain the role of shubha in averting hadd.

Core Idea
A marriage contract, even if void, creates shubha that averts hadd, leaving only ta'zir.

This lesson examines a classical dispute on whether a man who marries a permanently prohibited woman (e.g., stepmother) and consummates the marriage incurs the hadd penalty for zina. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the marriage contract, though invalid, creates a legal semblance (shubha) that prevents the application of hadd; instead, discretionary punishment (ta'zir) is imposed. The two companions (Sahibayn) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that hadd applies because the marriage is void ab initio, leaving the woman a stranger. We will trace the proofs of both sides and see how the Hanafi school resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
A man marries a permanently prohibited woman (e.g., stepmother) and has intercourse. The issue: does he incur hadd for zina?
The marriage is void (batil) from the start.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
No hadd, only ta'zir, because the marriage contract creates a shubha (semblance) of legality that removes the hadd.
Ta'zir may include execution, as seen in the hadith.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Two hadiths: (1) 'Avert the hudud from the Muslims as much as you can' (Tirmidhi). (2) The Prophet ordered execution of a man who married his father's wife; Abu Hanifa interprets this as ta'zir, not hadd.
The execution hadith is the key evidence for the severity of ta'zir.
4
Present the opposing view
Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Shafi'i say hadd is wajib. The marriage is void, so the woman remains a stranger; intercourse is pure zina. They interpret the execution hadith as a hadd punishment.
They deny that an invalid contract creates any shubha.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
Despite the invalidity, the contract itself creates a shubha that averts hadd. The Prophet's execution was discretionary (ta'zir), not a prescribed hadd.
The principle 'Avert hudud with doubts' applies.
6
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the man is not stoned or flogged (only ta'zir, possibly execution). Under Sahibayn/Shafi'i, he is stoned or flogged as hadd.
The difference is between a discretionary punishment and a fixed hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۸۳] (۴۰) ومن تزوج امرأة لا يحل له نكاحها فوطأها لم يجب عليه الحد.

شرح: کسی نے ایسی عورت سے نکاح کیا جس سے نکاح کرنا اس کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے اور اس سے وطی کی تو اس پر حد نہیں ہے مثلا سوتیلی ماں سے نکاح کر لیا حالانکہ اس سے نکاح کرنا حلال نہیں ہے۔ یا خالہ سے نکاح کر لیا حالانکہ اس سے نکاح کرنا حلال نہیں ہے اور وطی بھی کر لی تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر حد نہیں لگے گی البتہ تعزیر ہوگی۔ نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے بیوی ہونے کا شبہ ہو گیا اور او پر حدیث گزری کہ شبہ ہو تو حتی الامکان حدود ساقط کیا کرو عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله له ادرء وا الحدود عن المسلمين ما استطعتم (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی درء الحدود ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۴۲۴) یہاں نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے بیوی کا شبہ ہو گیا اس لئے حد نہیں لگے گی البتہ تعزیر کی جائے گی۔ اور تعزیر میں قتل بھی کیا جا سکتا ہے، چنانچہ حدیث میں ہے کہ سوتیلی ماں کے ساتھ شادی کی تو آپ نے اس کو تعزیر کے طور پرقتل کیا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن يزيد بن البراء عن ابيه قال لقيت عمى ومعه رايه فقلت له این ترید؟ فقال بعثنی رسول الله الله الله الى رجل نكح امرأة ابيه فامرنی ان اضرب عنقه واخذ ماله (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرجل یزنی بحریمہ ص ۲۶۴ نمبر ۷ ۴۴۵ ) اس حدیث میں سوتیلی ماں کے ساتھ نکاح کیا تو تعزیر کے طور پر اس کو قتل کیا گیا اور اس کے مال کو لے لیا گیا۔
نان امام ابو یوسف، امام محمد اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ حد لگے گی۔ کیونکہ جب نکاح حلال نہیں تھا تو نکاح ہوا ہی نہیں وہ اجنبی رہی۔ اور اجنبیہ سے وطی کرنے سے حد گتی ہے (۲) اوپر کی حدیث میں حضور نے حد کے طور پر قتل کرنے کوفرمایا تھا تعزیر کے طور پر نہیں۔
[2483] (40) Whoever marries a woman whose marriage is not lawful for him, and has intercourse with her: hadd is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa's position: if a man marries a woman who is permanently prohibited to him (e.g., stepmother, maternal aunt) and consummates the marriage, no hadd is imposed because the marriage contract creates a shubha (semblance) of being a lawful wife. Instead, ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is given, which can include execution as in the hadith of a man who married his father's wife; the Prophet ordered his execution and confiscation of property. The commentator cites the general hadith 'Avert the hudud from the Muslims as much as you can' (from Aisha, Tirmidhi).

Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad, and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that hadd is wajib because the marriage is void ab initio (the woman remains a stranger), and intercourse with a stranger is zina that requires hadd. They interpret the hadith of execution as a hadd punishment, not ta'zir.

The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: no hadd, only ta'zir.

Key Terms
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the judge, can include execution, for offenses for which no hadd is prescribed.
شبہ (shubha): A legal semblance that creates doubt, preventing application of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a man marries his stepmother (a permanently prohibited marriage) and consummates it, what is the ruling?
A) Hadd of stoning is wajib.
B) No hadd, but ta'zir is given (which may include execution).
C) The marriage is valid and no punishment.
D) Only flogging is wajib.

Key Takeaway
A marriage contract, though invalid, creates shubha sufficient to avert hadd; the penalty becomes ta'zir.

Ruling on Sodomy: No Hadd According to Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa's ruling on liwat with evidence and Sahibayn's opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liwat and evaluate the disagreement with the Sahibayn and Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: liwat is not zina, so only ta'zir; Sahibayn and Shafi'i: liwat is zina and incurs hadd.

This lesson tackles a key intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute: does sodomy (liwat) carry the fixed punishment (hadd) of fornication (zina) or a discretionary penalty (ta'zir)? The passage presents Abu Hanifa's position—no hadd, only ta'zir—and contrasts it with the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i, who equate liwat with zina. Understanding the reasoning behind each view is essential for grasping Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling attributed to Abu Hanifa: no hadd for liwat, only ta'zir. Note that this is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The matn explicitly states 'la hadd' (no fixed punishment).
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that liwat is like zina and thus carries the hadd penalty (lashes for non-muhsan, stoning for muhsan).
The text says 'qala' (the two said) and mentions Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the evidence cited by the opponents: (a) the hadith commanding killing the active and passive participants, which they interpret as a hadd; (b) athar from tabi'un equating the hadd of liwat with that of zina; (c) qiyas on zina itself.
Qiyas here is analogizing liwat to zina due to the presence of illicit penetration.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's counter-arguments: (1) the Quranic definition of zina is restricted to vaginal intercourse (firj), so liwat is not zina; (2) the hadith commanding killing is a ta'zir measure, not a hadd, because the fixed hadd is 100 lashes or stoning, not killing.
The Hanafis prioritize the literal definition over broad analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, the judge imposes a discretionary punishment (e.g., imprisonment, flogging without fixed number); under the opposing view, the fixed hadd (stoning or 100 lashes) applies.
This difference can result in radically different sentences for the same act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۸۴] (۴۱) ومن أتى امرأة فى الموضع المكروه او عمل عمل قوم لوط فلا حد عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ويعزر وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى هو كالزنا فيُحَدُّ [۲۴۸۴] (۴۱) کسی نے عورت سے مکروہ جگہ میں ولی کی یا قوم لوط کا عمل کیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر حد نہیں ہے اور تعزیر کی جائے گی ۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ زانی کی طرح ہے اس لئے حد لگے گی۔ تشریح اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ لواطت کیا یا کسی مرد کے ساتھ لواطت کیا یعنی دبر میں وطی کی تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک حد نہیں ہے البتہ تعزیر ہوگی۔ آیت میں زانی کو حد یار جسم کی سزا ہے۔ اور یہ زانی نہیں ہے کیونکہ زنا اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ مقام مخصوص میں ولی کرے اس لئے اس کو حد نہیں لگے گی (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے کہ لوطی کو تعزیر یگی ہے حد نہیں۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الله من وجد تموه يعمل عمل قوم لوط فاقتلوا الفاعل والمفعول به (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن عمل عمل قوم لوط ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۴۴۶۲ ترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی حد الوحی ص ۲۷۰ نمبر ۱۴۵۶) اس حدیث میں لواطت کرنے والے اور لواطت کروانے والے دونوں کو قتل کرنے کے لئے کہا۔ جو اس بات پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ وہ تعزیر کے طور پر تھا حد کے طور پر نہیں حد کے طور پر سو کوڑے لگتے یار جم کرتے ۔ نا صاحبین اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ لواطت زنا کی طرح ہے اس لئے لواطت کرنے والے کو حد لگے گی یعنی محصن ہو تو رجم اور غیر محصن ہو تو کوڑے لگیں گے۔ اوپر کی حدیث میں قتل کرنے کے لئے کہا جو اصل میں حد ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ وقال بعض اهل العلم من فقهاء التابعين منهم الحسن البصرى وابراهيم النخعى وعطاء بن ابي رباح وغيرهم قالوا حد اللوطى حد الزاني وهو قول الثورى واهل الكوفة (ب) ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء في حد اللوطی ص ۲۷۰ نمبر ۶ ۱۴۵ر السن للبیہقی ، باب ماجاء فی حد اللوطی ج ثامن، ص ۴۰۶ نمبر ۱۷۰۳۲) اس اثر اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ لواطت کا حکم زنا کے حکم کی طرح ہے۔
الموضع المكروه : سے مراد بر ہے جو مکر وہ جگہ ہے۔
2484 (41) Whoever comes to a woman in the disliked place or does the act of the people of Lut, there is no hadd according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, and he is given ta'zir. The two said, may Allah be pleased with them, it is like zina, so hadd is applied. (41) Someone committed intercourse with a woman in the disliked place or did the act of the people of Lut, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa there is no hadd upon him and he will be given ta'zir. And the Sahibayn say he is like a fornicator, therefore hadd will be applied. Explanation: He committed liwat with his wife or with a man, i.e., anal intercourse. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is no hadd, but ta'zir. In the verse, the fornicator is punished with hadd (flogging). And this is not a fornicator because zina is called when one comes in the specific place, therefore no hadd. (2) The hadith indicates that the lutite is given ta'zir, not hadd. From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lut, kill the doer and the one with whom it is done.' (a) (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). This hadith commands killing both the doer and the one who causes it to be done. Which indicates that it was by way of ta'zir, not hadd. As for hadd, it is a hundred lashes or stoning. Now the Sahibayn and Imam Shafi'i say that liwat is like zina, therefore hadd will be applied to the one who commits liwat: if muhsan, stoning; if non-muhsan, lashes. The above hadith commands killing, which is originally a hadd. (2) There is an athar: Some scholars from the tabi'un including Hasan al-Basri, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Ata' ibn Abi Rabah and others said: The hadd of the lutite is the hadd of the fornicator, and this is the view of Thawri and the people of Kufa. (b) (Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi). From this athar and hadith it is known that the ruling of liwat is like the ruling of zina. Al-mawdi' al-makruh means the back, which is a disliked place.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the punishment for liwat (sodomy). The matn states Abu Hanifa's position: there is no hadd (fixed punishment) for liwat; rather the offender receives ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that liwat is equivalent to zina and thus requires the hadd penalty (flogging for non-muhsan, stoning for muhsan). The commentator explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the Quranic verse on zina specifies a specific place (vaginal intercourse), and liwat does not fall under that definition. A hadith from Ibn Abbas commands killing the active and passive participants, which the Hanafis interpret as a ta'zir measure, not a hadd, because the killing is not a fixed number of lashes or stoning. In contrast, the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that the killing command is itself a hadd. They also cite an athar from the tabi'un equating the hadd of liwat with that of zina. The Hanafi position is that 'al-mawdi' al-makruh' means the anus, which is a disliked place for intercourse. Thus, the ruling depends on the definition of zina: if limited to vaginal intercourse, liwat cannot be zina. Abu Hanifa's view is based on linguistic and textual grounds, while the opponents rely on qiyas. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as stated in this text.

Key Terms
الموضع المكروه (al-mawdi' al-makruh): The anus, considered a disliked place for intercourse.
لواط (liwat): Sodomy, anal intercourse with a man or woman.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment set by the judge, not a fixed hadd.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Sharia (e.g., lashes, stoning).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what punishment is given for liwat (sodomy)?
A) Hadd: 100 lashes
B) Hadd: stoning
C) Ta'zir (discretionary punishment)
D) No punishment at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that liwat is not zina, thus no hadd; the punishment is ta'zir.

Bestiality: No Hadd, Only Ta'zir
Ruling with proof: bestiality does not incur hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bestiality and explain why no hadd is applied, citing the proof from Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Bestiality is not zina — no hadd, only ta'zir.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between zina (intercourse with a woman) and bestiality. Because the act does not meet the legal definition of zina, the fixed punishment (hadd) does not apply. Instead, the judge imposes a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). This lesson examines the reasoning and the scriptural basis for this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is intercourse with an animal (bestiality). The Hanafi ruling is that there is no hadd (fixed punishment) but only ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
The act is sinful (haram), but the punishment is not fixed.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the statement of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no hadd for the one who comes to an animal.' This is a qawl sahabi (companion's statement), which is a source of law in the Hanafi school.
A hadith commanding killing is also cited but interpreted as an extreme ta'zir, not hadd.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation of hadd in Ibn Abbas's statement directly shows that the fixed punishment of zina does not apply. The definition of zina is restricted to vaginal intercourse with a woman, so bestiality falls outside.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars (e.g., Hasan al-Basri, al-Thawri) equated bestiality with zina and imposed hadd. The Hanafi school rejects this analogy because of the difference in the object of intercourse.
The Hanafi position relies on the companion's explicit statement over analogy.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school prefers the explicit text (qawl sahabi) over analogical reasoning (qiyas). Thus, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is no hadd, only ta'zir.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab.

2485 (42) Whoever fornicates with an animal, there is no hadd upon him. (42) Someone had intercourse with an animal, then no hadd upon him. (1) Because zina is called only that which is done with a woman in the specific place. And here he is committing zina with an animal, therefore this is not zina. Hence the hadd of zina will not be applied, but ta'zir will be. (2) There is a hadith: Ibn Abbas reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever comes to an animal, kill him and kill it with him.' And in another narration there is an athar: Ibn Abbas said: There is no hadd for the one who comes to an animal. (c) (Abu Dawud). (a) He said: Whoever you find doing the act of the people of Lut, kill the doer and the one with whom it is done. (b) Scholars among the tabi'un, such as Hasan al-Basri, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, etc., said: The hadd of the lutite is the same as the hadd of the fornicator: i.e., one hundred lashes or stoning. This is the view of Thawri and the people of Kufa. (c) Ibn Abbas said: There is no hadd for the one who has intercourse with an animal.

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on bestiality: no hadd. The reasoning is that zina is legally defined as vaginal intercourse with a human woman; intercourse with an animal does not meet that definition. Therefore, the fixed punishment for zina does not apply. However, the act is sinful, and the judge may impose ta'zir (discretionary punishment). The commentator cites two narrations from Ibn Abbas: one that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered killing the human and the animal (interpreted as ta'zir, not hadd), and another that clearly states there is no hadd. This supports the Hanafi position. The passage also includes a tangent on liwat (from the same hadith chain), but the core ruling on bestiality is clear: no hadd.

Key Terms
بهيمة (bahima): Quadruped animal, specifically any animal used for bestiality.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment, not fixed.

The Hanafi school rules that bestiality does not incur a fixed hadd punishment because it does not meet the legal definition of zina; only discretionary ta'zir applies.

Zina in Dar al-Harb: No Hadd After Entering Dar al-Islam
Ruling on zina in dar al-harb; no hadd after entering dar al-islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for zina committed in dar al-harb and explain the reasoning based on athar and the principle of averting hadd.

Core Idea
A hadd not established at the time of offense cannot be revived later—even upon entering Islamic territory.

This passage addresses a critical question in Hanafi penal law: when does hudud apply across territorial boundaries? The ruling that hadd is not enforced for zina in dar al-harb even after the offender enters dar al-islam hinges on the concept that hadd requires the presence of Islamic authority at the moment of the act. We will examine the textual evidence (athar) and the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i counterview.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? (zina committed in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy). What is the ruling? (no hadd upon entering dar al-islam).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the specific proofs cited: the athar from Hasan al-Basri, Abu al-Darda', and Umar. Note their sources (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these athar support the ruling? Explanation: the athar assign hudud to the sultan, and dar al-harb lacks a sultan; Umar's order prohibits flogging until the gate, implying hadd is only within dar al-islam.
The Hanafi interpretation: Umar's order is to prevent flight, not to establish hadd retroactively.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view (Shafi'i): hadd applies upon entering dar al-islam because the person is now under Islamic jurisdiction and Umar's athar implies hadd at the gate.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because: (1) hadd requires authority at the time of offense, (2) once not established, it cannot be revived, (3) difficulty of producing witnesses from dar al-harb, (4) principle 'idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat'.
Tarjih authority: based on athar and the principle of averting hadd.
