حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا چار کام بادشاہ ہی کرے، زکوۃ وصول کرنا، نماز جمعہ قائم کرنا، حدود اور قضا قائم کرنا (ب ) حضرت ابوالدرداء نے روکا اس بات سے کہ حد دشمن کی زمیں میں قائم کی جائے ، اور دوسرے اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے لکھا کہ لشکر کا امیر اور سریہ کا امیر کوڑے نہ لگا ئیں یہاں تک کہ اسلامی پھاٹک پر نہ آجائیں تا کہ شیطان کی حمیت مجرم پر حملہ نہ کردے۔ اور کفار سے جا کر نہ مل جائے۔
2486 (43) Whoever commits zina in dar al-harb or in dar al-baghy, then comes out to us, hadd is not established upon him. (43) Someone committed zina in dar al-harb or in the territory of rebels, then came to our place, hadd will not be established upon him. If he was a Muslim and committed zina in dar al-harb, then fled to dar al-islam, or committed zina under rebel rule and came to dar al-islam, hadd will not be established upon him. Because in dar al-harb or rebel territory the hadd cannot be established, as there is no amir or sultan. So the sin did not initially become a cause for hadd. And after coming to dar al-islam, we will not establish hadd because when it did not become a cause for hadd initially, how could hadd be established later? (2) There is an athar: Four things are entrusted to the sultan: zakat, salah (i.e., jumu'ah), hudud, and judgment. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). And in dar al-harb there is no sultan or amir al-mu'minin, so hadd cannot be established there. (3) Another athar: Abu al-Darda' forbade establishing hadd upon anyone in enemy territory. And another athar: Umar wrote that the commander of an army or a detachment should not flog anyone with hadd until they appear at the darab (the gate of dar al-islam), lest the devil's fervor cause him to join the disbelievers. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). From this athar it is known that hadd is not established in enemy land, and since it was not established there, due to being an old hadd, it will not be established in dar al-islam either. Additionally, bringing correct witnesses from dar al-harb to dar al-islam is difficult. Therefore, under the principle 'Avert hadd as much as you can,' the hadd is dropped. However, if the imam deems appropriate, he may give ta'zir. Now Imam Shafi'i says: As long as he was in dar al-harb, hadd would not be established, but when he came to dar al-islam, hadd will be established here. After entering dar al-islam, he is bound by its rules, and since hadd is applicable here, hadd will apply. (2) The above statement of Umar indicates not to establish hadd while in enemy land, but when he comes to dar al-islam, hadd should be established. The word 'darab' means the gate of dar al-islam, i.e., once he arrives at the gate, hadd can be established. The wording of the athar is: Umar wrote that the commander should not flog with hadd until he appears at the gate. So the meaning is that upon reaching the gate, hadd can be established.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling that hadd is not enforced for zina committed in dar al-harb (enemy territory) or dar al-baghy (rebel territory) even after the offender enters dar al-islam. The key reasoning is that the hadd became due only if the authority (sultan) was present at the time of the offense. Since dar al-harb lacks Islamic authority, the act did not incur a hadd punishment initially. This is supported by athar from Hasan al-Basri (four things are for the sultan) and from Umar (do not flog until reaching the Islamic gate). The principle 'Avert hadd as much as possible' is also invoked. The commentator then contrasts Imam al-Shafi'i's view, who would apply hadd upon entering dar al-islam, relying on the fact that the offender is now under Islamic jurisdiction and that Umar's instruction only prohibits flogging in enemy territory but permits it at the border. The Hanafi response is that hadd, once not established, cannot be revived; also, witnesses are hard to bring. The footnote clarifies the athar: Umar's order was to prevent the criminal from fleeing to the enemy out of desperation. Thus, the Hanafi position is that no hadd is established; only ta'zir may be given at the imam's discretion.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced.
دار البغى (dar al-baghy): Territory controlled by rebels (baghi) against the Islamic state.
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment at the imam's discretion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hadd is established upon entry
B) No hadd is established; only ta'zir may be given
C) He is executed immediately
D) He is forgiven entirely

Key Takeaway
Hadd for zina in dar al-harb is not established upon entering dar al-islam because the absence of Islamic authority at the time of the act prevents the hadd from being due; only ta'zir may be applied.

Zina in Dar al-Harb: No Hadd Applied
Inter-madhhab dispute on jurisdiction for hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hadd for zina committed outside dar al-islam, explain the supporting athar, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Hadd is tied to territory: if not implemented initially, it cannot be applied later.

This passage addresses a critical territorial limitation on the application of hudud. The Hanafi school holds that if zina occurs in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy, the hadd punishment is never applied, even if the person later enters dar al-islam. The Shafi'i school disagrees. Let us examine the proofs and reasoning on both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: no hadd for zina committed in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy, regardless of later entry into dar al-islam.
2
Cite the Hanafi proofs
List the athar from Hasan al-Basri, Abu al-Darda', and Umar. Explain how each supports the Hanafi view.
These are qawl sahabi proofs.
3
Present the Shafi'i objection
State Imam al-Shafi'i's position: hadd applies upon entering dar al-islam. Identify his proof from Umar's letter.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis reinterpret Umar's letter: 'until they reach the gate' refers to acts after arrival, not past acts. Also note the difficulty of witnesses and the principle of averting hudud.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi school, no hadd; in Shafi'i school, hadd is applied. Also note that ta'zir is possible in Hanafi view.

كتاب الحدود
[۲۴۸۶] (۴۳) ومن زنى فى دار الحرب او في دار البغى ثم خرج الينا لم يقم عليه الحد. شریف ، باب فیمن اتی بھیم ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۴۴۶۵٫۴۴۶۴ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فيمن يقع علی الحمیمہ ق ص ۲۶۹ نمبر ۱۴۵۵) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جانور سے وطی کرنے والے کو تعزیر کے طور پر قتل کر دے۔ البتہ اس پر زنا کی طرح حد نہیں ہے۔ (۲۴۸۶] (۴۳) کسی نے دار الحرب میں زنا کیا یا باغیوں کی حکومت میں زنا کیا پھر ہمارے یہاں آ گیا تو اس پر حد قائم نہیں ہوگی۔ مسلمان تھا دار الحرب میں زنا کیا پھر وہاں سے بھاگ کر دار الاسلام آگیا یا با غیوں کی حکومت میں زنا کیا اور وہاں سے دار الاسلام میں آ گیا تو اس پر حد قائم نہیں ہوگی۔
ے دار الحرب میں یا باغیوں کی حکومت میں حد قائم نہیں کر سکتے ۔ کیونکہ وہاں امیر اور سلطان نہیں ہے تو گویا کہ یہ گناہ ابتدا میں حد کا موجب نہیں ہوا۔ اور وہاں سے دار الاسلام آنے کے بعد بھی حد قائم نہیں کریں گے کیونکہ جب شروع میں حد کا موجب نہیں ہوا تو بعد میں حد کیسے قائم کریں گے (۲) اثر میں ہے کہ چار کام سلطان کے سپرد ہیں وہی انجام دیں گے۔ عن الحسن قال اربعة الى السلطان الزكاة والصلوة (اى الجمعة) والحدود والقضاء (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۵۹ من قال الحدود الی الا مام ج خامس ص ۵۰۲ نمبر ۲۸۴۲۹) اور دارالحرب میں سلطان اور امیر المومنین نہیں ہیں اس لئے وہاں حد قائم نہیں ہو سکے گی (۳) ایک اثر میں ہے کہ ان ابا الدرداء نهى ان يقام على احد حد فی ارض العدو ، اور دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ کتب عمر الا يجلدون امير جيش ولا سرية احدا الحد حتى يطلع على الدرب لئلا يحمله حمية الشيطان ان يلحق بالكفار (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۳۴ فی اقامتہ الحد علی الرجل في ارض العدوج خامس ص ۵۲۳ نمبر ۲۸۸۵۲/۲۸۸۵۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دشمن کی زمین میں حد قائم نہ کریں اور جب وہاں قائم نہ ہوئی تو پرانی حد ہونے کی وجہ سے دار الاسلام میں بھی قائم نہیں کی جائے گی۔ یوں بھی دار الحرب سے دار الاسلام تک صحیح گواہوں کو پیش کرنا ایک مشکل کام ہے۔ اس لئے ادرء وا الحدود ما استطعتم کے تحت حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ البتہ امام مناسب سمجھے تو تعزیر کر دے۔
نان امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب تک دار الحرب میں تھا تو حد قائم نہیں ہوگی لیکن جب دارالاسلام میں آیا تو یہاں حد قائم ہوگی۔ دار الاسلام میں آنے کے بعد یہاں کے احکام کا پابند ہے اور یہاں حد کا کام کرتا تو حد لگتی اس لئے یہاں آنے کے بعد حد لگے گی (۲) اوپر حضرت عمر کے قول سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جب تک دشمن کی زمین ہو تو حد قائم نہ کرے لیکن جب دار الاسلام میں آجائے تو حد قائم کرے۔ کیونکہ درب کہتے ہیں دار الاسلام کے پھاٹک کو یعنی پھاٹک پر آجائے تو حد قائم کر سکتا ہے۔ اثر کے الفاظ یہ ہیں۔ کتب عمر الا يجلدون امير جيش ولا سرية احدا الحد حتى يطلع على الدرب (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۳۴افی اقسمة الحد على الرجل في ارض العدد ج خامس ص ۵۴۳ نمبر ۲۸۸۵۲) اثر کا انداز یہ ہے کہ دارالاسلام کے پھاٹک پر آئے تو حد قائم کر سکتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا چار کام بادشاہ ہی کرے، زکوۃ وصول کرنا، نماز جمعہ قائم کرنا، حدود اور قضا قائم کرنا (ب ) حضرت ابوالدرداء نے روکا اس بات سے کہ حد دشمن کی زمیں میں قائم کی جائے ، اور دوسرے اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے لکھا کہ لشکر کا امیر اور سریہ کا امیر کوڑے نہ لگا ئیں یہاں تک کہ اسلامی پھاٹک پر نہ آجائیں تا کہ شیطان کی حمیت مجرم پر حملہ نہ کردے۔ اور کفار سے جا کر نہ مل جائے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 3, page 389. Book of Legal Punishments. [2486] (43) Whoever commits zina in dar al-harb or in dar al-baghy then comes out to us, the hadd is not established against him. (Hadith references) From this hadith and athar it is known that the one who has intercourse with an animal should be killed as ta'zir. However, there is no hadd like zina upon him. [2486] (43) Someone committed zina in dar al-harb or in the government of the rebels, then came to us, then hadd will not be established on him. He was a Muslim, committed zina in dar al-harb, then fled from there to dar al-islam, or committed zina in the government of the rebels and came from there to dar al-islam, then hadd will not be established on him. (Reasoning) Because there is no amir or sultan there, so this sin did not initially cause hadd. And after coming to dar al-islam, we will not establish hadd because when initially it did not cause hadd, then how can hadd be established later? (2) There is an athar that four things are entrusted to the sultan; he will perform them: from Hasan: four things are for the sultan: zakat, prayer (i.e., Friday), hudud, and judgment. And in dar al-harb there is no sultan or amir al-mu'minin, so hadd cannot be established. (3) There is an athar that Abu al-Darda' forbade establishing hadd on anyone in enemy territory, and another athar: Umar wrote that the commander of the army and the commander of a detachment should not flog anyone with hadd until they reach the gate (darb) lest the zeal of shaitan cause him to join the disbelievers. From this athar it is known that hadd is not established in enemy land, and when it was not established there, due to being an old hadd, it will not be established in dar al-islam either. Also, presenting correct witnesses from dar al-harb to dar al-islam is a difficult task, therefore under 'avert the hudud as much as you can', the hadd will fall. However, if the imam deems fit, he may give ta'zir. Now Imam Shafi'i says: As long as he was in dar al-harb, hadd will not be applied, but when he comes to dar al-islam, hadd will be applied. After coming to dar al-islam, he is bound by its laws, and if the act of hadd occurs here, hadd would be applied; so after coming, hadd will be applied. (2) From the above saying of Umar, it appears that as long as in enemy land, do not establish hadd, but when he comes to dar al-islam, establish hadd. Because 'darb' means the gate of dar al-islam; i.e., when he reaches the gate, hadd can be established. The words of the athar are: Umar wrote: 'Do not flog... until they reach the gate.' The style of the athar is that when he comes to the gate of dar al-islam, hadd can be established. Footnote: (a) Hasan said: Four things the king does: collect zakat, establish Friday prayer, hudud, and judgment. (b) Abu al-Darda' forbade establishing hadd in enemy territory, and in another athar, Umar wrote that the commander of the army and the detachment commander should not flog until they come to the Islamic gate so that the zeal of shaitan does not attack the criminal and he joins the disbelievers.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the application of the hadd punishment for zina when the act occurs outside the territorial jurisdiction of an Islamic ruler. The Hanafi position, supported by multiple athar (traditions from the Companions), holds that no hadd is applied whether the person remains in dar al-harb/dar al-baghy or later enters dar al-islam. The key reasoning is that the implementation of hudud is a prerogative of the Islamic sultan, and in dar al-harb there is no such authority; therefore the sin never becomes subject to hadd. Additionally, the principle of averting hudud with doubts (idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat) and the practical difficulty of producing witnesses from enemy territory reinforce this view. The Shafi'i school argues that upon entering dar al-islam, the person becomes subject to Islamic law and thus hadd should be applied. They interpret Umar's letter regarding the gate (darb) as meaning that once the person reaches the Islamic gate, hadd can be carried out. The Hanafi response clarifies that the athar refers to acts committed after arrival, not past acts. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view, which also allows the imam to impose ta'zir (discretionary punishment) if deemed appropriate.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific offenses.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced.
دار البغى (dār al-baghy): Territory controlled by rebels against the Islamic ruler.
تعزير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment left to the judge's discretion, less than hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person commits zina in dar al-harb and then enters dar al-islam, what is the ruling?
A) Hadd is applied immediately.
B) Hadd is not applied.
C) Hadd is applied but reduced.
D) He is given ta'zir only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not apply hadd for zina committed in dar al-harb or dar al-baghy because hudud require the authority of an Islamic sultan, which is absent in those territories.

Conditions for Hadd on Drinking Wine
Ruling with proof on the hadd punishment for wine drinking when smell is present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for applying the hadd punishment for drinking wine and cite the primary evidence (Quran and Sunnah) that establishes the ruling.

Core Idea
Hadd for wine requires fresh evidence — the smell and witness/confession — not stale proof.

In the Hanafi school, the fixed punishment (hadd) for drinking wine is not applied automatically upon any confession or testimony. This lesson examines the precise conditions that must be met at the moment of apprehension. The passage from al-Sharh al-Samiri clarifies that the presence of the smell of wine is essential, and either two witnesses or a confession must occur while the smell remains. We will explore the textual proofs and the reasoning behind these requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is drinking wine (shurb al-khamr). The ruling is that the hadd (fixed punishment) becomes wajib upon fulfillment of conditions.
The hadd is 80 lashes in the Hanafi school, as derived from the practice of Umar and the hadith.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The prohibition is from Quran 5:90; the hadd is from the hadith of Mu'awiyah (Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi) where the Prophet commands flogging for repeated drinking.
The hadith uses the imperative 'fajliduhum', indicating wujub.
3
Extract the conditions for hadd
Two conditions are stated: (1) The person is caught while the smell of wine is present; (2) Either two male witnesses testify to willing consumption, or the person confesses while the smell remains.
The presence of smell proves recent consumption; stale evidence is unacceptable for such a severe punishment.
4
Understand the principle of stale evidence
Old testimony or confession (after the smell has gone) is not considered. The hadd is only for fresh, verifiable instances.
This protects against false accusations and ensures certainty.
5
Confirm with the practice of the Sahaba
The passage cites Umar ibn al-Khattab flogging a man from whom the smell of wine was found, demonstrating application of the condition.
This athar supports the requirement of smell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد الشرب
[۲۴۸۷](۱) ومن شرب الخمر فأخذ وريحها موجودة فشهد الشهود عليه بذلک او اقر وريحها موجودة فعليه الحد
باب حد الشرب
ضروری نوں شراب یا نشہ آور چیزوں کے پینے کو شرب کہتے ہیں اس میں حد ہے۔ اس کے حرام ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ یا ایھا الذین آمنوانما الخمر والميسر والانصاب والازلام رجس من عمل الشيطان فاجتنبوه لعلكم تفلحون (الف) ( آیت ۹۰ سورہ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت سے شراب حرام ہونے کا علم ہوا۔ اور اس کے پینے سے حد لگے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن معاوية بن ابی سفیان قال قال رسول الله الله اذا شربوا الخمر فاجلدوهم ثم ان شربوا فاجلدوهم ثم ان شربوا فاجلدوهم ثم ان شربوا فاقتلوهم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذ انتابع فی شرب الخمرص ۲۶۷ نمبر ۴۴۸۲) ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء من شرب الخمر فاجلدوه ومن عاد في الرابعہ فاقتلو ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۴۴۴) اس حدیث سے پتا چلا کہ شراب پینے والوں کو حد لگے گی۔ ۲۴۸۷] (۱) کسی نے شراب پی اور پکڑا گیا اس حال میں کہ اس کی بوموجود ہے اور گواہوں نے اس کی گواہی دی یا اقرار کیا اس حال میں کہ اس کی بوموجود ہو تو اس پر حد ہے۔ حد لگنے کے لئے دو شرطیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ شراب پینے کی حالت میں اس حال میں پکڑا گیا ہو کہ اس کے منہ میں شراب کی بو ہو۔ اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ اس پر گواہ گواہی دیں کہ اس نے خوشی سے پی ہے تب حد لگے گی۔ اگر بہت پہلے پی تھی یہاں تک کہ اس کے منہ سے بدبو جاتی رہی اس حال میں پکڑا گیا ، یا بد بو کی حالت میں پکڑا تو گیا لیکن اس پر کوئی گواہ نہیں ہے تو حد نہیں لگے گی۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ شراب کی بو کی حالت میں پکڑا گیا اور پینے والا اس کا اقرار کرے کہ میں نے خوشی سے پی ہے تب حد لگے گی ۔ اس حد میں اصول یہ ہے کہ پرانی گواہی یا پرانے اقرار کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اور منہ کی بدبو جانے کے بعد اس کو پرانا سمجھا جائے گا۔ اس لئے ہد ہو جانے کے بعد پکڑنا اقرار کرنا قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔ عن عمر بن الخطاب انه جلد رجلا وجد منه ريح شراب الحد تاما (ج) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب الاشربة و غیر حاج رابع ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۴۶۴۳ رسنن بیہقی ، باب من وجد منه ريح شراب اولقی سكران ج ما من ص ۵۴۷ نمبر ۱۷۵۱۳) اس سے اشارہ ہوا کہ بو کی حالت میں پکڑا گیا ہوتب حد لگے گی۔ اور گواہ یا اقرار کے بغیر تو حد جاری ہوتی ہی نہیں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) اے ایمان والو یقیناً شراب، جوا، بت اور قسمت آزمانے کے تیر ناپاک ہیں ، شیطان کے عمل ہیں اس لئے ان سے بچھو شاید تم کامیاب ہو جاؤ گے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اگر شراب پیئے تو ان کو کوڑے لگاؤ، پھر شراب پیئے تو ان کو کوڑے لگاؤ، پھر شراب پیئے تو ان کو کوڑے لگاؤ، پھر اگر شراب پیئے تو قتل کر دو (ج)
حضرت عمر نے ایک آدمی کو مکمل حد لگائی اس سے شراب کی بو آتی تھی۔
Chapter of the Hadd for Drinking. [2487] (1) Whoever drinks wine and is caught while its smell is present, and the witnesses testify to that, or he confesses while its smell is present, then upon him is the hadd. Chapter of the Hadd for Drinking. Necessary: Drinking wine or intoxicating substances is called 'shurb'; there is a hadd for it. The proof of its prohibition is this verse: 'O you who believe, indeed wine, gambling, idols, and divining arrows are abominations from the work of Satan, so avoid them that you may be successful' (Al-Maidah 5:90). From this verse it is known that wine is prohibited. And the proof that drinking incurs hadd is this hadith: from Mu'awiyah ibn Abi Sufyan: The Messenger of Allah said: 'When they drink wine, flog them; then if they drink, flog them; then if they drink, flog them; then if they drink, kill them.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is clear that those who drink wine will receive hadd. [2487] (1) Someone drank wine and was caught in a state where its smell was present, and witnesses testified, or he confessed while its smell was present, then he incurs hadd. There are two conditions for hadd: one is that he was caught in the state of drinking with the smell of wine in his mouth. The second condition is that witnesses testify that he drank willingly; then hadd will be applied. If he drank long ago such that the smell left his mouth, and he was caught in that state, or he was caught with the smell but there is no witness, then no hadd. The second case is that he was caught with the smell and the drinker confesses that he drank willingly, then hadd will be applied. The principle in this hadd is that old testimony or old confession is not considered. After the smell of the mouth is gone, it is considered old. Therefore, after the hadd has passed, catching and confessing is not acceptable. From Umar ibn al-Khattab: He flogged a man from whom the smell of wine was found with the full hadd. This indicates that if caught with the smell, hadd will be applied. Without witness or confession, hadd is not carried out. Footnote: (a) 'O you who believe, indeed...' (b) He said: if he drinks wine, flog them; then if he drinks, flog them; then if he drinks, flog them; then if he drinks, kill them. (c) Umar flogged a man with full hadd; the smell of wine was coming from him.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the hadd punishment for drinking wine. The chapter begins by defining 'shurb' as drinking wine or any intoxicant, establishing the prohibition via Quran (5:90) and the hadd via the hadith of Mu'awiyah, where the Prophet commanded flogging for repeated offenses, with death on the fourth occasion. The core ruling [2487] states that the hadd is only applicable if the person is caught while the smell of wine is present, and either two male witnesses testify (fulfilling the condition of willing consumption) or the person confesses while the smell remains. The commentary clarifies two conditions: (1) the smell must be present at the time of apprehension, and (2) there must be either witness testimony or confession. If the smell has dissipated, previous drinking cannot be proven, and thus no hadd is applied. The principle is that stale evidence is not accepted, as the hadd is a severe punishment requiring fresh proof. The athar from Umar confirms that flogging was carried out based on the presence of the smell. The footnote provides the full text of the Quranic verse and hadith.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): Drinking wine or any intoxicating substance.
ريح (rayḥ): The smell of wine emanating from the drinker's mouth.
حد الشرب (ḥadd al-shurb): The fixed punishment for drinking wine, which is 80 lashes in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when is the hadd punishment for drinking wine applied?
A) Whenever a person confesses to drinking.
B) Only if witnesses testify, regardless of smell.
C) If the person is caught with the smell of wine present and witnesses testify or he confesses.
D) Only if the person is found drunk.

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking wine is only applied when the drinker is caught with the smell of wine present and there is either witness testimony or confession made while the smell remains.

No Hadd for Confession After Wine Smell Fades
Ruling on confession after dissipation of wine smell

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a confession for wine drinking after the smell has dissipated and explain why the hadd is not applied.

Core Idea
Confession after wine smell fades is stale — it cannot trigger the hadd.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text presents a crucial condition for the application of hadd in cases of wine drinking. While confession is normally a valid proof, its timing matters: if the accused confesses after the physical evidence (the smell) has disappeared, the confession loses its legal force. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that no hadd is applied in such a case. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the broader principle behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is confessing to drinking wine. The ruling: no hadd is applied.
2
Recognize the condition that triggers the ruling
The condition is that the confession occurs after the smell of wine has disappeared. This timeliness element is decisive.
Compare with the case where the smell is present — then confession is valid.
3
Understand the rationale
Staleness creates doubt (shubha), and hadd is averted by doubts. The disappearance of the smell indicates the consumption is not recent, making the confession unreliable.
Hadd is applied only when evidence is unambiguous.
4
Contrast with the opposite scenario
If the confession is made while the smell is still present, the hadd would be applied. This highlights the importance of timeliness.
5
Memorize the ruling as a legal maxim
Confession after dissipation of the smell does not incur hadd.
Repeat this principle in your own words.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[2488] (2) And if he confesses after the disappearance of its smell, he is not punished with the hadd. [2488] (2) If he confesses to drinking after the smell has gone, then the hadd will not be applied. This passage is a short ruling statement that directly follows the previous ruling. It clarifies that a confession made after the smell of wine has dissipated is not legally effective for imposing the hadd punishment. The commentary gives an example: if someone drank wine the previous day and the smell has now vanished, then confesses, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no hadd is applied. The basis for this is that the hadd requires fresh evidence; once the smell is gone, the link to the act is broken, and the confession is considered delayed and unreliable. This aligns with the principle that hadd is averted by doubts, and stale evidence creates such doubt.

Key Terms

Conditions for Hadd on Drinking Khamr
Rules for applying the hadd on drinking khamr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for establishing the hadd on drinking khamr and apply them to a scenario.

Core Idea
Hadd for khamr requires recent smell plus witnesses or confession; neither alone suffices.

This lesson lays out the precise conditions under which a Muslim who drinks wine (khamr) incurs the fixed punishment (hadd). The Hanafi school is careful to balance the severity of the punishment with the need for certainty: only when the drinker is caught with the smell still on his breath and either two male witnesses testify or he himself confesses while the smell persists does the hadd become wajib. Understanding these conditions prevents both wrongful application and evasion of justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm level
From the matn: 'found upon him the hadd' – the ruling is that hadd is wajib (obligatory). Note that the hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is from a hadith (zanni al-thubut) and Quran establishes prohibition but hadd comes from Sunnah.
Hanafi: fard requires qat'i dalil; wajib can be established by zanni dalil.
2
Extract the two conditions
The text states: 'whoever drinks wine and is caught while its smell exists, and the witnesses testify to that, or he confesses while its smell exists'. Thus: (1) the smell of wine must be present on the drinker at the time of apprehension, indicating recent consumption; (2) there must be either two witnesses or a confession made while the smell is present.
The smell is a necessary but insufficient condition; it must be combined with witnesses or confession.
3
Analyse the proofs (dalil)
The commentary cites Quran 5:90 (prohibition) and the hadith of Muawiyah (flogging for drinking). The Quran establishes the act as haram; the Sunnah specifies the punishment. The athar of Umar (RA) shows that punishment was based on smell plus witnesses.
The hadd is not directly from Quran text but from the Sunnah; Quran provides the basis for prohibition.
4
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Scenario: A man is found unconscious with empty bottles of khamr nearby. When he wakes, his breath smells of wine, but there are no witnesses and he does not confess. According to the text, the hadd is NOT applied because the condition of witnesses or confession is missing.
This illustrates that smell alone does not suffice.
5
Note the opposing view (cross-madhhab)
The Hanafi position is that the hadd is only applied under these strict conditions. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may accept a confession made later or allow other forms of evidence. This lesson focuses on the Hanafi view.
Ikhtilaf is legitimate; the mufta bihi in Hanafi school is as stated.

Source Text

Chapter on the Hadd for Drinking. (2487) Whoever drinks wine and is caught while its smell exists, and the witnesses testify to that, or he confesses while its smell exists, then the hadd is upon him. ... (Urdu commentary: Explanation of conditions, proofs from Quran 5:90 and hadith of Muawiyah, and athar of Umar.)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Chapter on Hadd for Drinking. The matn states that hadd is obligatory on a person who drinks wine (khamr) and is apprehended while the smell of wine is still present on his breath, provided that either two witnesses testify that he drank it wilfully, or he himself confesses while the smell persists. The commentary explains that the Quranic verse (5:90) establishes the prohibition of khamr, and the hadith of Muawiyah (RA) prescribes flogging for drinking, with death after the fourth offense. The commentary further clarifies two conditions: (1) the drinker must be caught while the smell of wine is still in his mouth, indicating recent consumption; (2) there must be either witnesses or a confession made while the smell is present. If the smell has disappeared, or if there are no witnesses and no confession, the hadd is not applied. The athar of Umar (RA) is cited to show that punishment was carried out based on the smell. The established principle is that old testimony or old confession is not acceptable; after the smell goes, the matter is considered old. Without witnesses or confession, the hadd cannot be enforced.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (hadd al-shurb): The fixed legal punishment for drinking khamr (unlawful intoxicants).
رائحة الخمر (ra'ihat al-khamr): The smell of wine on the drinker’s breath, used as evidence of recent consumption.
اقرار (iqrar): A confession made by the drinker that he consumed khamr wilfully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The drinker must vomit wine, and the smell must be present.
D) The drinker must be caught in the act, and the wine must be proven by chemical analysis.

Key Takeaway
Hadd on drinking khamr is only wajib when both the smell is present at apprehension and there are witnesses or a confession made while the smell lasts.

No Hadd if Confession After Smell Gone: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Imam Muhammad
Ruling that confession after smell disappears does not incur hadd, with dispute on time limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on confession after smell is gone and explain the difference with the Shafi'i/Imam Muhammad position.

Core Idea
After the smell disappears, confession alone does not prove recent drinking — hadd is waived.

This passage addresses a key evidentiary requirement in hadd cases for wine drinking: the presence of smell as a sign of recent intoxication. The matn states that if a person confesses after the smell has gone, no hadd is applied. However, Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i limit this to confessions made within a month. We will unpack the reasoning and practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the matn: no hadd if confession after smell disappears. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa holds this position unconditionally.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if the drinking occurred within a month, hadd is still applied even after smell is gone.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their dalil: temporal proximity (within a month) makes the confession reliable; the absence of smell does not negate it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi: smell is a critical piece of evidence; without it, the confession is not credible enough to impose hadd. The matter becomes old and unreliable.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi (Abu Hanifa), a person who confesses after one day without smell is not flogged; under the other view, he is flogged if within a month.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۸۸] (٢) وان اقر بعد ذهاب رائحتها لم يُحدَّ .
[۲۴۸۸ (۲) بوجانے کے بعد پینے کا اقرار کیا تو حد نہیں لگے گی۔
شراب ایک دن پہلے پی تھی اور اب شراب کی بوجا چکی ہے اس کے بعد پینے کا اقرار کیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک حد نہیں لگے گی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) اے ایمان والو یقیناً شراب، جوا، بت اور قسمت آزمانے کے تیر ناپاک ہیں ، شیطان کے عمل ہیں اس لئے ان سے بچھو شاید تم کامیاب ہو جاؤ گے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اگر شراب پیئے تو ان کو کوڑے لگاؤ، پھر شراب پیئے تو ان کو کوڑے لگاؤ، پھر شراب پیئے تو ان کو کوڑے لگاؤ، پھر اگر شراب پیئے تو قتل کر دو (ج)
حضرت عمر نے ایک آدمی کو مکمل حد لگائی اس سے شراب کی بو آتی تھی۔
امام شافعی اور امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ بو جانے کے بعد اگر زمانہ قریب میں پی ہو اور اقرار کیا ہوتب بھی حد لازم ہوگی۔ اور زمانہ قریب کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک ماہ کے اندر کو قریب کہتے ہیں۔ اور ایک ماہ سے دور کو بعید کہتے ہیں۔ اس لئے ایک ماہ کے اندر اندر شراب پی ہو اور اقرار کرے یا گواہی دے دے تو حد لگ جائے گی۔
(2488) And if he confesses after its smell has gone, he is not to be punished with hadd. (Urdu commentary: Explanation of Imam Abu Hanifa’s view that no hadd, and the view of Imam Shafi’i and Imam Muhammad that if the drinking occurred within a month, hadd is still applied.)
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is an intra- and inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of a confession made after the smell of wine has disappeared. The matn states that if a person confesses after the smell is gone, the hadd is not applied. The commentary explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, even if the drinking occurred recently, once the smell dissipates, a confession is considered belated and cannot establish the hadd. However, Imam Shafi’i and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if the drinking happened within a month (the period during which the smell might still be detectable or the event considered recent), a confession or testimony is still acceptable, and the hadd must be applied. The practice of Umar (RA) is cited to show that the presence of smell was considered significant. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the presence of smell is a necessary condition for the validity of confession or testimony; without it, the matter becomes old and unreliable. The dispute highlights a difference in the definition of ‘recent’ and the weight given to physical evidence versus temporal proximity.

Key Terms
ذهاب رائحتها (dhahab ra'ihatiha): The disappearance of the smell of wine from the drinker's mouth.
زمان قریب (zaman qarib): A short period, defined as within one month in this context, within which the drinking is considered recent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He is subject to hadd only if he confesses within one month.
D) He is subject to hadd only if he has witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The presence of smell is a crucial indicator for hadd; without it, a belated confession is not accepted in the Hanafi school.

Hadd for Intoxication from Nabidh
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that intoxication from nabidh incurs hadd, identify the dalil from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and list the conditions for its application.

Core Idea
Any intoxicating drink, not just khamr, triggers the hadd punishment in Hanafi fiqh.

In this lesson we examine a clear ruling with proof: drinking an intoxicating amount of nabidh (a date-based beverage) carries the same hadd penalty as khamr. The source text presents the matn and then cites a hadith from Ibn Umar to establish the ruling. We will walk through the proof and the conditions that must be met for the punishment to be applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the matn: 'Whoever becomes intoxicated from nabidh is to be punished with hadd.' Note that the ruling is unconditional regarding the type of drink – it focuses on intoxication.
The term 'nabidh' covers any fruit-based infusion that can become intoxicating.
2
Examine the Dalil
The commentary cites a hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet (peace be upon him) flogged a man who was intoxicated from nabidh. This is a direct proof that the hadd applies to intoxicating nabidh.
The hadith is classified as ahad (single-chain) but its meaning is clear.
3
List the Conditions
From the commentary, three conditions emerge: (1) the person must be intoxicated, (2) the smell of the drink must be detectable, and (3) there must be witnesses (or confession). These mirror the conditions for khamr.
The Hanafi school does not require that the drink be specifically khamr; the effective cause ('illa) is intoxication.
4
Connect to Usul
The ruling is derived via qiyas (analogy) on khamr: the 'illa is intoxication (sukr), which is present in both. The hadith provides the direct precedent. This is a classic example of how a single hadith can expand a ruling beyond its literal text.
Note that the authority_weight is 'zahir riwayah' – the ruling is well-established in the school.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some other schools limit the hadd to khamr made from grapes, requiring a separate proof for nabidh. The Hanafi position is that any intoxicating drink suffices, based on the broader 'illa.
This difference shows the role of usul in expanding or limiting the scope of a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۸۹] (٣) ومن سكر ان النبذ حُدَّ .
(۲۴۸۹] (۳) کوئی نبیذ پینے سے نشہ ہو جائے تو حد لگائی جائے گی۔
حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله الا الله انتي برجل قد سكر من نبيذ فجلده (و) (دار قطنی ، کتاب الاشربة ص ۷۷ اج رابع نمبر ۲۶۵۴ رسنن للبیہقی ، باب ما جاء فی وجوب الحد علی من شرب خمرا او نبیذا اوسکراج ثامن ص ۵۴۳ نمبر ۱۷۴۹۹) اس حدیث سے
معلوم ہوا کہ نبیذ پیئے اور نشہ آ جائے اور بو کی حالت میں پکڑا جائے اور گواہ ہو تو حد لگے گی۔
(2489) And whoever becomes intoxicated from nabidh is to be punished with hadd. (Urdu commentary: Hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet flogged a man who was intoxicated from nabidh. So if one drinks nabidh, becomes intoxicated, is caught with the smell, and there are witnesses, hadd is applied.)
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that the hadd for drinking applies equally to nabidh (a drink made from dates or other fruits) if it causes intoxication. The matn explicitly states that becoming intoxicated from nabidh incurs the hadd. The commentary cites a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) flogged a man who was intoxicated from nabidh. The commentary adds the condition that the person must be caught while the smell is present and with witnesses, as in the case of khamr. Thus, nabidh is treated analogously to khamr with respect to the hadd punishment when it is intoxicating.

Key Terms
نبیذ (nabidh): A drink made from dates or other fruits that may cause intoxication if left to ferment.
سكر (sukr): Intoxication, loss of mental control due to consuming an intoxicant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hadd is wajib only if the nabidh is made from grapes.
B) Hadd is wajib if the person becomes intoxicated, and conditions of smell and witnesses/confession are met.
C) Hadd is not wajib because nabidh is not mentioned in the Quran.
D) Hadd is wajib automatically upon drinking any amount of nabidh, regardless of intoxication.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, intoxication (sukr) from any drink, including nabidh, triggers the hadd punishment, provided the conditions of detection and proof are satisfied.

No Hadd for Smelling or Vomiting Khamr
Ruling that simply smelling wine or vomiting it does not incur hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether hadd is incurred by the mere smell or vomiting of wine, and identify the excuses that prevent its application.

Core Idea
Smelling or vomiting wine does not prove wilful drinking; hadd requires clear evidence of voluntary intoxication.

This lesson explores a key detail in Hanafi hudud law: the presence of wine on a person's breath or in their vomit does not automatically trigger the hadd punishment. The ruling ensures that circumstantial signs do not replace the strict evidentiary requirements of witness testimony or confession. We will examine the conditions that excuse a person and why the Hanafi school treats these signs as insufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the act in question: the smell of wine on a person's breath or the act of vomiting wine. The ruling: no hadd is imposed.
The act itself is not punished; the punishment is for wilful drinking.
2
Distinguish the required evidence
Understand what would establish the hadd: either two male witnesses to the drinking or a voluntary confession by the offender.
Mere signs (smell, vomiting) are not sufficient.
3
List the valid excuses
Identify the excuses mentioned: coercion (the person was forced to drink) or medicinal use (the wine was consumed as medicine).
These excuses create uncertainty about wilful intoxication.
4
Understand the rationale
The core principle: hudud punishments require certainty (yaqeen). Circumstantial evidence does not provide that certainty.
This protects against wrongful punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۹۰] (٤) ولا حد على من وجد منه رائحة الخمر او من تقيأها.

Hadd for Drinking Nabidh Causing Intoxication
Ruling on flogging for intoxication from nabidh with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for intoxication from nabidh and identify the hadith proof used to extend the punishment to all intoxicants.

Core Idea
Any intoxicating drink, including nabidh, triggers the hadd punishment — the Prophet himself flogged a man for nabidh intoxication.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the hadd punishment for drinking nabidh (a date or fruit-based intoxicant). The passage cites a hadith where the Prophet flogged a man intoxicated from nabidh, establishing that the fixed punishment is not limited to grape wine. We will analyze the ruling, its proof, and the cross-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on nabidh intoxication
Identify the hukm: whoever becomes intoxicated from nabidh is liable for hadd (flogging).
2
Identify the hadith proof
Locate the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet flogged a man intoxicated from nabidh.
This is a hadith ahad, but accepted by Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The Prophet's action shows that hadd applies to any intoxicating drink, not just grape wine.
The illa (effective cause) is intoxication itself.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools restrict hadd to grape wine; Hanafis include all intoxicants.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that any intoxicating drink triggers hadd.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah and Al-Marghinani.

No Hadd for Smell or Vomit of Wine
Ruling with proof: no hadd for smell/vomit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for smell or vomiting of wine and identify the evidence and ikhtilaf surrounding it.

Core Idea
Mere smell or vomit of wine does not trigger hadd — evidence of voluntary consumption is required.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a person smells of wine or vomits wine, but there is no confession or witness. The Hanafi school clarifies that such circumstantial evidence does not automatically incur the hadd punishment. The ruling is grounded in a hadith and the principle of legal presumption (bara'ah asliyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being judged? Smelling of wine or vomiting wine. The ruling: no hadd is imposed solely based on these signs.
The hukm is that hadd is not obligatory (ghayr wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from A'mash (Bukhari and Muslim) about Ubaydullah ibn Mas'ud who did not flog until he established that the person had drunk.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but supports the principle.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows that even a companion like Ubaydullah required confirmation of drinking beyond smell. This indicates that smell alone is not sufficient evidence.
The proof is from the absence of action (he did not flog).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad and Imam Shafi'i consider that if the smell is recent (within a month) and there is a confession, hadd applies. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that smell alone is insufficient regardless.
This is both intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that smell or vomit alone do not necessitate hadd; direct evidence (two witnesses or confession) is required.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers this view.

The author explains that such evidence is ambiguous; the person might have consumed it for medicinal purposes or been forced. Therefore, without clear evidence (testimony or confession), no hadd is imposed. The footnote mentions that Umar once flogged a man based on smell, but that was likely because there was additional evidence or confession. The principle is that the hadd requires certainty, and smell or vomit alone do not provide that.

Conditions for Hadd on Intoxication: Source of Intoxication and Voluntariness
Condition: hadd only when intoxication from nabidh and voluntary drinking is confirmed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required before applying hadd for intoxication and explain why duress negates the hadd using Quranic and Hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking only applies when intoxication is from nabidh and consumption is voluntary; coercion is a complete defense.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text establishes two critical conditions before the hadd punishment for intoxication can be inflicted. It is not enough that a person is intoxicated; the specific intoxicant must be identified (nabidh or similar), and the drinking must have been voluntary. The author then provides evidence from the Quran and Sunnah to support the principle that duress (ikrah) removes criminal liability. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the hadd in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions stated in the ruling
Read the first line: 'The intoxicated person is not flogged until it is known that he became intoxicated from nabidh and drank it voluntarily.' List the two conditions explicitly.
These are the prerequisites for the hadd to be wajib.
2
Locate the proof for the principle of duress
The author cites Quran 24:33 and a hadith from Bukhari about Umar's judgment. Identify that both proofs establish that coercion removes sin and punishment.
The verse explicitly states that after compulsion, Allah is forgiving, indicating no sin remains.
3
Apply the principle via qiyas
The author draws an analogy between forced zina and forced drinking. Explain how the same principle—that duress negates hadd—extends from the case of forced zina to forced drinking.
This is a qiyas based on the same underlying cause (illah): lack of free will.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If a person is forced to drink, no hadd; if voluntary, hadd applies. This is the operative rule (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.
The passage mentions only nabidh, but the principle applies to all intoxicants by analogy.

The analogy (qiyas) is that just as coercion removes the hadd for zina, it also removes the hadd for drinking. Therefore, the hadd is only for voluntary consumption.

Hadd Postponed Until Intoxication Subsides
Ruling that flogging for intoxication is delayed until sobriety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying the hadd for drinking and explain the reason based on the hadith.

Core Idea
The hadd for intoxication is delayed until sobriety so the punishment serves as a deterrent.

In this lesson, we examine a specific procedural rule of hudud: the flogging for drinking is not applied while the offender is still intoxicated. The source text explains the rationale and provides a prophetic precedent. Understanding this ruling highlights how Islamic law balances justice and effectiveness in punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hukm
State the explicit ruling: the hadd flogging is not carried out until the intoxication wears off.
The text uses 'wa la yuhadd hatta yazula 'anhu al-sukr'.
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet (ﷺ) waited for a drunk man to become sober before ordering the flogging.
This is a sunnah ahad report.
3
Analyse the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action of waiting demonstrates that the flogging should be delayed until sobriety.
The Prophet's conduct (taqrir or fi'l) is a source of legislation.
4
Consider the Rationale
The commentary gives the reason: the purpose of hadd is deterrence (tanbih), which requires the offender to be conscious and understand why he is being punished.
This is a teleological (maqasid) reasoning.
5
Confirm the Ijma
The text indicates all Hanafis agree on this point; it is not a matter of ikhtilaf.
The ruling is considered standard (zahir al-riwayah).

The author supports this with a hadith where the Prophet waited for the man's intoxication to subside before ordering the flogging. This ruling ensures the legal procedure is both effective and just.

جلد (jald): Flogging, the physical punishment for hadd of drinking.

Conditions for Applying Hadd to a Drunkard
Ruling on conditions for hadd for drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for applying the hadd punishment for drinking and explain why compulsion negates the hadd, using the Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking requires voluntary intoxication from nabidh — mere smell or vomiting is insufficient.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses the specific conditions under which the hadd punishment for drinking can be applied. It distinguishes between voluntary and forced consumption, and requires that the intoxicant be specifically nabidh (date wine). The author also clarifies that sensory evidence like smell or vomiting is not enough; there must be a witness or confession linking the intoxication to voluntary nabidh consumption. Understanding these conditions prevents unjust punishments and highlights the Hanafi emphasis on procedural precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is drinking an intoxicant. The ruling is that hadd becomes wajib only if specific conditions are met.
Hadd is a fixed punishment; it is not automatically applied.
2
State the two conditions
First, the intoxicant must be nabidh (date wine). Second, the person must have drunk it voluntarily. Without both, no hadd.
The source states: 'until it is known that he became drunk from nabidh and drank it voluntarily.'
3
Examine the proof from Quran
Surah al-Nur 24:33 is cited: Allah forgives slave girls forced into prostitution, implying compulsion removes sin and punishment. By analogy, forced drinking also removes hadd.
Qiyas: compulsion in zina parallels compulsion in drinking.
4
Examine the proof from Hadith
Sahih al-Bukhari hadith 6949: 'Umar punished the slave who forced a woman but did not punish the forced woman. This directly shows that compulsion negates hadd.
The hadith is a clear precedent for the principle.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is do not require the drink to be specifically nabidh; any intoxicant suffices. Hanafis maintain the nabidh condition as a safeguard.
This distinction arises from different interpretations of the legal texts.

Source Text

باب حد الشرب
[٢٤٩١] (٥) ولا يحد السكران حتى يعلم أنه سكر من النبيذ وشربه طوعاً. لا يحد ببينة أو اعتراف. (سن للمبتی، باب من وجد منه ریح شراب أو هو سكران ج ثامن ص ٥٤٧ نمبر ١٧٥١٥) (٢) قلت لعطاء الريح وهو يعقل؟ قال لا أحد إلا ببينة أن الريح لتكون من الشراب الذي ليس به بأس وقال عمر بن دينار لا أحد في الريح (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الريح، ج تاسع ص ٢٣٠، نمبر ٧٠٣٧؛ مصنف ابن أبي شيبه ٩١ في رجل يوجد منه ريح الخمر ما عليه؟ ج خامس ص ٥٢٠ نمبر ٢٨٦٢٤) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بدبو کے ساتھ گواہ ہو تب حد لازم ہوگی۔ صرف بدبو آنے سے حد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور یہی حال قے کا ہے کہ جب تک قے کے بعد خوشی سے شراب پینے پر گواہ نہ ہو حد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔
[٢٤٩١] (٥) حد نہیں لگائی جائے گی نشہ والے کو یہاں تک کہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ نشہ نبیذ سے ہوا ہے اور خوشی سے پی ہے۔
نشہ آور چیز مجبور کر کے پلائی ہو تو اس سے حد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ خوشی سے پی ہو اور مست ہوا ہو تو حد لازم ہوگی۔
آیت میں ہے کہ مجبور کر کے زنا کیا ہو تو وہ معاف ہے۔ {ولا تكرهوا فتياتكم على البغاء إن أردن تحصنا لتبتغوا عرض الحياة الدنيا ومن يكرههن فإن الله من بعد إكراههن غفور رحيم} (آیت ٣٣ سورة النور ٢٤) اس آیت میں ہے کہ مجبور کر کے زنا کیا ہو تو اللہ ان باندیوں کو معاف کرنے والا ہے (٢) حدیث میں ہے کہ مستکرہ پر حد لازم نہیں ہے۔ عن صفية بنت أبي عبيد أخبرته أن عبدا من رقيق الإمارة وقع على وليدة من الخمس فاستكرهها حتى اقتضها، فجلده عمر الحد ونفاه ولم يجلد الوليدة من أجل أنه استكرهها (بخاری شریف، باب إذا استكرهت المرأة على الزنا فلا حد علیها ص ٠٢٧ نمبر ٦٩٤٩) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مجبور باندی پر حد نہیں لگائی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب یا نبیذ خوشی سے پی ہو تب حد لگے گی، مجبور کر کے پلایا ہو تو حد نہیں لگے گی۔
Chapter of Hadd for Drinking. [2491] (5) The drunkard is not punished until it is known that he became drunk from nabidh and drank it voluntarily. He is not punished without evidence or confession. (Sunan al-Mabti, chapter on he from whom the smell of wine or who is drunk is found, vol. 8, p. 547, no. 17515) (2) I said to 'Ata': the smell while he is sane? He said: I do not impose hadd without evidence, because the smell can be from a drink that has no problem. And 'Umar ibn Dinar said: I do not impose hadd for the smell. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter of smell, vol. 9, p. 230, no. 7037; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 91, about a man from whom the smell of wine is found, what is against him? vol. 5, p. 520, no. 28624) From this athar it is understood: if there is a witness along with the smell, then hadd becomes necessary. Only from smell, hadd does not become necessary. And the same is the case with vomiting: until after vomiting there is a witness that he drank wine voluntarily, hadd will not be necessary. [2491] (5) Hadd will not be applied to the drunkard until it is known that the intoxication was from nabidh and he drank it voluntarily. If an intoxicating substance is forced upon him, hadd is not necessary. If he drank voluntarily and became intoxicated, then hadd is necessary. There is a verse: 'And do not compel your slave girls to prostitution, if they desire chastity, to seek [thereby] the temporary benefits of worldly life. And whoever compels them, then indeed, Allah is [to them], after their compulsion, Forgiving and Merciful.' (Surah al-Nur 24:33) In this verse it is that if forced to commit zina, then Allah forgives those slave girls. (2) There is a hadith that the one compelled does not have hadd imposed. From Safiyya bint Abi 'Ubayd that a slave of the amirate fell upon a slave girl of the khums and forced her until he had intercourse with her, so 'Umar flogged him with the hadd and exiled him and did not flog the slave girl because he had forced her. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: if a woman is forced to commit zina, there is no hadd on her, p. 027, no. 6949) From this hadith it is that hadd was not imposed on the forced slave girl. From this it is understood that if wine or nabidh is drunk voluntarily, then hadd will be imposed; if it is forced, then hadd will not be imposed.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the conditions for applying the hadd punishment for drinking. It states two conditions: first, it must be established that the intoxication was from nabidh (date wine or similar alcoholic drink), and second, that the person drank it voluntarily. The text emphasizes that mere smell of alcohol or vomiting is not sufficient; there must be a witness or confession linking the intoxication to voluntary consumption of nabidh. It cites an athar from 'Ata' and 'Umar ibn Dinar that smell alone does not warrant hadd. Then it provides proofs from Quran and Sunnah to support that compulsion negates the hadd: the Quranic verse about forced slave girls and the hadith where 'Umar did not punish the slave girl who was forced. The commentary explains that the same principle applies to drinking: if forced, no hadd.

Key Terms
نبيذ (nabidh): An intoxicating drink made from dates or raisins; the specific type of alcohol for which hadd is established in Hanafi fiqh.
استكره (istukriha): To be compelled or forced against one's will; negates the hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required to establish the hadd for drinking?
A) The mere smell of alcohol from the person
B) Testimony that the person drank an intoxicating substance voluntarily
C) Confession without specifying the drink
D) A witness seeing the person intoxicated

Key Takeaway
Hadd for drinking requires proof that the person voluntarily became intoxicated from nabidh, and compulsion negates the punishment.

Timing of Hadd: Must Be After Intoxication Subsides
Ruling with prophetic proof on timing of hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school delays the hadd punishment for drinking until the person is sober, and cite the hadith evidence for this ruling.

Core Idea
Hadd for drinking punishes a sober person for having been drunk, not a drunk person.

This lesson addresses a crucial procedural aspect of the hadd punishment for drinking in Hanafi fiqh. While the punishment itself is prescribed for the act of drinking, the timing of its execution is governed by a distinct principle: the purpose of punishment (admonition) must be effective. A person in a state of intoxication cannot understand why he is being punished, so the hadd is deferred until sobriety. This ruling is firmly based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exact act is being ruled upon? It is the execution of the hadd punishment for the crime of drinking intoxicants. The ruling is that it must be delayed until the person becomes sober.
The hukm level of this delay is wajib, not merely recommended.
2
Understand the rationale (hikmah)
Why does the school prescribe this delay? Because the primary purpose of hadd is tazkir (admonition/reminder). A drunk person would not comprehend the reason for the punishment, nullifying its purpose.
This rationale is derived from the maqasid al-shari'ah.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet ﷺ was brought a drunk man. The narration explicitly states that the Prophet waited until the intoxication went away before ordering the flogging.
Reference: Sunan al-Bayhaqi, hadith 17525.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The specific phrase 'فلما ذهب سكره' (when his intoxication went away) shows that sobriety is a condition for executing the hadd. The Prophet's action demonstrates the ruling.
The dalala is qati (definitive) because the action is explicit.
5
Note the scholarly agreement
This ruling is mufta bihi and agreed upon by all major schools. There is no ikhtilaf on this procedural point.
See hanafi_position_box: cross_madhhab_status is muttafaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٤٩٢] (٦) اور نہیں حد لگے گی یہاں تک کہ نشہ اتر جائے۔ حد لگانے کا مقصد تنبیہ کرنا ہے اور نشہ کے عالم میں مارنے سے اس کو کچھ پتا نہیں چلے گا کہ مجھے کیوں مارا جا رہا ہے۔ اس لئے نشہ اترنے کے بعد حد لگائے (٢) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أتي برجل سكران أو قال نشوان فلما ذهب سكره أمر بجلده (سن للبیهقی، باب ما جاء في إقامته الحد في حال السكر أو حتى يذهب سكرو ج عامن ص ٥٥١ نمبر ١٧٥٢٥؛ مصنف ابن أبی هیت ٩٠ ما جاء في السكر أن متى يضرب إذا أصحا أو في حال سكره؟ ج خامس ص ٥١٩ نمبر ٢٨٦١٥) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نشہ اترنے کے بعد حد لگائے۔ السكر: نشہ۔
[2492] (6) And hadd will not be imposed until the intoxication disappears. The purpose of imposing hadd is to admonish, and in the state of intoxication, beating will not make him know why he is being beaten. Therefore, hadd is imposed after intoxication fades. (2) There is a hadith: From Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was brought a drunk man, or he said intoxicated, and when his intoxication went away, he ordered him to be flogged. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on imposing hadd in the state of intoxication or until intoxication goes, vol. 8, p. 551, no. 17525; Musannaf Ibn Abi Hayta, 90, chapter on intoxication: when should he be flogged, when sober or in his intoxication? vol. 5, p. 519, no. 28615) From this hadith it is understood that hadd is imposed after intoxication fades. al-sukr: intoxication.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling with prophetic proof that the hadd punishment for drinking is not administered while the person is intoxicated. Rather, it is postponed until he is sober. The reason given is that the purpose of punishment is admonition, and a drunk person would not understand why he is being punished. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar explicitly shows that the Prophet waited until the man's intoxication subsided before ordering the flogging. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
السكر (al-sukr): Intoxication; the state of being drunk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon being found intoxicated
B) After the person becomes sober
C) At the next court session
D) After the person confesses

Key Takeaway
The hadd for drinking must be delayed until the person is sober, based on the prophetic practice of waiting until intoxication subsides.

Hadd for Free Person: Eighty Lashes Distributed Over Body
Ruling on quantity and method of hadd for free person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd punishment for a free person drinking wine according to the Hanafi school, explain its historical development, and describe the prescribed method of administration.

Core Idea
Eighty lashes evenly distributed, avoiding face, head, and private parts – the Hanafi hadd for a free drinker.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the hadd (fixed punishment) for a free person who consumes wine or intoxicants. The text establishes the number of lashes as eighty and emphasises that the punishment must be administered by distributing strikes over the body, protecting sensitive areas. We will explore the proof from a hadith narrated by al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid and the athar of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, and understand why this method is prescribed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State the number of lashes for a free drinker according to the Hanafi school (eighty). Recognise that the ruling is derived from the actions of 'Umar, as recorded in a hadith, and from an athar of 'Ali.
The ruling is not based on a direct Quranic text but on Sunnah and ijtihad of the Companions.
2
Understand the historical change from forty to eighty
Note that during the Prophet's time and the rule of Abu Bakr and early 'Umar, the punishment was not fixed; later 'Umar set it at forty, then increased to eighty when people became defiant.
This shows that the punishment can be adjusted by the ruler based on circumstances, but the Hanafi school has settled on eighty for a free person.
3
Analyse the proof: the hadith of al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid
Read the hadith carefully. It mentions striking with hands, sandals, and garments initially, then 'Umar flogged forty, then eighty when people became wicked. The Hanafi school uses this to establish eighty as the fixed number.
The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim, so it is authentic (sahih).
4
Analyse the proof: the athar of 'Ali
The athar instructs to 'give each limb its right' and to avoid the face and private parts. This indicates distribution over the body and protection of sensitive areas.
The term 'al-madhakir' refers to male private parts, but Hanafis also include the head and face as areas to avoid.
5
Apply the method of administration
Conclude that the lashes must be distributed; striking the same spot repeatedly is not allowed. The face, head, and private parts are avoided because they are delicate.
This ensures the punishment is painful but not life-threatening or permanently disfiguring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٤٩٣] (٧) وحد الخمر والسكر في الحر ثمانون سوطا يفرق على بدنه كما ذكرنا في الزنا. شراب اور نشہ کی حد آزاد میں اسی کوڑے ہیں، اس کے بدن پر متفرق جگہ مارے جائے جیسا کہ میں نے زنا میں ذکر کیا۔ شراب اور نشہ کی حد پہلے چالیس کوڑے تھی بعد میں حضرت عمر کے زمانے میں لوگوں کی زیادتی کی وجہ سے اسی کوڑے کر دیئے گئے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن السائب بن يزيد قال كنا نؤتى بالشاريب على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وإمرة أبي بكر وصدرا من خلافة عمر فنقوم إليه بأيدينا ونعالنا وأرديتنا حتى كان آخر أمر عمر فجلد أربعين حتى إذا عتوا وفسقوا جلد ثمانين (بخاری شریف، باب الضرب بالجريد والنعال ص١٠٠٢ نمبر ٦٧٧٩؛ مسلم شریف، باب حد الخمر ص اے نمبر ١٧٠٦) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ آزاد کی حد شراب میں اسی کوڑے ہیں۔ اور جسم میں الگ الگ جگہ مارے جائے اس کے لئے اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن علي قال أتي برجل سكران أو في حد فقال اضرب واعط كل عضو حقه واتق الوجه والمذاكير (مصنف ابن أبي شيبه ١٠٠ ما جاء في الضرب في الحد ج خامس ص ٥٢٤ نمبر ٢٨٦٦٦؛ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب ضرب الحدود وصل ضرب النبي بالسوط؟ ج سابع ص٣٧٠ نمبر ١٣٥١٧) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سب عضو پر تھوڑے تھوڑے کوڑے مارے جائیں گے۔ البتہ چہرہ، سر اور شرمگاہ پر نہیں ماریں گے کیونکہ یہ نازک اعضاء ہیں۔
[2493] (7) The hadd for wine and intoxication in the free person is eighty lashes, distributed over his body as we mentioned in zina. The hadd for wine and intoxication was initially forty lashes, later in the time of 'Umar due to people's excess, it was increased to eighty. There is a hadith: From al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid, he said: We used to bring the drinker in the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and the rule of Abu Bakr and the early part of 'Umar's caliphate, and we would strike him with our hands, sandals, and cloaks, until the latter part of 'Umar's rule: he flogged forty. Then when they became defiant and wicked, he flogged eighty. (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter of striking with palm branches and sandals, p. 1002, no. 6779; Sahih Muslim, chapter of hadd of wine, p. e, no. 1706) From this hadith it is established that the hadd for a free person in wine is eighty lashes. And for striking on different parts of the body, an athar has passed: From 'Ali, he said: A drunk man was brought, or in a hadd case, so he said: Strike and give each limb its right, and avoid the face and the male organ. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 100, what is said about striking in hadd, vol. 5, p. 524, no. 28666; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter of striking of hudud and the Prophet's striking with the whip, vol. 7, p. 370, no. 13517) From this athar it is understood that a few lashes will be struck on each limb. However, the face, head, and private parts will not be struck because they are delicate organs.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This ruling states that the hadd for drinking for a free person is eighty lashes, and they must be distributed over the body, not concentrated on one area. The passage traces the historical development: initially, during the Prophet's time and early caliphate, the punishment was less formal (strikes with hands, etc.), then 'Umar set it at forty lashes, and later increased it to eighty when people became more defiant. The hadith of al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid is cited as proof. Additionally, the method of striking is derived from the athar of 'Ali, who instructed to give each limb its due and avoid the face and private parts. The commentary explains that this is because those are sensitive areas.

Key Terms
المذاكير (al-madhakir): The male private parts (plural of dhakar); areas to be avoided when flogging.
السكر (sukr): Intoxication, the state caused by consuming an intoxicant.
الحد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Shariah for certain crimes, such as drinking, theft, zina, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 40
B) 80
C) 100
D) It varies by judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hadd for a free drinker is eighty lashes, distributed over the body while avoiding the face, head, and private parts.

Hadd for a Slave: Forty Lashes
Ruling on hadd for slave for drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadd for a slave for drinking and identify the Quranic proof and analogy.

Core Idea
The Quranic half-punishment for slave women (Nisa 4:25) applies by analogy to all hudud, making a slave's hadd forty lashes.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling that the hadd for a slave who drinks wine is forty lashes, half of the free person's eighty. The ruling is derived from a direct Quranic text and supported by the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The hadd for a slave for drinking is forty lashes.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Quranic verse (Nisa 4:25) states that slave women receive half the punishment of free women for zina.
3
Understand the analogy
The principle of half punishment is extended to all hudud, including drinking, by qiyas.
4
Confirm with practice of the Companions
An athar from Ibn Shihab records that 'Umar, 'Uthman, and Ibn 'Umar flogged their slaves half the hadd of a free person for wine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢٤٩٤] (٨) فإن كان عبدا فحده أربعون. پس اگر غلام ہو تو اس کی حد چالیس کوڑے ہیں۔ پہلے کئی مرتبہ گزر چکا ہے کہ غلام اور باندی کی سزا آزاد سے آدھی ہے۔ اس لئے آزاد کی سزا اسی کوڑے ہیں تو غلام باندی کی سزا چالیس کوڑے ہوں گے۔ آیت ہے۔ {فإن أتين بفاحشة فعليهن نصف ما على المحصنات من العذاب} (آیت ٢٥ سورة النساء ٤) (٢) اثر میں ہے کہ غلام کو آزاد سے آدھی سزا دی۔ عن ابن شهاب أنه سئل عن جلد العبد في الخمر فقال بلغنا أن عليه نصف جلد الحر وأن عمر بن الخطاب وعثمان بن عفان وعبد الله بن عمر قد جلدوا عبيدهم نصف حد الحر في الخمر.
[2494] (8) And if he is a slave, his hadd is forty. So if he is a slave, his hadd is forty lashes. It has passed several times that the punishment of a slave and slave girl is half that of a free person. Therefore, the free person's punishment is eighty lashes, so the slave and slave girl's punishment will be forty lashes. There is a verse: 'But if they commit adultery, then for them is half the punishment for free [unmarried] women.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:25) (2) There is an athar that a slave is given half the punishment of a free person. From Ibn Shihab that he was asked about flogging a slave in wine, so he said: It has reached us that upon him is half the flogging of a free person, and that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, and 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar flogged their slaves half the hadd of a free person in wine.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This ruling states that the hadd for a slave (male or female) for drinking is forty lashes, half of the free person's eighty. The proof is the Quranic verse that establishes half punishment for slave women in the case of zina, and by analogy (qiyas) this principle applies to all hudud. The commentary cites an athar from Ibn Shihab confirming that the Companions implemented half the flogging for slaves in the case of wine drinking.

Key Terms
المحصنات (al-muhsanat): Free, chaste women; in the verse, it refers to free women who are not slaves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 40 lashes

D) 100 lashes

Key Takeaway
The hadd for a slave for drinking is forty lashes, derived from the Quranic principle of half punishment for slaves.

Retraction of Confession Drops the Hadd for Drinking
Ruling with hadith proof on retraction of confession for drinking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of confession for drinking and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
A retracted confession drops the hadd for drinking—the door to repentance remains open.

This lesson examines a critical principle in Hanafi hudud law: the effect of retracting a confession before the penalty is carried out. While a confession may establish the hadd, the school holds that retraction nullifies it, based on a prophetic hadith encouraging the possibility of repentance. This ruling highlights the Hanafi preference for averting punishments whenever doubt or mercy can be invoked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? (confession to drinking, then retraction) What is the ruling? (hadd is dropped)
The ruling is a legal outcome, not a classification of an act.
2
Locate the dalil
Which proof is cited? (hadith: 'Why did you not leave him...')
Hadith is from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? (encouragement to leave him implies dropping punishment upon retraction)
The phrase 'hala taraktumuh' indicates a desire to leave him unpunished.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? (some schools may not accept retraction)
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why does Hanafi school adopt this? (based on hadith and analogy with zina)
The ruling is mufta bihi.

[۲۴۹۵] (۹) ومن اقر بشرب الخمر والسكر ثم رجع لم يُحد. کسی نے شراب پینے کا اقرار کیا یا نشہ پینے کا اقرار کیا پھر بعد میں اس سے پھر گیا تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ پہلے زنا کی حد کے سلسلے میں گزر چکا ہے کہ رجوع کر جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے ۔ هلا تركتموه لعله ان يتوب فيتوب الله عليه (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب رجم ما عزین مالک من ۲۶۰ نمبر ۴۴۱۹ ر ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی در والحد من المعترف اذا رجع ص ۲۶۴ نمبر ۱۴۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حد شرب سے رجوع کر جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
Whoever confesses to drinking wine or an intoxicant and then retracts, he is not punished with hadd. If someone confesses to drinking wine or an intoxicant and then later retracts, the hadd is dropped. It has already passed in the chapter on zinā that if he retracts, the hadd is dropped. The hadith portion is: 'Why did you not leave him, perhaps he would repent and Allah would forgive him.' (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is understood that if he retracts from the hadd of drinking, the hadd is dropped.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding retraction of confession for the hadd of drinking. The author first states the ruling: if a person confesses to drinking wine or any intoxicant and then retracts, the hadd penalty is not carried out. The commentary explains that retraction nullifies the hadd, similar to the ruling for zinā. The proof is a portion of a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'Why did you not leave him, perhaps he would repent and Allah would forgive him.' This indicates that retraction before execution of the penalty should bring forgiveness. Thus, in Hanafi fiqh, if the confessor retracts, the hadd is dropped.

Key Terms
حد الشرب (hadd al-shurb): The fixed penalty (hadd) for consuming alcohol or intoxicants.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession, admitting to committing an offense in front of a judge.
رجوع (rujū‘): Retraction of a confession before the penalty is carried out.

Proof of Hadd of Drinking: Witnesses and Confession
Ruling on proof of drinking hadd with witnesses or confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on proof of the hadd of drinking, identify the evidence for witnesses and confession, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of confessions.

Core Idea
Two male witnesses or one confession establishes the hadd of drinking.

This passage establishes the evidentiary requirements for the hadd of drinking. It explains that two male witnesses or a single confession suffice, referencing Quranic verses and prophetic practices. A disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad against Abu Yusuf on the number of confessions is also presented.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modes of proof
The passage states that the hadd of drinking is proven by either the testimony of two male witnesses or a single confession. Note the contrast with zinā, which requires four witnesses.
The number of witnesses for zinā is explicitly given in Quran 24:4.
2
Analyze the dalil for witnesses
The author cites Quran 2:282 (transactions requiring two men or one man and two women) and the practice of Ali (RA) in theft cases, showing that two men suffice. Also, the effect of Az-Zuhri prohibits women's testimony in hudud.
The verse is about transactions; hudud are included by analogy (qiyas).
3
Analyze the dalil for confession
The hadith of the thief who confessed once and was punished by the Prophet (PBUH) is presented. This serves as the primary evidence that a single confession is sufficient for hadd.
The hadith is reported by Abu Hurayrah (RA) and recorded in several collections.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that two confessions are required, analogizing from the effect of Ali (RA) where a thief confessed twice before his hand was cut. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) disagree, considering the hadith of the single confession as stronger evidence.
Abu Yusuf's view is a valid ikhtilaf within the school, but it is not the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that one confession suffices, as held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. This is supported by the clear hadith and is the majority view.
For fatwa, a single confession is accepted; Abu Yusuf's view is considered weak (marjuh).
