سارق مرتين فقطع يده وعلقها في عنقه (ب) (سن بیہقی ، باب ماجاء فی تعلیق اليد في عنق السارق ج علا من ص ۴۷۸ نمبر ۱۷۲۷۴) اس اثر میں دو مرتبہ چوری کا اقرار کیا تب حد سرقہ ثابت کیا جس سے پتا چلا کہ حد شرب میں بھی دو مرتبہ اقرار کرے تب حد شرب ثابت ہوگی۔
The hadd of drinking is established by the testimony of two witnesses or by a single confession. For establishing zinā, four witnesses were required because of the verse, so four witnesses were made necessary there. But for the hadd of drinking, the verse does not require four witnesses, so it returns to the original principle. In general, things are established by two witnesses, so the hadd of drinking is established by two witnesses. The verse says: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men, and if there are not two men, then one man and two women from among those you approve as witnesses.' This verse pertains to transactions: two men or one man and two women. Thus, two men are sufficient to establish the hadd of drinking. There is an effect: 'Two men came to Ali ibn Abi Talib with a man and testified against him for theft, so he cut off his hand.' This effect shows that the hand was cut based on the testimony of two men. And the testimony of women is not sufficient in hudud because it is prohibited in another effect: 'Az-Zuhri said: The sunnah from the Messenger of Allah and the two caliphs after him is that the testimony of women is not valid in hudud.' From this it is understood that the testimony of women is not permissible in hudud. Therefore, the hadd of drinking is only established by two men. Also, the hadd of drinking or theft is established by a single confession. Its proof is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: 'A thief came to the Messenger of Allah and confessed to stealing a cloak...' In this hadith, the thief confessed once and said 'Yes' and the hadd was imposed. From this it is understood that the hadd of drinking is also established by a single confession. Imam Abu Yusuf says that two confessions are required for the hadd of drinking. (1) Just as two witnesses are necessary for proof, similarly two confessions should be made. (2) There is proof in an effect: 'I saw Ali that a thief confessed twice before him, so he cut off his hand and hung it around his neck.' In this effect, a thief confessed twice and the hadd of theft was established, which indicates that for the hadd of drinking also, two confessions are required.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and includes an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author states that the hadd for drinking is established by two male witnesses or a single confession. The proof for witnesses is the verse on transactions (2:282) and the practice of Ali (RA) in theft cases. For confession, the hadith of the thief who confessed once suffices. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring two confessions, analogizing from theft where a double confession is reported. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that one confession is sufficient, as held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony in court; for hudud, two male witnesses are required.
اقرار (iqrār): Confession of the accused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two
C) One
D) Confession is not accepted

Key Takeaway
The hadd of drinking is proven by two male witnesses or a single confession; the mufta bihi is one confession, though Abu Yusuf required two.

Women's Testimony and Confessions in Hudud
Intra-Hanafi dispute on confessions and ruling on women's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's testimony in hudud and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the number of confessions required for establishing hadd punishments.

Core Idea
Women's testimony is rejected in hudud; for hadd, one confession suffices per Abu Hanifa, but two per Abu Yusuf.

This passage from a Hanafi manual addresses two critical procedural rules in hudud (fixed punishments): the admissibility of women's testimony and the number of confessions needed to establish guilt. While the ruling on women's testimony is settled within the school, the number of confessions required for hadd – specifically for drinking (shurb) and theft (sariqa) – reveals an important intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding these details is essential for correctly applying hudud punishments in a court setting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling on women's testimony
Locate the statement that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, even when accompanied by men. Note the source: the sunnah from the Prophet and the two caliphs.
This ruling is presented as an established sunnah, not subject to dispute within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the dispute over number of confessions
Read the passage that discusses the number of confessions required for hadd. Abu Hanifa's position is supported by a hadith where a thief confessed once. Abu Yusuf's position is supported by an athar from Ali where a thief confessed twice, and by analogy to two witnesses.
The dispute is limited to the number of confessions, not the validity of confession as a proof.
3
Examine the proofs for each position
For Abu Hanifa: the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the thief said 'yes' once. For Abu Yusuf: the athar of Ali where the thief confessed twice; also the qiyas linking two confessions to two witnesses.
Both proofs are considered valid transmissions within the Hanafi tradition.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a person confesses once to drinking, Abu Hanifa says the hadd is applied; Abu Yusuf says it is not until a second confession occurs. This directly affects judicial procedure.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is not specified in this passage, but many later works prefer Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Revisit the ruling on women's testimony and its rationale
The passage returns to women's testimony, citing an athar from al-Zuhri that the sunnah has continued that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. The reasoning is that hudud require the highest level of proof.
Women's testimony is accepted in other areas like financial transactions, but not in hudud or qisas.

ایک مرتبہ اقرار سے بھی حد شرب یا حد سرقہ ثابت ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی مريرة قال اتى رسول الله الله بسارق سرق شملة فقالوا ان هذا سرق فقال لا اخاله سرق فقال بلى يارسول الله ! قد سرقت قال اذهبوا به فاقطعوه ثم احسموه ثم التونى به (الف) ( سنن للمبتی ، باب ما جاء فی الاقرار بالسرقة والرجوع عندج عامن ص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۷۲۷۵ اردار قطنی کتاب الحدودج ثالث ص ۸۲ نمبر ۳۱۳۹ رنسائی شریف ، باب تلقین السارق ص ۶۷۲ نمبر (۱۳۸۸) اس حدیث میں ایک مرتبہ اقرار کیا اور قال بلی کہا جس پر حد سرقہ لازم کر دی گئی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حد شرب بھی ایک مرتبہ اقرار کرنے سے ثابت ہو جائے گی۔
امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دو مرتبہ اقرار کرے تب حد شرب ثابت ہوگی۔ (1) جس طرح ثبوت کے لئے دو گواہ ضروری ہیں اسی طرح دو مرتبہ اقرار بھی ہو (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ رایت علیا اقر عندہ سارق مرتين فقطع يده وعلقها في عنقه (ب) (سن بیہقی ، باب ماجاء فی تعلیق اليد في عنق السارق ج علا من ص ۴۷۸ نمبر ۱۷۲۷۴) اس اثر میں دو مرتبہ چوری کا اقرار کیا تب حد سرقہ ثابت کیا جس سے پتا چلا کہ حد شرب میں بھی دو مرتبہ اقرار کرے تب حد شرب ثابت ہوگی۔
۲۴۹۷] (۱۱) اور حدود میں عورتوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی مردوں کے ساتھ۔ پہلے اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن الزهري قال مضت السنة من رسول الله له والخليفتين من بعده الا تجوز شهادة النساء في الحدود (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبت نمبر ۲۸۷۰۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق نمبر ۱۵۴۱۰) اس اثر سے ثابت ہوا کہ حدود میں عورتوں کی گواہی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے صرف دو مرد کی گواہی چاہئے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابو ہریرہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور کے سامنے ایک چور لایا گیا جس نے چادر چرائی تھی تو لوگوں نے کہا اس نے چرایا ہے تو آپ نے فرمایا میں سمجھتا ہوں کہ چرایا نہیں ہے۔ لوگوں نے کہا کیوں نہیں اے اللہ کے رسول! انہوں نے چرایا ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا اس کو لے جاؤ اس کا ہاتھ کا ٹو پھر اس کو داغ دو پھر میرے پاس لاؤ (ب ) میں نے حضرت علی کو دیکھا کہ ان کے پاس چور نے دومرتبہ اقرار کیا تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا اور اس کو اس کی گردن میں لٹکا دیا (ج) حضرت زہری نے فرمایا حضیر کے زمانے اور دونوں خلیفہ کے زمانے سے اور ان کے بعد سے یہ سنت جاری ہے کہ عورتوں کی گواہی حدود میں جائز نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the punishment for drinking. 2497] And the testimony of women is not accepted in it along with men. With one confession also, the hadd punishment for drinking or the hadd punishment for theft is established. Its evidence is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah was brought a thief who had stolen a cloak. They said, 'This one stole.' He said, 'I do not think he stole.' He said, 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah, I stole.' He said, 'Take him away, cut off his hand, then cauterize it, then bring him to me.' (a) (Sunan al-Mabti, Chapter on Confession of Theft and Retraction...). In this hadith, he confessed once and said 'yes' (bala), upon which the hadd punishment for theft was imposed. From this it is understood that the hadd punishment for drinking will also be established by a single confession. Imam Abu Yusuf says that he should confess twice, then the hadd punishment for drinking will be established. (1) Just as two witnesses are necessary for proof, likewise two confessions are needed. (2) There is proof for this in the athar: 'I saw Ali that a thief confessed before him twice, so he cut off his hand and hung it around his neck.' (b) (Sunan Bayhaqi, Chapter on Hanging the Hand of the Thief...). In this athar, the thief confessed twice, then the hadd punishment for theft was established, so it becomes clear that for the hadd punishment for drinking as well, one should confess twice, then it will be established. 2497] (11) And in the hudud, the testimony of women is not accepted along with men. An athar has passed earlier. From al-Zuhri, he said: The sunnah has continued from the Messenger of Allah and the two caliphs after him that the testimony of women is not permissible in the hudud. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...). This athar establishes that women's testimony is not considered in hudud. Therefore, only two men's testimony is required. Footnote: (a) Abu Hurairah says: A thief was brought before the Prophet who had stolen a cloak. The people said he stole. The Prophet said, 'I think he did not steal.' They said, 'Why not, O Messenger of Allah, he stole.' He said, 'Take him away, cut off his hand, then cauterize it, then bring him to me.' (b) I saw Ali that a thief confessed twice before him, so he cut off his hand and hung it around his neck. (c) Zuhri said: From the time of the Prophet and the two caliphs after him and after them, this sunnah continues that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of confessions required for establishing hadd punishments, particularly for drinking (shurb) and theft (sariqa), along with the general ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud. The author begins by stating the ruling that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud (punishments prescribed by Allah). The commentary then discusses how a hadd punishment can be established: by one confession according to the apparent position of Imam Abu Hanifa, supported by the hadith of the thief who confessed once and was punished. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that two confessions are required, analogizing to the need for two witnesses. He cites an athar from Ali where a thief confessed twice. The text then returns to the original ruling on women's testimony, providing an athar from al-Zuhri that the sunnah has continued that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud. Therefore, only two male witnesses are accepted. Footnotes provide the Arabic text and translation of these proofs.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for certain crimes (e.g., drinking, theft, zina).
شهادة النساء (shahadat al-nisa): Testimony of women as witnesses in court; in hudud, it is not accepted even with men.
اقرار (iqrar): Confession of guilt; a basis for establishing hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, how many confessions are required for the hadd punishment for drinking (shurb) to be established?
A) One confession
B) Two confessions
C) Four confessions
D) No confession is needed; only witnesses

Key Takeaway
Women's testimony is not accepted in hudud; for establishing hadd, Abu Hanifa requires one confession while Abu Yusuf requires two, with the mufta bihi generally being Abu Hanifa's view.

Hadd al-Qadhf: Definition and Proofs
Defines hadd al-qadhf, provides its Quranic and hadith evidence, and states the condition of explicit accusation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hadd al-qadhf, cite its Quranic and hadith proofs, and identify the condition of explicit accusation.

Core Idea
False accusation of zina carries eighty lashes and forever bars testimony.

The hadd punishment for qadhf is a severe penalty that protects the honour of chaste individuals. In this lesson, we examine the definition of qadhf, its evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and the crucial condition that the accusation must be explicit. This ensures that only clear cases of defamation are subject to the hadd, while ambiguous remarks may be handled differently.

Guided Path
1
Define qadhf legally
Identify the act of qadhf as accusing a chaste (muhsan) person of zina with explicit words, which triggers a fixed punishment (hadd).
The term 'muhsan' refers to a free, Muslim, adult who has never committed zina.
2
Identify the primary proof
Cite the Quranic verse (Surah an-Nur 24:23) that commands flogging eighty lashes and perpetual rejection of testimony for those who accuse chaste women without four witnesses.
The imperative 'fajliduhum' indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
3
Identify the secondary proof
Refer to the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet (peace be upon him) applied the hadd to two men and a woman after the incident of slander.
This hadith confirms the application of the Quranic ruling.
4
Recognize the condition of explicit accusation
Understand that the hadd applies only when the accusation uses an explicit word for zina (sarih), not by implication (kinayah).
Citing the athar of Qasim ibn Muhammad and the hadith of the Bedouin who used implication and was not punished.
5
Summarize the conditions for hadd to apply
List the essential conditions: accused must be muhsan, accusation explicit, accuser free and Muslim, no four witnesses, and maqdhuuf demands hadd.
If any condition is missing, hadd is not applied; tazir may be used instead.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حد القذف
۲۴۹۸] ( ا ) اذا قذف الرجل رجلا محصنا او امرأة محصنة بـصـريح الزنا وطالب به الحد فانه يحد ثمانين جلدة ولوکان قاذفا حرا مسلما
ضروری نوں کسی پاکدامن مرد یا عورت پر تہمت ڈالے کہ تم نے زنا کرایا ہے یا کیا ہے اور اس کو چار گواہوں سے ثابت نہ کر سکے اور جس پر تہمت ڈالی ہے وہ حد کا مطالبہ کرے تو اس پر حد لگے گی۔ اس حد کو حد قذف کہتے ہیں۔ قذف کا معنی ہے زنا کی تہمت لگانا۔ ثبوت اس آیت میں ہے۔ والذين یرمون المحصنات ثم لم يأتو باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا واولئک هم الفاسقون (الف) ( آیت سورۃ النور ۲۳) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کسی محصنہ عورت پر زنا کی تہمت لگائے پھر چار گواہ نہ لا سکے تو اس کو اسی کوڑے مارو اور کبھی اس کی گواہی قبول نہ کرو (۲) حدیث میں ہے ۔ عن عائشة قالت لما نزل عذرى قام النبي الله على المنبر فذكر ذلك وتلا تعنى القرآن ، فلما نزل من المنبر امر بالرجلين والمرأة فضر بواحدهم (ب)(ابوداؤد شریف، باب في حد القذف ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۴۳۷۴ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب حد القذف ص ۳۶۹ نمبر ۲۵۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حد قذف لگائی جا سکتی ہے۔ [۲۴۹۸] (۱) اگر زنا کی تہمت لگائی کسی آدمی نے محصن مرد کو یا محصنہ عورت کو صریح زنا کی اور مقذوف نے حد کا مطالبہ کیا تو حاکم اس کو اسی کوڑے لگا ئیں گے اگر وہ آزاد ہو۔
کسی آدمی نے محسن مرد یا محصنہ عورت کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی اور اشارہ کنایہ سے نہیں بلکہ زنا کی صریح لفظ سے تہمت لگائی اور جس کو تہمت لگائی اس نے حد کا مطالبہ کیا۔ پس اگر تہمت لگانے والا آزاد ہے تو حاکم اس کو اسی کوڑے حد قذف لگائے۔ اوپر کی آیت میں موجود ہے کہ محصن مرد یا محصن عورت کو تہمت لگائے تو حد قذف لگے گی۔ اور محسن کس کو کہتے ہیں اس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے اور مسئلہ نمبر ۵ میں دوبارہ آرہی ہے۔ زنا کے صریح لفظ سے تہمت لگائے تب حد لگے گی۔
اثر میں ہے۔ عن القاسم بن محمد قال ما كنا نرى الجلد الا في القذف البين والنفى البين (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب من قال لاحد الا فی القذف الصریح ج ثامن ص ۲۴۰ نمبر ۱۷۱۴۵ار مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب التعریض ج سابع ص ۴۲۰ نمبر ۱ ۱۳۷۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک صریح نہ کہے حد لازم نہیں ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں اعرابی نے اشارہ سے بیوی پر تہمت لگائی تو آپ نے حد نہیں لگائی۔
حاشیہ : (الف) جو لوگ پاکدامن عورتوں پر تہمت لگاتے ہیں پھر چار گواہ نہیں لا سکتے تو ان کو اسی کوڑے مارو اور کبھی بھی ان کی گواہی قبول نہ کرو، وہ فاسق ہیں (ب) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں جب میرے عذر کے متعلق آیتیں اتریں تو حضور منبر پر کھڑے ہوئے اور اس کا تذکرہ کیا اور قرآن کی آیتیں پڑھیں ۔ پس جب منبر سے اترے تو دومرد اور ایک عورت کے بارے میں حکم دیا اور ان کو حد قذف لگائی (ج) حضرت قاسم بن محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو ڈانگا نا نہیں مناسب سمجھتے مگر صریح تہمت میں یا صریح بچے کے انکار میں۔
Chapter of the punishment for false accusation (qadhf). 2498] (a) When a man accuses a muhsan man or a muhsana woman with explicit zina and demands the punishment, then he is punished with eighty lashes if the accuser is a free Muslim. Essentials: If someone accuses a chaste man or woman of zina, saying 'you committed zina,' and cannot prove it with four witnesses, and the accused demands the punishment, then the punishment is applied. This punishment is called hadd al-qadhf. The meaning of qadhf is to accuse of zina. The proof is in this verse: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and do not accept their testimony ever, and those are the transgressors.' (a) (Surah an-Nur verse 23). In this verse, if someone accuses a muhsana woman of zina and cannot bring four witnesses, then flog him eighty lashes and never accept his testimony. (2) In the hadith: From Aisha, she said: When my innocence was revealed, the Prophet stood on the pulpit and mentioned that and recited the Quran, and when he descended, he ordered regarding two men and a woman and they were flogged. (b) (Abu Dawood, Sunan, Bab fi Hadd al-Qadhf...). From this hadith, it is understood that hadd al-qadhf can be applied. [2498] (1) If a person accuses a muhsan man or a muhsana woman of explicit zina, and the maqdhuuf (accused) demands the hadd, then the judge will flog him eighty lashes if he is free. A person accuses a muhsan man or a muhsana woman of zina with an explicit word for zina, not by suggestion or implication, and the accused demands the hadd. Then if the accuser is free, the judge will flog him eighty lashes for hadd al-qadhf. The verse above mentions that if a muhsan man or woman is accused, then hadd al-qadhf applies. The definition of muhsan has passed earlier and will come again in issue number 5. The hadd applies only when the accusation is with an explicit word for zina. In the athar: From al-Qasim ibn Muhammad, he said: We only considered flogging in the case of explicit qadhf and explicit denial of lineage. (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Whoever Says 'Except in Explicit Qadhf'...). From this athar, it is understood that as long as one does not say explicitly, the hadd does not apply. (2) In the hadith, a Bedouin accused his wife by implication, and the Prophet did not apply hadd. Footnote: (a) Those who accuse chaste women and then cannot bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony; they are transgressors. (b) Aisha said: When the verses about my innocence were revealed, the Prophet stood on the pulpit, mentioned that, and recited the Quran. When he descended, he ordered regarding two men and a woman and applied hadd al-qadhf to them. (c) Qasim ibn Muhammad said: We do not consider flogging appropriate except in explicit accusation or explicit denial of a child.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of zina). The author defines qadhf as accusing a chaste (muhsan) person of zina, and the punishment is eighty lashes for a free accuser who cannot produce four witnesses. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse (Surah an-Nur 24:23), which commands flogging and perpetual rejection of testimony. A hadith from Aisha illustrates the application when the Prophet flogged two men and a woman. The text then elaborates that the accusation must be explicit (sarih) – using a clear word for zina – and not by implication (kinayah). An athar from Qasim ibn Muhammad confirms that flogging only occurs in explicit cases. The condition of the accused being muhsan is mention but its details are referenced elsewhere. The passage also notes that the hadd applies only when the maqdhuuf demands it. The footnotes provide the Arabic text and translation of the Quranic verse, the hadith from Aisha, and the athar from Qasim.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person (muhsan) of zina, which triggers the hadd punishment of eighty lashes.
محصن (muhsan): A person who is free, Muslim, adult, and has never committed zina (chaste).
صريح الزنا (sarih al-zina): Explicit wording for the act of zina; necessary for hadd al-qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Eighty lashes and perpetual rejection of testimony

Key Takeaway
Hadd al-qadhf is eighty lashes for a free Muslim who explicitly accuses a muhsan of zina without four witnesses, and the accusation must be explicit with the word zina.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate

Punishment for Slander (Qadhf) of a Muhsan Person
Defines qadhf, its conditions, and the 80-lash punishment for a free person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of qadhf for a free person, identify its three conditions (muhsan, explicit accusation, demand), and cite the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Slandering a chaste person with explicit zina incurs 80 lashes — a fixed Quranic penalty.

In this lesson, we examine the crime of qadhf — falsely accusing a chaste (muhsan) person of fornication or adultery. The Quran establishes a severe but measured response: 80 lashes and perpetual disqualification from testimony. However, this punishment is not automatic; it hinges on specific conditions, including the explicit nature of the accusation and the victim's demand for retribution. Understanding these conditions ensures the penalty is applied justly and only where intended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qadhf: accusing a muhsan (chaste, free, adult Muslim) person of zina using an explicit word. The ruling for a free slanderer is 80 lashes, imposed by the judge when the slandered demands it.
The ruling comes from the matn: 'if a man slanders a muhsan man or woman with explicit zina... the judge flogs him eighty lashes if he is free.'
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic proof is Surah An-Nur 24:23, which commands flogging of those who accuse chaste women and fail to bring four witnesses. The imperative 'fajliduhum' indicates obligation, and 'thamanina jaldah' sets the exact number.
The verse also adds permanent rejection of testimony and labels them as wicked.
3
Identify the conditions for the hadd to apply
Three conditions are required: (1) The accused (the slandered person) must be muhsan — free, adult, Muslim, and chaste (never convicted of zina). (2) The accusation must be explicit (sarih) using a direct word for zina; innuendo or indirect speech does not suffice. (3) The slandered person must demand the punishment; it is a personal right that can be forgiven like blood money.
The condition of explicit accusation is supported by the athar of Qasim ibn Muhammad and the incident of the Bedouin who implied but did not state zina.
4
Note procedural requirement of demand
The slandered must actively demand the hadd. If they forgive the slanderer, the punishment lapses. This mirrors the right of the victim in cases of bodily harm (diyah).
This underscores that qadhf involves a personal right (haqq adami) alongside a public right (haqq Allah).

Source Text

کسی آدمی نے محسن مرد یا محصنہ عورت کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی اور اشارہ کنایہ سے نہیں بلکہ زنا کی صریح لفظ سے تہمت لگائی اور جس کو تہمت لگائی اس نے حد کا مطالبہ کیا۔ پس اگر تہمت لگانے والا آزاد ہے تو حاکم اس کو اسی کوڑے حد قذف لگائے۔ اوپر کی آیت میں موجود ہے کہ محصن مرد یا محصن عورت کو تہمت لگائے تو حد قذف لگے گی۔ اور محسن کس کو کہتے ہیں اس کی تفصیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے اور مسئلہ نمبر ۵ میں دوبارہ آرہی ہے۔ زنا کے صریح لفظ سے تہمت لگائے تب حد لگے گی۔
للبیہقی ، باب
اثر میں ہے۔ عن القاسم بن محمد قال ما كنا نرى الجلد الا في القذف البين والنفى البين (ج) (سنن . من قال لاحد الا فی القذف الصریح ج ثامن ص ۲۴۰ نمبر ۱۷۱۴۵ار مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب التعریض ج سابع ص ۴۲۰ نمبر ۱ ۱۳۷۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک صریح نہ کہے حد لازم نہیں ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں اعرابی نے اشارہ سے بیوی پر تہمت لگائی تو آپ نے حد نہیں
حاشیہ : (الف) جو لوگ پاکدامن عورتوں پر تہمت لگاتے ہیں پھر چار گواہ نہیں لا سکتے تو ان کو اسی کوڑے مارو اور کبھی بھی ان کی گواہی قبول نہ کرو، وہ فاسق ہیں (ب) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں جب میرے عذر کے متعلق آیتیں اتریں تو حضور منبر پر کھڑے ہوئے اور اس کا تذکرہ کیا اور قرآن کی آیتیں پڑھیں ۔ پس جب منبر سے اترے تو دومرد اور ایک عورت کے بارے میں حکم دیا اور ان کو حد قذف لگائی (ج) حضرت قاسم بن محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو ڈانگا نا نہیں مناسب سمجھتے مگر صریح تہمت میں یا صریح بچے کے انکار میں۔

المقذوف بالحد حَدَّه الحاكم ثمانين سوطا ان كان حرا 
لمبی حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة ان رسول الله الا الله جاءه اعرابی فقال يا رسول الله الله ان امرأتی ولدت غلاما اسود فقال هل لك من ابل؟ الخ (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب ماجاء فی التعریض ص ۱۰۱۲ نمبر ۶۸۴۷ مسلم شریف کتاب اللعان ص ۴۸۸ نمبر ۱۵۰۰) اس حدیث میں اشارہ سے بیوی پر تہمت لگائی اس لئے آپ نے اس پر حد قذف نہیں لگائی۔ مقذوف مطالبہ کرے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ اس کا حق ہے۔ اگر وہ معاف کر دے تو معاف ہو جائے گا جیسے دیت میں وارث معاف کر دے تو معاف ہو جائے گا۔ اسی کوڑے کی وجہ خود آیت میں موجود ہے۔ ثمانين جلدة ( آیت ۴ سورۃ النور ۲۴)
Chapter of Punishment for Slander. [2498] (1) When a man slanders a muhsan man or a muhsan woman with explicit zina, and the slandered demands the punishment, the judge flogs him eighty lashes if he is free. Necessary: if someone accuses a chaste man or woman of zina and cannot prove it with four witnesses, and the accused demands punishment, then punishment is imposed. This punishment is called hadd al-qadhf. Qadhf means accusing of zina. Proof is in this verse: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and they are the wicked.' (Surah An-Nur: 23). (2) Hadith: from Aisha: when my innocence was revealed, the Prophet stood on the pulpit and recited Quran, then ordered two men and a woman to be flogged. (Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah). [2498] (1) If a man accuses a muhsan man or woman with explicit zina and the slandered demands punishment, the judge flogs him eighty lashes if he is free. Explanation: he accuses with explicit word, not innuendo. The verse mentions muhsan. The definition of muhsan has passed. Only explicit accusation incurs hadd. There is an athar from Qasim ibn Muhammad: we only consider flogging for explicit slander and explicit disavowal of paternity. (Bayhaqi, Abdurrazzaq). Hadith: a Bedouin insinuated against his wife but the Prophet did not impose hadd. Footnotes: (a) Quran verse translation. (b) Hadith translation. (c) Athar translation. The slandered must demand punishment because it is his right; he can forgive it like blood money. The eighty lashes are from the verse 'eighty lashes'. (Surah An-Nur: 4).
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the punishment of slander (qadhf). The author first states the ruling in the matn: if a free person slanders a muhsan (chaste, free, Muslim adult) man or woman with an explicit accusation of zina, and the slandered person demands punishment, then the judge must flog the slanderer eighty lashes. The commentary expands on this: it defines qadhf as accusing of zina, and provides the primary evidence from Surah An-Nur verse 23, which commands flogging of those who accuse chaste women and fail to bring four witnesses. The hadith of Aisha confirms that the Prophet implemented this hadd. The passage also stresses that the accusation must be explicit (sarih) using a direct word for zina; innuendo or indirect speech does not incur the hadd, as shown by the athar of Qasim ibn Muhammad and the story of the Bedouin who implied his wife gave birth to a black child. The demand of the slandered person is required because it is his personal right; he may forgive it, similar to blood money (diyah). The verse explicitly states 'eighty lashes' as the punishment. This lesson establishes the foundational ruling of qadhf, the conditions of muhsan, explicit accusation, and demand, along with the scriptural proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of zina (fornication/adultery).
محصن (muhsan): A free, adult, Muslim person who has never committed zina and is chaste.
صريح (sarih): Explicit, using a clear word for zina; innuendo does not suffice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the punishment for a free person who explicitly accuses a muhsan of zina and the slandered demands punishment?
A) 40 lashes
B) 80 lashes
C) 100 lashes
D) 80 lashes plus exile

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf (80 lashes) applies only when a free person explicitly accuses a muhsan of zina and the victim demands the penalty, as commanded in Surah An-Nur.

beginner
6 min
Method of Administering Lashes for Qadhf
Procedural rulings for flogging in qadhf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two procedural rulings for administering the hadd of qadhf and identify the proofs from the athar of Ali and Mughira.

Core Idea
When flogging for qadhf, distribute lashes over limbs, avoid face and private parts, and only remove heavy outer garments.

This lesson covers the specific method of implementing the hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation of zina). Two key rulings from the Hanafi school ensure the punishment is both effective and dignified: distribution of lashes over the body to prevent serious injury, and retention of light clothing to preserve modesty. These rulings are based on the practice of the Companions Ali and Mughira.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its rulings
The act is the execution of flogging for qadhf. There are two procedural rulings: how to strike and what clothing to remove.
These are part of the execution method, not the conditions of the punishment.
2
Describe the first ruling
Lashes must be distributed over the criminal's limbs, avoiding the head, face, and private parts.
The athar from Ali provides the evidence.
3
Describe the second ruling
The criminal is not stripped of his clothes except that heavy garments like fur coats and padded clothing must be removed.
The athar from Mughira provides the evidence.
4
Identify the proofs
First ruling: athar from Ali: 'beat and give each limb its right, and avoid his face and genitals.' Second ruling: athar from Mughira: 'do not remove clothes unless it is a thick garment or padded.'
These are ahad (single) narrations, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for establishing wajib procedures.
5
State the Hanafi position
These rulings are wajib (obligatory) to follow when implementing the hadd. Deviation may invalidate the punishment.
They are part of Zahir al-Riwayah and mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۴۹۹] (۲) يُفرق على اعضائه ۲۵۰۰ (۳) ولا يُجرَّد من ثيابه غير انه ينزع عنه الفرو والحشو
مجرم کے اعضاء پر تفریق کر کے مارے۔ یہ اسی کوڑے جسم کی ایک جگہ پر نہ مارے بلکہ ہر عضو پر تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے مارے سوائے سر، چہرہ اور شرمگاہ کے۔ پہلے اثر گزر چکا ہے. عن اتى عليا رجل في حد فقال اضرب واعط كل عضو حقه واجتنب وجهه ومذاكيره(ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب ضرب الحدود هل ضرب النبی من بالسوط اج سابع ص ۳۷۰ نمبر ۱۳۵۱۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مختلف اعضاء پر مارے۔
[ ۲۵۰۰] (۳) مجرم کا کپڑا نہ اتارے علاوہ یہ کہ اس سے پوستین اور روئی بھرا ہوا کپڑا اتارے۔ کوڑا لگاتے وقت مجرم سے کپڑا نہ اتارے قمیص وغیرہ پہنے ہوئے ہی کوڑا لگائے۔ البتہ موٹا کپڑا اور پوستین اتر والے تا کہ کوڑا لگ
اس اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ سألت المغيرة بن شعبة عن القاذف انتزع عنه ثيابه؟ قال لا لا تنزع عنه الا ان يكون فردوا او حشوا (ج) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب وضع الرداء ج سابع ص ۳۷۴ نمبر ۱۳۵۲۶/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۳۸ فی الزامیة والزانی يخلع عنهما یا بھما او یضربان فیهاج خامس ص ۴۹۲ نمبر ۲۸۳۲۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوڑا لگاتے وقت موٹا کپڑا اتر وادے باقی کپڑے نہ اتارے۔
[2499] (2) Distribute upon his limbs. [2500] (3) He is not stripped of his clothes except that the fur and padded garment are removed. (Commentary: flog the criminal with distribution over limbs. Do not beat all on one spot; rather, beat each limb a little, except the head, face, and private parts. An athar: Ali was brought a man in hadd; he said: beat and give each limb its right, and avoid his face and genitals. (Abdurrazzaq). This shows beating on different limbs. [2500] (3) Do not remove the criminal's clothes except that fur and padded garments are removed. When flogging, do not remove his clothes; let him be beaten wearing his shirt etc. However, thick clothes and fur should be removed so the lash can hit. Proof: I asked Mughira ibn Shuba about the slanderer: should we remove his clothes? He said: no, do not remove unless it is a thick garment or padded. (Abdurrazzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba).
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage details two procedural rulings for administering the hadd of qadhf. Ruling (2): The lashes must be distributed over the criminal's body, not concentrated in one area. Specifically, the head, face, and private parts are to be avoided. The proof is an athar from Ali ibn Abi Talib, who instructed to give each limb its right and avoid the face and genitals. Ruling (3): The criminal is not to be stripped of his clothes during flogging, except that heavy garments like fur coats and padded clothing (such as quilted coats) must be removed to ensure the lash reaches the skin. The proof is an athar from Mughira ibn Shuba, who stated that clothes are not removed unless they are thick or padded. This preserves modesty while ensuring the punishment is effective. Both rulings are based on the practice of the Companions and are considered part of the Sunnah in execution of hadd.

Key Terms
تفريق على الاعضاء (tafriq 'ala al-a'da'): Distributing lashes over different limbs, not concentrating on one spot.
فرو (fariw): A fur garment or coat worn for warmth.
حشو (hashw): Padded or quilted garment, stuffed with cotton etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which parts of the body must be avoided when distributing lashes in qadhf?
A) Head, face, and private parts
B) Arms and legs
C) Back and shoulders
D) Only the face

Key Takeaway
When implementing the hadd of qadhf, the Hanafi school mandates distributing lashes over the body and keeping the criminal's light clothing intact, removing only heavy or padded garments, as proven by the practice of the Companions.
